Silver Springs

by annadelamico

Summary

When Agatha and Rio met, sparks flew, but a misunderstanding ripped them apart the morning after.
A year later, they're forced back into each other's lives, leading to unusual consequences.

Based loosely on the film Anyone But You.

The Meet Cute

Rio Vidal rushed desperately into the first coffee shop she could find. It was one of those fancy ones that catered for the executive crowd, filled with people in suits,talking obnoxiously loud on their cell phones.

She ran over to the counter. “Hey, can I use the bathroom?”

The barista looked her up and down. “It’s for paying customers.”

Rio hated her instantly. “Then I’ll buy something.” She grabbed a bagged loaf of bread on the counter. “Here, I’ll take this.”

“There’s a line.” The barista nodded to Rio’s left and to her dismay, there were near a dozen people already waiting.

“Look, I really…”

“Oh, hey hun.” a strong voice cut her off, and Rio looked to see the next person in line walk towards them. The woman was tall with long brown hair, piercing blue eyes, and a jaw that Rio was already obsessed with. The killer suit and confident smile also didn’t help her mind totally short-circuiting.

“I was wondering where you had gotten to,” the woman continued. “I was worried you’d got lost.”

Rio frowned at the woman, who simply stared her down expectantly. If she wasn’t totally distracted by the goddess before her, she probably would have gotten the hint quicker, but she got it in the end.

“Sorry sweetheart. I got held up at work.”

“It’s fine,” the woman assured. “Good choice on the bread. Grilled cheese for dinner?”

Rio smirked. “With that fancy cheese we got from the deli? Sounds amazing.”

“It does.” A gleam of amusement appeared in the woman’s eyes, before she stared down the barista with a cool gaze. “My wife asked for the bathroom key.”

While the woman’s words sent a not unpleasant shockwave through Rio’s body, they startled the barista into action. She reluctantly held out the bathroom key, and Rio snatched it away with a spiteful smile.

“I’ll be right back, babe,” she told the woman, who reached out and took the bread from her, their fingers just avoiding touching.

“Sure hun, do you want your usual?”

“An iced coffee, yes,” Rio confirmed. “But I can get it when I get out…”

“Remember, what’s mine is yours,” the woman answered with a wink, and Rio had to bite her cheek to not giggle like a lovestruck girl. “I’ll wait for you out here.”

“Thanks sweetheart.” Rio shot one last glare at the barista before finally, FINALLY, making her way to the bathroom.

In there, she thought over what had just happened. The most gorgeous woman she had ever seen just pretended to be her wife! Maybe her stepsister was right and she had officially gone crazy, because there’s no way that had just happened to her.

She got out her phone and decided to text said stepsister.

RIO

Okay either I’ve gone totally crazy after all or the world has decided I’m blessed today.

ALICE

???

RIO

Long story but the sexiest woman on the planet just pretended to be my wife so I could get a bathroom key.

ALICE

Wait what?! I need more details!

RIO

No time! I’m in the bathroom and she’s bought me coffee! What should I do?!

ALICE

GET OUT THERE AND TALK TO HER YOU IDIOT!!

Rio raced to freshen up before all but tumbling out of the bathroom door. Luckily, she recovered herself and strode confidently through the coffee shop. The woman was stood to one side, the bread under her arm and the drinks in her hands.

She smiled when she saw Rio walking over. “All good?”

“Yeah.” Rio tossed the bathroom key on the counter, and it hit the surface with a clatter. The barista (and several others) flinched, and she saw her fake wife bite back a laugh.

Rio accepted the iced coffee held out to her. “Thanks, how much do I owe you?”

“Don’t worry about it.” The woman held out the bread with a smile. “I’m Agatha.”

“Rio.”

“Rio.” The name rolled off Agatha’s tongue in a way Rio had never heard before. “Nice to meet you.”

Trying hard not to blush, she took a sip of her coffee. “Well, thank you for the help, and the coffee, and the bread.”

“In all honesty, I needed entertaining, and there is nothing better than making someone squirm.” Agatha looked over at the barista and pursed her lips. “Especially someone who has messed up my coffee order one to many times.”

Rio smirked. “We really did make her squirm, didn’t we?”

Agatha’s lips curled into a devious grin. “We make quite the pair of antagonists.”

Rio tilted her head. “You busy right now?”

Agatha reached for her phone. “Well I can…not be busy, why do you ask?”

“How do you feel about finishing our coffees together. Somewhere other than here.”

She watched Agatha tap away at her phone and wondered if she had been too bold with her proposition. It wouldn’t be the first time; Alice always said she came on too strong.

When she stopped typing, Agatha pocketed her phone again and nodded towards the door. “Ladies first.”

Agatha Harkness wasn’t sure why she’d done it.

Since her assistant Ralph had quit, she found herself having to get her own drinks from the coffee shop around the corner of the office. Usually, she didn’t like being around so many people, all irritating in their own way. That visit, she been too preoccupied reading an email from one of her clients asking for his novel’s release date to be brought forward. She was just drafting a response email when she heard a commotion ahead of her. Over the bathroom key of all things.

Great , she thought, just what I need right now.

She only meant to steal a glance at the scene out of pure nosiness. Yet the moment she saw the woman arguing with the barista, she couldn’t look away. The face, the hair, the big brown eyes…Agatha couldn’t take her eyes off her.

She listened to the back and forth between the mystery woman and the bitchy barista, and the next thing she knew, they were married and having grilled cheese for dinner. Crazy? Even crazier was buying said woman bread and iced coffee, waiting for her to use the bathroom, and had cancelled the rest of her schedule for the day to wander through a nearby park with said woman.

Rio.

“So, what do you do for work?” Rio asked. “I’m guessing you’re a boss or something.”

“Or something,” Agatha confirmed. “I work for major publishing house. I’m in charge of making sure everyone is doing their job properly.”

“So, you’re the boss?”

“No, but he’s scared of me so I might as well be.”

Rio laughed. “Well, I’m certain you look better in a power suit.”

Agatha chuckled while subtly looking over Rio’s attire. She had a blazer on, and a white button up blouse and black trousers that, well, hugged. Her hair was up, and her make-up was neat. Anyone would think she fit into the corporate world. Yet the shoes gave her away.

Converse sneakers were not business attire.

“What do you do?”

“I’ve just started my PhD, so that takes up most of my time. I help out my sister too. It’s complicated but her mom’s estate is hard to manage alone.”

Agatha was certainly intrigued. “What are you studying?”

Rio laughed awkwardly and bowed her head. “Erm…botany.”

Agatha tried to cool her reaction, but her eyebrows had a mind of their own. “So…flowers?”

“No, I mean I guess yes. My speciality is poisonous plants. I was actually meeting with a company to see if they’d finance a study I’m working on, but I guess we’ll see.”

Okay, she was back on board. “That actually sounds interesting. So you’ve, like, handled all these plants?”

“With the correct safety procedures, yes. I also dabble in the study of arachnids, but that’s just a hobby. I have a tarantula.”

“A tarantula? Is that your idea of cute and cuddly.”

“Yes,” Rio answered without hesitation. “Have you ever held a tarantula? They’re actually very gentle.”

“I’ll take your word for it.”

Rio dropped her empty cup in a trash can as they walked by. “Okay then, what is your idea of cute and cuddly?”

“Something that doesn’t have six legs,” Agatha sassed, but when Rio stared her down, she sighed. “Fine, I like rabbits.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “Rabbits?”

Agatha sighed. She couldn’t believe she was admitting this to a complete stranger. “Yes, I actually just got a baby bunny…”

Rio stopped in her tracks. “Woah, woah, woah. You have a baby rabbit?”

“Yes, but…”

“Can I see it?”

“A photo or in person?” Agatha cursed herself. Why the hell did she ask that?

Rio grinned. “In person is an option?”

“Sure,” Agatha answered casually. “Unless you have other plans?”

“Nope, you?”

Agatha got out her phone again and texted her sister.

AGATHA

Can’t make it tonight. Something came up.

In true Rebecca style, she replied straight away.

REBECCA

Work??

Agatha glanced up at Rio, who was watching her closely, before responding.

AGATHA

No, something else.

Agatha indeed had a bunny, and Rio was in love. He had mostly white fur, with little beige patches and random black speckles, and the most precious little face. While she was not one to subscribe to conventional ‘cuteness’, he was certainly an exception.

“What’s his name?” Rio asked from her stop on the floor, sat crossed legged with the rabbit cradled in her arms.

“Senõr Scratchy,” Agatha answered from where she stood at the kitchen counter, making them some tea. “My nephew named him. He was originally his, but it turns out his dad is allergic to rabbits.”

“How old is your nephew?”

“He’s 14. He’s…well, he’s going through a lot. My sister and brother-in-law got him the rabbit to help, but then when his dad came out in hives…”

“So you took the rabbit instead?”

“I did.”

“But you’re secretly happy about it?”

Though Agatha had her back to her, Rio could tell she was smiling. “It didn’t take much persuading.”

Other than the rabbit, Agatha’s living area consisted of a set of leather couches, an antique looking coffee table, rows and rows of bookshelves taking up the walls without kitchen fixtures and large windows that looked out over the city. It was an expensive place, Rio knew from the location, but it felt as homely as Alice’s box apartment in a pre-war building (where she was currently staying on the couch).

When Agatha was done with the drinks, she carried it over and placed one on the coffee table, before settling at the far end of the sofa with her own. Rio instantly noticed the designs didn’t match: the white one Agatha was holding had ‘COOL AUNT CLUB’ printed on it in big purple writing, while hers was black with ‘WITCHES BREW’ written in white lettering.

“You need to get a crazy rabbit lady mug,” Rio commented. “Alice got me a crazy plant lady one.”

Agatha paused for a moment. “Alice?”

“My step-sister,” Rio clarified, before smirking. “Was that a hint of jealousy I heard there?”

“No.” Agatha frowned at her coffee like a sulking child. Rio’s smirk grew. She was definitely jealous.

“No, I’m very much single.”

Agatha looked up at her with a disbelieving look. “So there’s no one...?”

Rio shrugged. “Alice likes to set me up on blind dates, but I’m not a people person. I’m guessing you have plenty of admirers, though?”

Agatha scoffed. “Jen says I scare everyone I meet.”

Rio set Senõr Scatchy down and  climbed onto the couch. She reached for her coffee and took a sip. “Jen, huh?”

When she saw the other woman smirk, she knew she’d failed at playing cool.

“Now who’s jealous?"

“What if I was?” Rio quickly turned the tables.

“Then I’d say she’s my friend, and I’d be disappointed if you weren’t jealous.”

Rio smiled at her answer. “Glad to know we’re on the right page.”

They continued chatting about this and that: Rio gave Agatha a crash course in poisonous plants to watch out for, and Agatha told Rio about her love for literature, which she got from her grandmother.

“I lived with her for a while,” Agatha admitted. “My mother didn’t want me in her house but wouldn’t let me go to my dad’s more than the court allowed it, so I ended up there.”

“Did you live there long?”

“The whole last year of middle school until the end of spring break freshman year. My dad got a good lawyer, and my grandmother was getting too old to give me the support I needed. It meant I got to live with my half-sister too, which gave us time to get under each other’s feet enough to form a sisterly bond.”

“Yeah, Alice and I had plenty of time for that too. What happened to your grandmother?”

“She died not long after I finished college.” Agatha reached into shirt, revealing a chain with an old locket with a cameo image of three figures against a deep purple. “This was hers. A family heirloom. I know it’s not the fanciest of jewellery, but it was hers.”

“I like it,” Rio insisted. “It’s classic, and unique.”

Agatha smiled and tucked it back in her shirt. She looked out of the window and frowned. “Huh.”

“What?” Rio followed her gaze and saw the sun had started to dip behind the buildings. “Wow, I didn’t realise it was this late.”

“Do you have to be anywhere?” Agatha asked. “I mean, it’s fine if you do, but if not do you want to go get dinner? Or I can get us some take out?”

“Well, I have that bread.” Rio nodded to the loaf that had been abandoned on the breakfast bar. “If you have cheese, we can have that grilled cheese dinner we talked about earlier.”

“Anything for my darling wife,” Agatha teased, before getting up to gather what they needed.

Rio used the opportunity to text Alice.

RIO

Having dinner with my coffee wife. Don’t wait up.

ALICE

Weirdo but also tell me everything tomorrow.

Rio sent her a wink face before following Agatha. Something she hoped would be a new habit.

They ate the grilled cheeses over the sink as they turned out to be messier than they anticipated, and between their laugher, Agatha found out Rio had never seen The Conjuring , so a movie night quickly followed.

When Rio cackled at yet another jump scare, Agatha couldn’t help but laugh with her.

“How are you both wonderful and the strangest person I’ve ever met?”

“Strange is my superpower,” Rio answered. “And I saw you laughing too.”

Agatha sighed. “Fine, I’m strange too I guess.”

Rio shifted to rest her head on Agatha’s shoulder. “That’s why we get on so well.”

“Yeah,” Agatha agreed. “Maybe.”

By the time the movie ended, Rio was pretty much in her lap, and when the credits rolled, she shifted until she was pretty much straddling Agatha’s thigh.

Rio hummed. “It’s late.”

“It is,” Agatha agreed. “What shall we do about that?”

“I could stay?” Rio suggested.

“You could,” Agatha agreed.

“But no sex.”

Agatha blinked. “Okay…”

“I don’t want a one-night stand,” Rio clarified, and Agatha smiled in relief.

“Okay, yes, of course.”

“But we could kiss, and cuddle, and maybe let our hands wander.”

Agatha smirked. “That sounds like a reasonable plan to me. I’ll get you something to sleep in…”

She went to get up, but Rio pushed her back down. The next thing, Rio was straddling her properly, their faces so close, Agatha could feel her breath against her lips.

She waited for the kiss, waited for the floodgates to open, but it never came. Rio slid off her lap and walked towards the bedroom. “Come on then.”

Agatha didn’t need telling twice.

She found Rio a baggy shirt and got her a toothbrush and towels to freshen up in the en-suite. Agatha changed into her own shorts and an old Carhartt shirt. Sitting on the end of the bed, she waited for Rio to emerge.

When the bathroom door opened, Rio stepped out in a Fleetwood Mac t shirt that sat at the top of her thighs. She placed her folded clothes on the chair in the corner of the room, and Agatha hadn’t failed to notice her bra was on said pile.

“Okay I love this shirt,” Rio announced. “I may have to steal it.”

“Maybe, but not tonight,” Agatha teased as she stood. She felt Rio’s eyes trail over her.

“I might steal that shirt at some point too.”

Agatha shook her head and past her to head into the bathroom. “Make yourself at home.”

When the bathroom door was shut, she released a heavy breath. Rio was going to kill her. She had never wanted someone so much, but she also just wanted to hold her. Was this how it felt when you made a true connection? She didn’t know, but it was enough to make her handshake as she rushed to brush her freshen up and brush her teeth. Still, it took to long, and eventually her impatience got the better of her.

She stepped out of the bathroom and spotted Rio laid out on the bed waiting for her. Without a second thought, she walked over and crawled on top of her, their chests, their legs, their everything touching, apart from their lips.

“You’re beautiful,” she praised, closing her eyes as Rio’s hands cupped her cheeks.

“You’re magnificent.”

Agatha allowed Rio to pull her down, to crush their lips together, sealing a connection like neither of them had known before.

The Morning After

As always, Agatha woke with the first sign of sunrise, her eyes adjusting to the room’s darkness. She checked the clock and saw it was half 5. Usually, she would just get up and start some work from home, but currently she had a gorgeous woman burrowed into her side.

Agatha watched her face as light began to faintly filter into the room. Rio looked so peaceful when she slept, her dark hair spread across the pillow behind her. A strand of it had fallen over her face, and Agatha carefully hooked it with her finger and tucked it behind her ear. Rio stirred, only to shuffle closer to her.

Agatha’s heart fluttered, something she hadn’t experienced…well ever. She didn’t do stuff like this: just meeting someone and actually liking them. She never connected with someone like she had last night. They barely did more than kiss, but somehow it had been so intimate. So deep and true.

Her mind began to run away with itself, but she quickly pulled herself back. She wanted to enjoy the moment. With Rio, in their first morning after.

She was about to drift back into a light slumber when her phone vibrated on the bedside table.  With a sigh, she reached over to check.

Two messages from Rebecca.

Agatha carefully pulled away from Rio to sit up and opened the texts.

REBECCA

Have you talked to William?

REBECCA

He’s just left the house without his phone. Jeff has gone to look for him.

Agatha got out of bed and rushed into the bathroom, texting as she went.

AGATHA

I’m on my way.

Freshening up, she threw on whatever clothes she could find and was about to rush out of the apartment when she caught sight of Rio’s sleeping form once more. Agatha moved and sat on the edge of the bed. She looked too peaceful to wake, and it wasn’t even six in the morning.

Despite herself, she leaned down and kissed her forehead, before moving through to the living area. She grabbed some sticky notes from her desk and scrubbed down a message.

Morning beautiful,

Sorry family emergency!

The door pulls shut so leave whenever you want. Make sure to make some breakfast and coffee!

Call me later?

Agatha scribbled down her number and pulled the note from the pad. Looking around the room, she tried to think of a place where Rio would definitely see it. A shuffling sound directed her attention to the cage, where Senõr Scratchy was currently moving around.

“Hey,” she greeted him with a cup full of food, before securing the sticky note to the bars of the cage. “Make sure she sees this, okay?”

Senõr Scratchy was too busy tucking into his breakfast to care.

Agatha stole one last glance towards the bedroom, before grabbing her things and rushing out the door.

Rio woke up to the sound of her weekday phone alarm. Half 7 on the dot. She grumbled and buried her face in the pillow. A pillow that was softer than the one she was used to, and smelt like perfume and-

Agatha.

She smiled and bit her lip, her hand reaching out to the other side of the bed. Only to be met with a bare and cold mattress.

Rio pulled herself up, blinking at the light. Looking around the room, Agatha was nowhere to be seen. With a frown, she got out of bed and wandered through to the living area.

The only person there was Senõr Scratchy, who was too busy nibbling on something to acknowledge her presence.

“Agatha?” She called out, but no reply.

She looked around for a note, even checking the floor in case it fell under something, but there was nothing. Agatha had just left her in her apartment without a word.

Rio went back through to the bedroom and changed back into her now creased clothes, throwing the Fleetwood Mac shirt to the top of the bed with a frustrated growl.

How could she have been so stupid?

Checking she hadn’t left anything, she headed out, making a d-tour to see Senõr Scratchy as she went. He had now finished whatever he’d been doing and now looked up at her with an emotionless expression.

“Tell your mom she can rot in hell,” Rio told him, before heading out of the apartment, slamming the door behind her.

Agatha eventually found her nephew walking down a street a mile or so away from his house. She slowed the car and rolled the passenger window down.

“Hey!”

He looked at her, surprised at first before his expression turned to annoyance. “Mom called you.”

“Hell yeah she did. Now get in the car!”

William sighed. “You don’t understand…”

Agatha heavy braked. “William Kaplan, if you don’t get in this car right now…”

He scampered over and climbed in the passenger seat without argument. She unlocked her phone and passed it to him. “Tell your mom I found you and I’m taking you for a drive.”

“But…”

“Do it.”

He sighed and typed out the text as she set off down the street. When he set the phone down, Agatha waited until they were almost out of the neighbourhood they’d found themselves in before speaking, calmer this time.

“Okay kid, talk to me.”

William was silent for a moment, but eventually gave in. “They don’t get me.”

“So you ran out the house at 5 in the morning?”

“I just needed to get away,” he admitted. “I haven’t slept.”

“Why not?”

“Because I have too much on my mind.”

Agatha sighed and pulled up the car. She turned off the engine and adjusted in her seat to face him.

“What’s wrong?”

William looked out the window. “I got asked to go on a date.”

“And you don’t want to go?”

“No I do,” William insisted. “I really…they’ve been my crush for ages.”

“Then that’s good, isn’t it?” Agatha didn’t understand the new parameters of dating (or the old ones really), but she couldn’t see what was wrong with the situation.

“It is but…it’s complicated with mom and dad. You know how they are.”

Agatha nodded. She knew her sister and brother-in-law had a tendency to be overprotective, but they had their reasons.

“You think they won’t like the idea of you dating?”

William sucked in a deep breath. “I think they won’t like the idea of me dating a boy.”

Agatha leaned back in her seat and folded her arms. William stole a glance her way. “You don’t have anything to say?”

“Like what?”

“Like, I don’t know, you’re surprised…”

“Well yes it’s shocked me to my core.”

He narrowed his eyes. “You knew already, didn’t you?”

“Of course I knew.”

“How?”

Agatha rolled her eyes. She wasn’t even dignifying that with an answer. “You do know that I’m a lesbian, right? If your parents had a problem with gay people, you wouldn’t even know I existed.”

“You’re not their son, and you’re no-“

“Don’t you dare bring that into this,” Agatha warned him. “Look, it’s scary for anyone, but you’re lucky. You have good parents, and even if they didn’t take it well, you have me. I can get an apartment with a spare room, but you’d have to share with Senõr Scratchy.”

That succeeded in making him laugh. “I wouldn’t want to interrupt your bachelor lifestyle.”

Oh the irony, Agatha thought.

“So you think I should just tell them?”

“Yes, I do. We could tell them together? Or we could work out what you could tell them alone? But you’ll need to tell them at some point, and the sooner you do, the sooner you’ll have your mom taking you shopping for a date outfit.”

“I’d rather you took me,” he admitted. “You’re cooler.”

“Of course I am, but she’s your mom. Let her have this.”

He nodded in understanding. “Also, I don’t want to be called William anymore. I want to be called Billy.”

Agatha let out a snort of laughter. “Good luck convincing your mom of that one.”

William, Billy, laughed along with her. “Hey, why didn’t you come for dinner last night?”

“Is that part of the reason you were upset?”

“No…well, I was going to talk to you about this last night, then I couldn’t get it out of my head.”

“Sorry kid.”

“It’s okay, but Mom said it wasn’t for work, so what happened?”

Agatha thought for a moment, before choosing the truth. “I met someone yesterday.”

Billy bolted up in his seat. “You did? What’s her name? What she like?”

“Her name is Rio and she’s the most bizarre person I’ve ever met.”

“So she’s cool?”

“I think so.”

“When are you seeing her again?”

“I don’t know,” Agatha answered regretfully. “I had to leave her in bed to come look for you…”

Billy covered his ears. “Please tell me you weren’t having sex.”

“What?! No! I mean, she stayed over but we neve-why am I explaining myself? Let’s go talk to your parents so I can get back to the city.”

“And your girl,” Billy added with a smirk, earning him a playful shove.

As expected, Rebecca and Jeff took it well. Agatha stood by and watched the little family cry and embrace, before both parents looked to her for guidance as the old wise lesbian that she was. Eventually, she managed to slip into the kitchen to check her phone.

Plenty of work emails, but nothing else. Nothing from Rio. It was almost 10. Surely she wasn’t still asleep?

“William said you were on a date last night.”

Agatha sighed. “Your son is a gossip.”

Rebecca ignored her comment as she moved to stand beside her. “He said you left her when I text you. I’m sorry.”

“It’s fine.”

“No, it’s not. He’s our son, not yours. And now I’ve ruined your love life…”

“He comes first,” Agatha insisted. “No matter what I’m doing, where I am, who I’m with. If you need me, you call.”

Rebecca patted her on the shoulder. They weren’t huggers, but that was enough for them.

“You should go to her.”

Agatha shrugged. “I left my number, but she hasn’t text me.”

“Then go see if she’s waiting at your apartment. You’ve done enough for us today, so go do something for you.”

Agatha kissed her sister’s cheek before rushing out the house.

By the time she got to her apartment building, she still had no texts. Agatha had hoped there would be something. An emoji, a cute little hi. Something she could reply to. Still, she headed up to her apartment with a mix of nervousness and anticipation. In her head, she formed a plan of Rio was still there. Explain what happened, ask if she has any plans that day, then kiss her like their lives depended on it.

As she walked to her front door, her heart beat heavy in her chest. Scrambling for her keys, she let herself into the apartment.

“Rio?” She called out as she shut the door, receiving no reply.

The note was gone from Senõr Scratchy’s cage, and there was no other sign of movement in the room. When she made her way to the bedroom, the only evidence Rio even existed were the screwed-up sheets and the Fleetwood Mac shirt discarded carelessly at the head of the bed.

Agatha picked up the shirt and brought it to her nose. It smelled like Rio. A scent that has been saved in her sensory memory.

Hugging the shirt to her chest, she sat on the end of the bed and called texted Rebecca

AGATHA

She’s gone

REBECCA

She’ll call. Don’t worry!

Agatha waited, and waited, and waited.

It took her two days not to jump for her phone when she got a message, another week after that before she stopped obsessively checking if she had any new messages, and another month after that to stop hoping one would come. In the end, only one thing was certain…

Agatha Harkness had been ghosted, and she didn’t take kindly to that.

The Meet Again

Chapter Notes

Also I'd like to add that I do kind of practise Tarot but I'm definitely no expert!

One year later…

“SHARON!”

The small lady toddled into Agatha’s office, all smiles like always. “How can I help?”

“Can you call the London office and ask them to send me their latest numbers?”

“Of course, sweetie. Do you need anything? Tea? Coffee? Chocolate?”

“No, I’m fine.” Agatha waved her off irritably, but as always Sharon didn’t seem to care.

Sharon was currently her longest running assistant. She’d had enough of the fresh graduate crowd, so took a shot with the recent widow who ‘wanted to look after someone’. Her longest assistant before had lasted a month. So far, Sharon had lasted seven.

“Oh and Jen called. She said you need to answer her texts.”

“What? Jen hasn’t text me.” Agatha reached for her phone and saw she had five messages and two missed calls.

JEN

Are you free tonight.

JEN

????

JEN

HELLO???

Missed call from: Jen

JEN

Bitch answer your phone!!!

Missed call from: Jen

JEN

I’m calling your assistant

Agatha sighed. “I’ll call her now.”

She waiting until Sharon was out of the room before calling her back.

Jen answered on the third ring. “Do you every answer your phone?”

“If you gave me chance,” Agatha huffed. “What’s happening tonight?”

“I need you to meet me at Josie’s Bar at eight.”

“Why?”

“You know I’m seeing that girl…”

Agatha rolled her eyes. She should have known. Jen had met a girl a month or so ago and hadn’t shut up about her since. While she was pleased her friend was happy, she was sick of hearing about the woman, and she hadn’t even met her yet.

“Well, she wants me to meet her sister, and she asked if I had a friend, so she wasn’t a third wheel.”

“This better not be a date,” Agatha warned, to which Jen laughed.

“You think I’d let you date my girlfriend’s sister? I actually want this relationship to work.”

Agatha smirked. “So it’s official now, huh?”

“Shut up,” Jen huffed. “See you at eight?”

Agatha sighed. “Fine, I’ll be there.”

“Great, and wear something sexy.”

“Why would I…”

Jen hung up the phone, and Agatha cursed under her breath. She knew this was a set up. Her (only) friend and her sister had been playing matchmaker since the ghosting incident. But Agatha Harkness didn’t believe in love anymore, at least not romantic love.

She looked at the framed picture of her and Billy on her desk and smiled softly. He was doing better. He’d met a nice boy and seemed to be a lot more settled. There were still down moments, times when he regressed, but it was mostly fine. In a way she was glad Rio left her, as it meant she could devote herself to her work and her family.

Still, she never wanted to see her face again.

Rio woke to the sound of the blender, and instantly cursed every decision she had made in her life. The blender meant one thing: smoothie day.

She got up and pushed her hair back out of her face. Throwing on a hoodie, she dragged herself out of bed and stumbled towards the noise.

“Lilia,” she groaned as she staggered towards the kitchen, a hand over her face to conceal her eyes from the sunlight. “Why do you always blend so early.”

“It’s almost 9,” her roommate shouted over the blender. “And you need nutrients.”

“I need sleep! I was working late last night.”

Lilia turned off the blender and checked the contents. “What you need is a proper schedule. You’re acting like a college student.”

“I am a college student.”

“You’re 18 months away from a doctorate,” Lilia reminded her as she poured the smoothie into two glasses. “You need to toughen up and think about your life.”

“Okay mom,” Rio sassed, but accepted the smoothie. They weren’t that bad really, but she preferred the over-sugary cereal Lilia disapproved of.

Lilia was older, wiser. She didn’t have any kids, too busy with her boutique and her famous tarot readings. Rio had expected their relationship to be unique when she answered Lilia’s ad for a roommate. What she didn’t expect was to become a pseudo daughter.

Just as they were about to sit at the table, Rio heard her phone ringing in her bedroom,

“Shit.” She put down her smoothie and ran through, her heart dropping when she saw it was Alice.

Alice never called.

She scrambled to answer. “What is it? What’s wrong?”

“Nothing,” her stepsister assured. “Just checking we’re still on for tonight.”

“Tonight?”

“Please say you didn’t forget…”

“I didn’t,” Rio insisted. “Just remind me when and where we’re meeting again?”

Alice sighed. “Josie’s Bar at eight. You’re meeting Jen, remember?”

“Oh yes. Jen.” How could Rio forget? Honestly, she thought she got down bad, but Alice was making her look hard to get. Jen this, Jen that. Not a conversation went by without Jen, Jen, Jen.

“Yeah well she’s just called and said she’s bringing a friend.”

Rio put a hand on her hip. “Why?”

“So you’re not a third wheel.”

“So it’s not a double date?”

“Totally not,” Alice answered. “But Jen did say she’s single.”

It was Rio’s turn to sigh. “You know I’m over the whole dating scene.”

“Just because you had a bad experience…”

“It wasn’t ‘Just’ anything and you know that.”

Alice had been the first person to see her that morning after. She held her as she cried, calmed her as she raged. It wasn’t a bad date, or even a bad break up; it was Rio losing faith in love. All because she’d been stupid enough to think a random woman in a coffee shop was her soulmate.

“I know,” Alice replied. “I just want you to be happy.”

“I am happy,” Rio insisted. “I have you, and Lilia, and Webbers.”

“You have your sister, your roommate who is twice your age, and a spider.”

“Tarantula.”

“Whatever. Just come tonight and meet Jen, and see what her friend is like. Okay?”

Rio rubbed a hand over her face. “What’s her friend’s name?”

“Agnes I think?”

“Fine, okay, I’ll see you then.”

“Wear something nice.”

“Fuck you. My fashion sense is flawless.”

Alice laughed and hung up the phone.

Rio tossed her phone back on her bed and, after a moment’s thought, headed back to the living area.

“Lilia?”

“Yes?” Lilia was sat at the table with her smoothie in one hand and her phone in the other.

“Can you do me a reading?”

Lilia looked at her in surprise. “You hate my readings.”

“No, I don’t. I just sometimes disagree with them.”

“Fine, pass me the cards on the table.”

Rio retrieved the aged box of cards and handed them to Lilia as she moved to sit opposite her.

Lilia unboxed the cards. “What do you want?”

“Just your usual past, present, future.”

Lilia knocked on the cards and shuffled them, before laying three on the table. She turned the past card, revealing the Three of Swords. Rio glared at it. “I always get that one.”

“The cards don’t lie,” Lilia reminded her, but didn’t repeat the meaning of the card. Rio already knew the score: grief, heartbreak, pain. She guessed it had some truth to it.

Lilia turned the present card- the Six of Cups.

“That’s a new one,” Rio commented. “What does it mean?”

“It means something from the past will be coming to the present.”

“Like what?”

“I’m not that kind of psychic.” Lilia turned over the future card, only to tense. “Oh.”

“‘Oh’ what?”

Lilia blinked at the card. “The Tower Reversed.”

“Is that bad?”

“There are no bad cards,” Lilia insisted. “It could mean a number of things.”

“Such as?” Rio pressed.

“Mostly, it warns that you’re going to go through a great change.”

“What kind of change?”

“I can’t answer that, doll.”

Rio grumbled and got to her feet. She hated those stupid cards.

“It doesn’t have to be a big change,” Lilia reassured. “Just a big one.”

In Rio’s experience, all big changes were bad.

“I’m meeting Alice tonight,” she announced. “Don’t wait up.”

“I’ll be up anyway,” Lilia replied, and Rio knew that would be true. Lilia didn’t sleep much.

“You never know,” Rio said with a smirk. “I might meet my Six of Cups.”

“Maybe,” Lilia agreed with a sad smile. “Just…be careful.”

Rio nodded, though she wasn’t worried. It was only a stupid deck of cards.

Agatha left work around 6 and headed home. She ate some leftover pizza and fed Senõr Scratchy, yet instead of her usual nightly routine of cuddling up with a good book, she ransacked her wardrobe and headed out in a slick black pantsuit over a black corset top.

Jen said look sexy, so she’d make her eat her words. If she was feeling really spiteful, she might have made a point of seduced her future sister-in-law, but she decided to settle on getting everyone in the room to fixate on her chest.

She was just down the street from the bar when Jen called.

“Where are you?”

“It’s not even 8 yet,” Agatha argued.

“But we’re all here already.”

“And that’s my problem because?”

She heard Jen curse. “Where are you, Agatha?”

“Literally down the street.”

“I’m stood outside.”

It wasn’t long before Agatha spotted her. Jen was wearing a long pink sundress which was too chilly for a September night, but she looked amazing, nonetheless.

When Jen saw her, she stomped over. “I’m sorry for snapping but I’m nervous.”

“Why?”

“Because her sister looks super scary.”

“Have you spoken to her?”

“No, I saw them in there and ran back out.”

Agatha shook her head in disgrace. “I thought I taught you better than this. Be the scariest person in the room.”

“I don’t want to scare her. I want to impress her!”

“This is pathetic,” Agatha said with grimace. “Take us inside.”

She followed Jen back into the bar, trailing her path through the crowd. Agatha spotted a short woman with bright red streaks in her hair rushing towards them before embracing Jen in a tight hug.

“You’re here!” The woman’s voice was full of glee, and Jen’s smile was unlike any Agatha had seen before. They were already sickening.

“Where’s your sister?” Jen asked once they pulled apart.

“She’s just getting drinks,” the woman, Alice, looked past Jen to Agatha and smiled. “Is this your friend?”

“Yeah.” Jen moved to reveal Agatha fully. “Alice, this is…”

“Agatha?”

Her heart dropped in her chest. She knew that voice. She could never forget that voice.

A familiar face appeared beside Alice, who looked equally surprised.

Agatha pursed her lips. “Rio.”

“Fuck,” Jen cursed. “Agatha, I didn’t…”

Rio tilted her head. Annoyingly, she was still beautiful, but her eyes had changed. They were no longer filled with adoration and desire. No, they were darker. Hateful.

“It’s been a long time,” Rio commented. “Picked up any girls in coffee shops recently?”

Agatha’s jaw tightened. “Why, you jealous?”

Rio laughed bitterly. “No, why? Do you want me to be?”

“I want nothing to do with you,” Agatha bit back.

“Okay, okay.” Alice stepped between them. “Let’s calm down and…”

“Because I see you for who you really are,” Rio accused, ignoring her sister’s attempt at peace. “A coward.”

Agatha growled in anger, wanting to wipe the smug look off Rio’s face, but instead stormed off towards the door.

“That’s it, run away,” she heard Rio call after her. “It’s what you’re good at.”

As soon as Agatha got outside, she stopped and sucked in a deep breath. This couldn’t be happening.

“Agatha,” Jen stood beside her. “I’m so sorry. I didn’t know, I swear.”

“I don’t want to see her,” Agatha insisted. “I won’t go back in there and I won’t see her again.”

“But…”

“No Jen,” she snapped. “No.”

She didn’t wait for Jen’s answer and stormed back down the street. She needed to get as far away from Rio as she could get. She never wanted to be anywhere near her again.

Rio knocked back another shot before slamming her hand on the bar. “Another.”

“Rio, stop,” Alice ordered, but Rio accepted the shot and gulped it down.

“I’m having fun.”

“Well, no one else is.”

Rio went to wave at the bartender again, but Alice pulled her arm down. “Hey!”

“Look, I’m sorry. I must have misheard her name.”

Rio smirked at her sister. “No, I’m glad. I’ve been wanting to piss her off for a year.”

“I know you’re upset,” Alice insisted, “I saw the way you looked at her.”

“With a thirst for revenge?”

“No,” Alice countered. “With grief and pain.”

Rio blinked at her, the three of swords flashing in her mind. “What did you just say?”

Alice didn’t respond, instead her attention was caught by something in the crowd. Rio followed her gaze and saw Jen walking towards them.

“Hey, where’s Agatha?”

“She’s gone, and I’m going to head off too.”

“What?” Alice took hold of Jen’s hands. “You don’t have to, us three…”

Jen met Rio’s gaze and shot her an icy glare, before looking back to Alice with neutral expression. “I’ll call you tomorrow.”

Jen kissed Alice’s cheek, before walking away. Rio watched as her sister’s shoulders slumped and felt a little bad about it. A little. She was totally in the right; she just wished Alice wasn’t caught in the middle.

“Are we going home?” She asked Alice, who simply nodded.

They shared a cab home: Alice only lived a block from her apartment, so Rio walked the rest of the way home. Her mind was fixed on one thing.

Agatha.

Agatha.

Agatha.

The look on her face when their eyes met. The tiny spark of pain when Rio called her out. The way she ran away. It all satisfied the itch for revenge she had for so long, but it still wasn’t enough to make her feel any better.

It didn’t help that she still looked like a sexy sapphic goddess.

When she walked into the apartment, Lilia was sat on the couch watching the shopping channel, but quickly turned it off. Worst thing about living with a psychic? They knew when something was up.

“What happened?”

“Your stupid cards were right.” Rio slumped onto the couch beside her.

“You met your six of cups I take it?”

“Yeah.” Rio got up and walked to the kitchen, grabbing beer for herself and a coke can for Lilia.

“Did I ever tell you about Agatha?”

Lilia accepted the can. “I don’t think so?”

Rio settled back on the couch, her legs crossed. “She’s my six of cups, and my three of swords.”

Lilia nodded in understanding. “Tell me everything.”


Taking a sip of her own beer, Agatha looked out over the city lights. She wasn’t paying much attention to it; just distracting her eyes while her mind went over the evening’s events.

Rio.

Why did it have to be Rio?

Jen could have met anyone, anyone, and it was Rio’s stepsister. Oh, how the universe liked to torment her.

Agatha downed the rest of her whisky and headed over to Senõr Scratchy’s cage. Picking him up, she hugged him to her chest. He was a big boy now, which made him twice as cuddly. She rubbed her chin against the top of his head.

“I saw Rio again,” she told him. “She might have gotten the upper hand this time but trust me. She’ll learn I’m not someone to be messed with.”

The Aftermath

Chapter Notes

thanks for all the comments! i'm loving writing this so much! i'm hoping to have chapter 5 up tomorrow!

Rio had spent the next day studying a new specimen of dried azalea that had been found in a library book in Colorado. The librarian that discovered it had ended up in an induced coma, while others who handled it ended up in hospital. Everyone survived, so not too exciting, but the neurotoxins in the samples were still fascinating.

After decontamination, Rio returned home from the college to find Alice and Lilia sat at the dining table.

“What is this? An intervention?” she joked, but neither of them laughed. “Okay, what’s going on?”

“I need to talk to you,” Alice announced. “It’s important.”

“Okay…” Rio sat at the head of the table. “What’s up?”

“I talked with Jen, and she told me Agatha’s version of that morning.”

“She did?” Rio folded her arms. “What did she say?”

“That she left a note with her number on it, and you never called.”

“She didn’t leave anything,” Rio insisted. “Besides me, anyway.”

“Well, that’s what Jen said.”

“Yes, because your girlfriend is the fountain of all truths.”

“Rio,” Lilia warned.

“What? I was the one there. I know what happened.”

“Just let Alice finish.”

Rio stuck her middle finger up at her, which Lilia simply tutted at.

“Jen told me why Agatha left,” Alice continued. “And we think maybe she thought she’d written the note but forgot in the moment.”

“How could she forget?” Rio questioned.

“Her nephew had run away,” Alice explained. “She had to go.”

Rio, for the slightest of seconds, felt guilty…only to quickly think better of it.

“She could have woken me up if it was an emergency.”

Lilia scoffed. “Would be easier to wake the dead.”

Alice cleared her throat. “Either way, Jen and I talked, and we think this is a big misunderstanding.”

Rio was about to ask why Alice and her stupid girlfriend felt the need to pass judgement on the situation, but a more important question came to mind. “What does Agatha think?”

“Jen’s going to talk to her today,” Alice answered. “We want us all to be able to move on from this. You’re my sister, and Agatha is Jen’s best friend. We can’t go on like this, especially over a…”

“If you say misunderstanding one more time, I’m going to stab you.”

Used to her sister’s antics, Alice appeared more exasperated than threatened. “Well?”

Rio leaned back in her chair. “If Agatha admits she forgot the note, I’ll think about it.”

Lilia looked to Alice. “Think that’s as good as you’ll get.”

Alice nodded in defeat. “I’ll take it. So if we organise a meet between you two…”

Rio made a show of sighing. “I guess I’ll be the bigger person and talk with her.”

Alice grinned and jumped to her feet. “This is great! Let me call, Jen.”

Rio watched Alice run into her room with a skip in her step. She smiled to herself, only for it to drop when she caught Lilia’s eye. “What?”

“What are you plotting?”

“I’m not plotting,” Rio insisted with mock insult. “I’m accepting peace negotiations.”

“Alice likes that girl,” Lilia warned. “Don’t mess this up for her, or for yourself.”

“For me?” Rio questioned, only to be interrupted by a loud scream.

“RIO!” YOUR SPIDER IS ON THE LOOSE AGAIN!”

With a cackle, Rio raced to her room, missing Lilia laying her tarot cards on the table.

“No.”

“Agatha…”

“I said no.”

“Look, Rio is up for settling this,” Jen snapped. “Why can’t you do this for me?”

Agatha clenched her jaw as she turned onto a new street. The only thing worse than Jen nagging her was Jen nagging her through her car’s surround-sound stereo.

“I told you I never want to see her again.”

“Over a misunderstanding?”

“I told you there was no misunderstanding,” Agatha stated sternly. “I didn’t forget the note. She’s lying.”

“Why would she lie?” Jen questioned. “Alice said she was a wreck afterwards.”

“Maybe because she’s a psychopath.”

“You can’t say things like that, Agatha.”

“Yeah, well I just did, and just because you want to hang out with the weird sisters doesn’t mean I have to.” Agatha pulled into her sister’s driveway. “I’ve got to go.”

“I’ll send you Rio’s number,” Jen declared, still unswayed by Agatha’s protests. “Maybe when you’ve calmed down, you’ll realise how childish you’re be-.”

Agatha hung up the call and put the car in park.

Her sister’s house was a world away from her life in the city. The street was quiet, with trees and lawns and an illusion of safety. Agatha walked up the drive and tried the front door, finding it was unlocked.

“You know anyone could just walk in,” she called out as she did just that.

A rush of footsteps rumbled above her, and soon Billy came hurtling down the stairs.

“You’re late,” he commented as he walked towards her, arms open.

“Fashionably,” she added, wrapping her arms around him. Agatha didn’t hug, but she made an exception for Billy. Sometimes holding him was the only thing that calmed the conflicts in her mind. Because she could feel him, warm and solid. Alive and well. That was all that mattered.

Billy pulled away and smiled at her with adoration. “Mum and dad are in the kitchen.”

She followed her nephew to the back of the house and found her sister preparing a salad bowl while Jeff worked on turning steaks on the grill.

“Look at you two,” she teased. “All domestic.”

“We’ve been married for 19 years,” Jeff reminded her, but Agatha waved him off.

“You’re late,” her sister commented. Like mother like son.

Agatha just shrugged. “Traffic.”

She could tell Rebecca didn’t believe her. Her sister probably thought it was work, but it wasn’t. Agatha had been on and off the phone with Jen all day; over and over asking if she could have just ‘thought’ she wrote that damn note for Rio. Like she was trying to convince her she’d made it up. Unfortunately for her, Agatha’s mind was impenetrable, and her excellent memory was fuelled by her signature stubbornness.

Agatha set the table with Billy and helped carry the food through. They went through their usual routine: Jeff talked about work, Rebecca about the neighbours, and Billy complained about a project for school.

“I hate science.”

“You need to pass,” his mother reminded him. “You need to make up for that mid-term.”

“I know, but it’s hard.” Billy looked to his aunt. “Right, Agatha?”

Agatha looked up from her plate. “Huh?”

Rebecca put her cutlery down. “Okay, what’s wrong?”

“Nothing,” Agatha quickly replied.

“Is that why you’ve been too busy pushing your food around to listen to the conversation.”

“I was listening,” Agatha argued defensively.

“You didn’t call the little old lady down the street a bitch, and you didn’t even bite when Jeff said he dinted his car in the McDonalds drive thru.”

Agatha laughed loudly. “What happened? Did the big shiny M distract you?”

Jeff, however, was unaffected. “That would have worked five minutes ago, but you missed your moment.”

Agatha was about to shoot back an insult when her watch vibrated against her wrist. She checked it and saw a message from Jen.

Jen

Here is Rio’s number. Just think about it please!

Agatha scowled down at the digits. She didn’t know who she hated more: Rio or Jen for making her think about Rio.

“What’s wrong?” Billy asked with clear worry. “And don’t lie.”

She waved him off. “Just some personal stuff. Nothing I can’t ignore and make go away.”

“Because that’s a really good coping mechanism,” Rebecca commented. Agatha shot her a glare.

“Tell me what’s happened,” Billy pleaded and, unable to deny her nephew anything, Agatha gave in.

“Do you remember that woman I met in a coffee shop last year?”

“The day before I ran away?” Billy questioned.

“Can’t forget that day,” Jeff added. “My blood pressure…”

“Shut up, Jeff,” Rebecca stopped him, before her eyes fixed on Agatha. “The woman who ghosted you?”

“Rio, yes,” Agatha confirmed. “Well, she just happens to be the sister of Jen’s new girlfriend.”

“What?”

“Seriously?”

“No way!”

“Yes, neither of us knew until we unknowingly agreed to meet at a bar,” Agatha continued. “She was a bitch, and I walked out. Now Jen wants us to work things out, so it doesn’t affect her relationship.”

“Why would you work things out with her?” Billy asked. “She hurt you for no reason.”

“She says I didn’t leave a note,” Agatha explained. “Even though I most certainly did.”

“You did,” Rebecca confirmed. “You told me you did.”

“Well Jen keeps asking me if I’m sure that I did and even though I’ve told her I am, she’s still not convinced. And now she’s sent me Rio’s number.”

“You need to text her,” Billy insisted. “You need to face her so you can move on.”

“No, she needs to stay away from her,” Rebecca argued. “That woman will only hurt her even more.”

“I’m right here,” Agatha reminded them, before looking to her brother-in-law. “What do you have to say?”

“I don’t know, is she still hot?”

“Jeff!”

“Dad!”

“Annoyingly, yes,”

“This is so gross,” Billy grimaced. “I kind of want to see her though. Do you have a picture?”

Agatha grimaced. “Why would I want a picture of her?”

Billy seemed to think for a moment before a mischievous grin appeared on his face. “I just need to check something!”

“What…” Agatha watched her nephew jump up from his chair and bolt out the room. “Hey!”

She ran after him, chasing him up the stairs and through to his room. Her nephew was faster though, and he had already gotten onto his phone by the time she caught up with her.

“What are you doing?”

“Finding Rio,” he announced. “What’s Jen’s last name again?”

“I’m not tell…”

“Never mind. I’ve found her.”

“How…”

Agatha was interrupted by her sister walking into the room. “What’s going on?”

“Your son is antagonising me again,” Agatha accused.

“Yes, and I wonder where he got that from.” Rebecca moved to stand by Billy. “What are you doing?”

“I’m sleuthing,” he told her. “Okay, I’ve found Jen’s girlfriend.”

“How?” Agatha repeated.

Billy held his phone to show her the screen. It was a picture of Alice kissing Jen’s cheek with the caption ‘she’s pretty cute’, accompanied by way too many heart emojis. It made her feel sick.

“Oh good, she’s tagged her,” Billy tapped at his phone. “Now let’s see if I can find Rio.”

Agatha sat down on the edge of his bed. She was so glad she didn’t have social media.

She watched as Billy scrolled and Rebecca supervised. Naively, she hoped Alice hadn’t posted anything of her sister, but unfortunately it seemed the pair were annoyingly close.

Billy gasped. “Is this her?”

“Oh she’s gorgeous,” Rebecca commented, earning surprised looks from her son and sister. “What, she is.”

Agatha stood up to look at the photo. It was taken on what looked like a fire escape, Alice grinning while Rio smirked, holding a cigarette close to her lips. She did indeed look (annoyingly) gorgeous.

Billy clicked on Rio’s tagged profile ( poisonhag , which Agatha thought fit her perfectly) only to find it was private. “Should I request her?”

“No,” his mother and aunt replied in unison. He pouted but went back to the photo. “Even I can see why me running away was a big inconvenience for you.”

Agatha knew he was joking, but she still didn’t like it. “You’ve never inconvenienced me, and it was probably for the best anyway.”

“Hey, can I join the party?” Jeff asked as he walked in. He moved to stand next to his wife and peered down at the phone. “Who’s who?”

“That one is Jen’s girlfriend,” Billy explained. “And that is Rio.”

Jeff looked at Agatha sympathetically. “You weren’t kidding. She’s hot.”

Rebecca elbowed him in the side.

“What? Can you not see…”

“Stop digging your own grave, Dad,” Billy teased, earning a smirk from Agatha.

“Yeah, that’s my job.”

Rebecca sighed. “Can we get back to the matter at hand? Now I know what she looks like, I can see the appeal, but I still think you should stay away from her.”

“Why Mom? She looks cool.”

“She broke your aunt’s heart.”

“But…”

“Enough.” Agatha held up her hands to silence them. “Dinner will be getting cold. My love life can wait.”

Billy smiled. “See, she said love.”

“Downstairs,” all three adults told him, and Billy did as he was told.

“I swear he gets more like you every time you visit,” Rebcca huffed at her sister as she went to follow her son.

“You’re welcome,” Agatha grinned, before she looked to her brother-in-law. “Well?”

Jeff patted her on the back. “Just do what you think is right. Gotta trust your gut.”

Agatha gave him a thankful smile, and the pair headed back downstairs.

The rest of the meal was pretty uneventful, and the Kaplan’s did give her the curtesy of not bringing Rio up again (even if she could tell Billy was desperate to do so).

When she made it back to her apartment, Agatha still hadn’t made up her mind on what to do. She went through her usual night routine: completed chores, picked out her outfit for the next day, then had cuddles and snuggles with Senõr Scratchy, before tucking into reading a manuscript draft.

Usually, she accompanied it with a glass of whisky, but that night, she decided to brew some tea. Warming, calming, soothing. Still, she had read the first page three times and couldn’t take in a word of it. She was too busy thinking about Rio.

The pressure from Jen, the eagerness from Billy, the reluctance from Rebecca. They’d thrown her internal compass out of its usually trustworthy alignment.

“I wish you could talk,” she said to Senõr Scratchy, who was nibbling on some fresh veg she’d thrown in for him. “You’d probably give me some good advice.”

In fact, the only constructive advice had come from Jeff, which was quite unnerving.

“Follow my gut,” she muttered to herself. “You know what? Fuck it.”

She pulled out her phone and added Rio’s number to her contacts. Despite her temptation to give her an insulting nickname, she didn’t want to give the woman any more of her time, so she was simply Rio.

She opened up a message and typed a few versions out:

Jen gave me your number so what do you want?

Hey bitch heard you’ve been lying.

Fuck you I hate your guts!

In the end, she settled on something bland and sent it before she could overthink anymore.

“There,” she said to Senõr Scratchy once more. “Now Jen can stop nagging.”

Senõr Scratchy peered at her out of his cage for a moment before continuing with his feast.

Rio was sat on the fire escape outside of her bedroom window. She leaned against the mental rail, watching the world go by while taking drags of her cigarette.

Lilia didn’t like her smoking inside, which is one of the reasons she shifted to just doing it socially. Beore she met Agatha, she used to smoke a pack every three days. After Agatha, she smoked two packs per day, some days more, until she moved out of Alice’s place. It had taken her five weeks to finish her last pack, but since Agatha came back into her life, she had gone through another in a matter of days.

It calmed her, sitting out on the fire escape with the golden glow from the streetlight illuminating the paths and roads, while sharpening the shadows of those walking by. The city was never quiet, but she found this time of night the closest to tranquil it could get.

Her phone vibrated on the windowsill, and she leaned over to retrieve it. She saw the message and almost dropped her cigarette through the grate.

(Unsaved number)

Hey it’s Agatha. Jen gave me your number.

Rio grinned wickedly. Oh, this was going to be fun. She saved Agatha’s number before typing back a reply.

Rio

Well, well, well. This is a surprise.

She took another drag of her cigarette, and by the time she had finished favouring the nicotine, she’d got a reply.

Agatha

Yeah, yeah. Jen wants us to talk.

She pursed her lips as she responded.

Rio

Alice wants the same. What are we going to do about that?

Agatha

You free 2pm tomorrow?

Rio smirked. Oh this was too good.

Rio

Very specific.

Agatha

Well?

Rio

I can be. Shall we meet at our coffee shop?

Agatha

Fine.

Rio

See you then sweetheart!

Rio stubbed out her cigarette. She had some plotting to do.

The Sabotage

Chapter Notes

hi! this chapter has been so fun to write. let me know what you think!

Agatha paced outside of the coffee shop. People were looking at her like she’d gone crazy, but she had a good reason.

They agreed 2pm. It was currently 2:13. Rio was late.

Agatha hated lateness.

She checked her phone again, and saw she had no messages, no missed calls. Nothing. Cursing under her breath, she called her.

Rio answered almost straight away: Hello?

“You’re nearly 15 minutes late,” Agatha snapped. “Where are you?”

“Chillax m’lady. Turn around.”

Agatha whirled round and saw Rio walking towards her. She was casual: baggy jeans, white t-shirt, with a black denim shirt over the top. Irritatingly adorable.

Rio hung up the phone and smiled at her. “Sorry. I took the wrong subway.”

Agatha’s bullshit detector started ringing, but she chose to ignore it. She gestured to the door. “Ladies first.”

Rio sauntered in and Agatha followed, only to end up ahead when they reached the counter. Unlike the last time they were both there, the place was pretty quiet. The barista was different also and greeted them both with a smile.

“What can I get for you?”

“A black coffee and an iced coffee please.” Agatha glanced back to Rio, who appeared surprised. “Is that still your order?”

Rio nodded and shot her a smile that was too wide to be genuine. Agatha looked away from her. She wasn’t in the mood for her antics.

The barista prepared their drinks and handed them over. Agatha swiped her cup and marched towards a vacant table by the window. She didn’t look back to see if Rio was following, but by the time she was sitting in her seat, the other woman was already settled opposite to her.

“So,” Agatha began.

“So,” Rio repeated.

They sat in awkward silence, neither willing to begin peace discussions. It seemed they had met each other’s matches in the stubborn department. Annoyingly, it was Rio that eventually had the guts to start.

“Alice said you left a note.”

“That’s true,” Agatha stated. “Jen said you couldn’t find it.”

Rio shrugged. “Maybe because there wasn’t one.”

“No, there was.”

“Okay then.” Rio leaned forward in her chair. “Where was it?”

“Oh no,” Agatha protested. “I’m not playing this game.”

“Then what game shall we play?” Rio challenged. “Because you seem very committed to your little lie.”

Agatha clenched her jaw. “I’m not lying.”

“Well neither am I.”

She was, Agatha was sure, but this was getting them nowhere.

“I hate you,” she admitted.

“I hate you too,” Rio added.

“But I love Jen.”

“And I love Alice.”

“So what are we going to do about this?” Agatha questioned. “Because I’m sick of Jen nagging me, and I imagine you’re the same with Alice.”

“Alice doesn’t nag; she politely pesters.”

Weirdo, Agatha thought, but kept her outward civility. “They might not be together forever. Jen’s relationships don’t usually last long.”

“Same with Alice,” Rio added. “So what do you suggest? We just pretend we’re okay until then?”

“I don’t think I’m that good an actor,” Agatha grumbled.

“I think it’s our only option.”

“So what?” Agatha questioned. “We just tell them we’re okay now?”

Rio chuckled. “No, silly. They won’t believe us until they see it. Why don’t we suggest a second take of our little meet-up, give them what they want, then forever make excuses why we can’t see each other.”

Agatha eyed her suspiciously. “You’ve thought this through.”

“I have,” Rio confirmed. “So what do you think?”

The plan was scheming, manipulative, and downright yet devious. It was perfect, though she refused to admit it.

“Well it’s the only plan we have.”

Rio took a sip of her iced coffee, and to anyone else she would look the picture of innocence. “So we’re doing this?”

“I suppose,” Agatha reluctantly agreed. “But you’re organizing this.”

“Oh it will be my pleasure,” Rio grinned. “So, what do you think…”

Agatha’s phone beeped and she saw it was the planned reminder she had asked Sharon to send fifteen minutes before her next meeting. “I’ve got to go.”

Rio’s smiled dropped. “What? Now? We’ve barely sat down.”

“I told you 2pm,” Agatha reminded her. “I’m a busy lady.”

“But…”

“Text me the details,” she ordered before waving. “Au revoir.”

Agatha walked out with her head help high, confident she had established her high ground.

Rio, on the other hand, thought everything was going to plan.

She hadn’t been late. She had actually been twenty minutes early, finding herself a good hiding spot so she could watch for Agatha’s arrival. Soon enough, she arrived and stood outside the coffee shop, dressed in a navy power suit that made it all the sweeter.

She watched Agatha checking the time, her patience thinning by the second. Watched her pace and check her phone. Only when she turned her back and put her phone to her ear did Rio begin to walk towards her, answering the call with a wicked grin.

What she hadn’t expected, however, was for Agatha to remember her coffee order. It wasn’t a complex one. Pretty generic, really. Still, she remembered it, and Rio couldn’t help but wonder what else she remembered. Because she remembered everything about Agatha. Everything. Down to the smell of her pillows in the morning, with the perfume that caught her nostrils as Agatha moved by her to grab her coffee.

God, she hated how much it affected her.

Rio let the conversation run naturally, then dropped in her little plan. A plan Agatha was more than happy to go along with. Her plan B was blackmail, which would have been fun, but perhaps not as effective.

No, she needed Agatha in a false sense of control, and by the way she dismissed her with that teasing little wave, Rio knew she had her exactly where she wanted her.

Alice was very happy with the news. She suggested they meet for drinks the next night. Same place and time as before. Rio had happily agreed and ticked off another part of her scheme.

Lilia commented that Rio had been smiling most of the evening, but Rio kept her reasonings to herself. Why spoil the big surprise?

When Lilia decided to put on Real Housewives, Rio excused herself to sit in her room. She got Webbers out of her enclosure and allowed the tarantula to run up and down her left arm, while her right was other occupied setting in motion the next phase of her plan.

RIO

Drinks tomorrow night with A and J

Agatha replied almost instantly.

AGATHA

I know Jen told me.

RIO

So what’s our story?

AGATHA

Our what??

RIO

You know. How did we become friends?

AGATHA

Friends is a stretch even for a lie

Rio laughed at that.

RIO

Fine. Former enemies. So??

AGATHA

You can just make something up I really don’t care.

Rio grinned in delight. Oh, how she was going to make her regret saying that. She thought for a moment, before messaging her again.

RIO

What are you wearing?

AGATHA

No

RIO

Tease

AGATHA

I’ll block you

RIO

Then I’ll tell Alice and Jen

AGATHA

Snitch

RIO

So what are you wearing?

AGATHA

The exact same outfit I was wearing when you saw me earlier.

RIO

Really? I changed mine ages ago.

AGATHA

Why what are you wearing?

RIO

Nothing.

Agatha stopped replying after that.

Rio cackled and manoeuvred Webbers into her palm. She lifted her up so her many eyes met hers. “Mommy is an evil mastermind, isn’t she?”

Webbers wiggled one of her legs at her and she grinned. This was going to be so much fun.

Agatha arrived at the bar wearing her favourite leather jacket and a simple black dress that hugged her hips just the way she liked it. She wanted to look like she didn’t make much of an effort, but she also wanted to put Rio in a tailspin. (Just like she had been in the night before, her mind plagued with images of Rio in ‘nothing’).

Jen and Alice were sat at a table, Jen’s bag reserving a seat to her left while Alice guarded the one to her right with her boot-clad foot.

Jen smiled when she saw her and put her bag on the floor. “Here’s my best friend.”

Agatha hung her jacket on the back of her chair and sat down. “Just because I did as you asked.”

“And did it go so bad?” Alice asked, smiling with the false knowledge Rio had planted.

“No, it didn’t.”

Jen and Alice shared a smile, and Agatha hid her grimace by looking at her phone.

Billy had sent her a message.

BILLY

can i set you up an ig??

AGATHA

English please?

BILLY

can i make you an instagram account??

AGATHA

No

BILLY

why??

Agatha was about to type out a list of reasons why she would never, ever, join Instagram when she saw Alice wave at someone behind her.

“Rio, over here!”

Forgetting her phone, she turned in her seat to see Rio striding towards them. She was wearing black slacks with a red blouse that cut low enough to show she wasn’t wearing a bra. Agatha quickly turned back to her phone, making a show of not caring.

AGATHA

Because I don’t need one

BILLY

Pleasepleasepleaseplease

Agatha sighed.

AGATHA

We’ll talk about it later.

“Agatha,” Jen scolded. “Leave your work emails alone.”

“Sorry, it was Billy.” Agatha looked to Rio, who was now sat next to her. She forced a smile. “Hi.”

“Hey,” Rio beamed. “Do you not have a drink?”

“No, I only just got here.”

Rio stood again. “Come on then.”

Agatha wanted to protest, but she could feel Jen and Alice watching them closely, so put on another smile and followed Rio to the bar.

“What have they said so far?” Rio asked.

“Nothing, really. They were too busy staring into each other’s eyes and I was too busy trying to deal with my nephew.”

Rio waved over the bartender. “What do you want?”

“I’ll order,” Agatha insisted. “What do you want?”

“No, I’ll get these,” Rio insisted. “You got the coffees.”

“I have a six-figure salary,” Agatha reminded her. “You can pay me back by not making this evening unbearable.”

Rio smirked. “That was almost a perfect sentence.”

Agatha looked at her with a confused frown, before deciding she didn’t want to know. “What do you want?”

“Whatever you’re having.”

The bartender reached them- a blonde twenty-something with a septum piercing and arms covered in tattoos. She looked at Rio first, before her eyes raked over Agatha with a delighted gleam. “What can I get you, gorgeous?”

“Two whiskeys on ice,” she answered, unfazed. Though she was a pretty little thing, she wasn’t Agatha’s type.

“Coming right up,” the bartender said with a wink. Agatha heard Rio mumble something beside her.

“What did you say?”

“I didn’t say anything.”

The bartender came over with the drinks. “Shall I start you a tab?”

“No, we’re good,” Rio spoke for her. “Aren’t we, sweetheart?”

Agatha chose to ignore Rio’s teasing and paid for the drinks, before picking them both up of the counter. She carried them over, all too aware of Rio’s presence behind her, and placed the glasses onto the table.

“Look at you,” Jen praised. “All gentlemanly.”

Agatha shot her a warning look as she sat down.

Alice looked between her and Rio with an excited grin. “So, tell us how you two ended up burying the hatchet.”

Agatha looked to Rio, who was all to happy to step up. “Well, she texted me after Jen sent over my number, and we started texting back and forth, then we called and talked about what happened. We met up yesterday and we realised something?”

Agatha rolled her eyes and took some sips of her whiskey. She knew Rio would make this weird.

“Really?” Alice asked. “What?”

“That we still have feelings for each other.”

Agatha chocked on her drink.

“Shit, Agatha!” Jen patted her on the back. “You okay?”

Agatha nodded and tried to catch her breath.

“Sorry Aggie.” Rio placed a hand on her shoulder. “I know we were going to keep it to ourselves, but after last night and this morning I just…I can’t contain myself.”

Jen hid her head in her hands. “Okay I don’t need to hear about my best friend having sex.”

“Or my sister,” Alice added with equal disgust.

“We didn’t have sex,” Agatha insisted.

“She’s right,” Rio added. “We’re taking things slow, or at least we were. I don’t know, honey. I don’t think I can keep my hands off you for much longer.”

Jen got up. “I need to go to the bathroom.”

Alice watched her girlfriend go before looking to her sister in horror. “Is this a joke?”

Agatha was about to take the out, but Rio beat her to it.

“No, this is real.” She captured Agatha’s hand on the table. “I’m sorry if this causes any issues for you guys, but technically I got there first.”

Agatha didn’t know what to do. Usually, she could talk herself out of anything, make everyone around her feel inferior and assert her dominance. Yet her mind wouldn’t work. No witty comments, no sarcastic remarks, nothing.

The shock seemed to wear off Alice at least, and she smiled. “This is actually great.”

“It is?” Agatha questioned.

“Yes, we can have cute double dates.”

This was a living nightmare.

The rest of the night went by in a daze of lovey dovey nonsense and Rio using any opportunity to turn the conversation to their ‘relationship’. After a few rounds, Jen and Alice said they were calling it a night, so the four of them headed out to wave down some cabs.

“Are you sharing with us?” Alice asked Rio when Jen managed to get a cab, who shook her head.

“I’m going to have a smoke first.”

“Okay, Agatha?”

“I’ll make sure she gets home,” she answered. Oh, she was not done with Rio tonight. Not by a long shot. She waited until the cab drove away before she stormed over to Rio. “What the hell was that?”

Rio didn’t reply, just lit her cigarette and took a drag. “Damn that’s good. Want one?”

“No, I don’t. Why the hell did you do that?”

Rio smirked as she blew out a cloud of smoke. “You said I could make up the story.”

“Yes, the story. Not a fake relationship. You’re going to fix this right now!”

Rio made a show of thinking. “Erm, let me see…nope!”

“Why?”

“Because seeing you struggle, seeing you squirm. It really warms the heart.”

“You don’t have a heart,” Agatha accused.

“Yes, I do. It’s black.” Rio batted her eyelashes ridiculously. “And it beats for you.”

Blowing a puff of smoke in Agatha’s direction, Rio turned on her heel and walked towards a taxi that had just pulled up. Stubbing out her cigarette on a lamppost, she tossed Agatha a teasing wave.

“Te veo”.

Agatha glared at the disappearing cab. It seemed she had underestimated her rival, but two could play at that game.

The Deal

Chapter Notes

hi! i hope you enjoy the new chapter! i'm going away tomorrow but i'll have at least one chapter ready to post on wednesday!

Rio waited in the foyer for the building; on a sofa that was probably more expensive than her and Lilia’s apartment, watching people walk by in suits that were also probably more expensive than her and Lilia’s apartment. And there she sat in her baggy jeans, bobbly black sweater, and off-white converse. Very out of place.

Yet she had been invited, with her first name at the front desk, and given the instruction to sit there until someone came to get her.

That someone turned out to be a tiny grandma with a big smile. “Are you Rio?”

“I am.” Rio got to her feet.

“Ms Harkness asked if I’d come down and get you. Please, follow me.”

Rio followed the woman to the elevator and waited until the doors closed to speak again. “Do you work for Agatha?”

“I’m her assistant,” the woman replied, holding out her hand. “Sharon Davis.”

Rio took her hand and shook it firmly. “Rio Vidal.”

The elevator opened on the twelfth floor, and Sharon led her out into an open space of desks, an expensive suit person sat at each one. They watched her as she followed Sharon across the room, all likely wondering what a girl like her was doing in a place like that.

Turning a corner at the far side of the room, Sharon stopped by a lone desk and picked up the phone.

“Agatha, Miss Vidal is here for you…Yes, that’s her.” Sharon put the phone down and pointed to the door opposite. “She says go in when you’re ready.”

Rio stared at the door, willing her legs to move. Messing with Agatha was all fun and games in the outside world but in this office, in this building, she had to admit she was a little intimidated.

“Here.” Sharon handed her a polka dot backing tin. “That’ll soften her up for you.”

“Thanks.” Rio gave the woman a small smile before making her way through the door.

Agatha’s office was huge. Bigger than her apartment huge, with a conference table, an area with couches surrounding a TV, and bookshelves. Lots of those. She spotted Agatha sat at her large desk, her back to her as she stared out the window.

Rio shut the office door and carried the baking tin across the room towards her.

“Agatha Harkness,” she tested the name on her lips. “It suits you.”

Agatha looked at her and pointed to the chair opposite. “Sit.”

Rio sat and put the tin on the desk. Agatha eyed it suspiciously. “What’s that?”

“Your assistant told me to bring it in.”

Agatha leaned forward and tore off the lid, before shoving her hand in and retrieving a cookie. “This is why you hire a grandmother.” She took a bite out of the cookie and groaned in a way that made Rio slightly envious. “Fuck me, those are good.”

Curious, Rio took one and cautiously bit into it, only to moan in ecstasy. “Did she make these?”

“She did, now let’s cut to the chance.” Agatha placed her cookie down on her desk and folded her arms. “What do you want?”

“Huh?” Rio asked through a mouthful of cookie.

“This little game you’re playing,” Agatha accused. “I want you to tell Alice and Jen we were messing around, and that we are barely even friends.”

“Why would I do that?” Rio leaned back in her chair. “I’m having so much fun.”

“Come on, there must be something you want.”

Rio didn’t respond, instead she reached out and grabbed a photo frame sat on the desk. She turned it over to see it was a picture of Agatha and a boy with black curly hair grinning at the camera.

“Is this your nephew?”

Agatha snatched the frame back and put it in her desk draw. “Well? What is it? Do you want money? Do you want me to apologise for leaving?”

“Nope, but I wouldn’t say no to either.”

“Then what is it?” Agatha demanded.

Rio stared Agatha down. “I want you to admit you never wrote the note.”

“Okay?” Agatha shifted in her chair. “So you want me to lie?”

“No, I want you to tell the truth,” Rio countered.

Agatha stood from her chair. “So you want me to say that I did write the note.”

“No I don’t!”

“Then I’m confused.” Agatha began to slowly walk round the desk. “Because you want me to tell the truth, and you also want me to lie. So what do you actually want?”

“Stop playing games,” Rio demanded, but soon found Agatha towering over her. She watched as the woman leaned down, bracing her hands on the arms of her chair.

“You started it, hun. I’m just finishing it. Now what I want you to do is call up your sister and tell her we were just messing around, and then I never want to see you again.”

Rio swallowed. She could smell Agatha’s perfume again, and she couldn’t think properly. “And if I refuse?”

“Then you’ll be hearing from my lawyers,” Agatha answered. “A cease and desist, or a good old defamation suit. I’ll let them decide, just as I’m letting you decide what you do. But don’t take too long. I’ll be calling my lawyer tomorrow morning.”

Shit, Shit. Shit. Rio barely had enough money to get through her degree, let alone pay for legal costs.

“You can’t file anything against me.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “I can’t?”

“No, because I haven’t done anything wrong, legally anyway, and besides…you don’t even know my last name!”

Agatha laughed and moved away from her. “Vidal right?”

Shit.

Agatha grabbed a sticky note and a pen. “Is that spelt V-I-D-A-L?”

“I hate you.”

Agatha smiled smugly. “I hate you more.”

Rio glowered at her, before surging forward and grabbing a load of cookies.

“Hey!” Agatha protested, but Rio was already running out of the room.

“Thanks for the cookies,” she said to Sharon as she raced by.

“Anytime dear,” Sharon called after her. “See you again soon.”

Rio didn’t respond, just ran through the office and back into the elevator. When the doors shut, she leaned against the wall, the cookies still clutched to her chest.

Agatha Harkness was certainly a piece of work.

Another dinner at the Kaplans. Billy had nagged enough that Rebecca had invited her round, and since it was Friday and she had no meetings after 3, Agatha decided to head out early. She pulled up just as Billy was walking in from school, and seeing the grin when he saw her was worth the mountain of emails that would be waiting for her Monday morning.

It was said smile that also led to her being slumped on the couch while Billy tapped away at her phone.

“Okay, what do you want your name to be?”

“How about my name?” Agatha frowned.

“No I mean like your handle.”

Agatha just stared at him.

“I’ll make one up.” He bit his lip in thought before grinning. “Please say this isn’t taken.”

“What?” She leaned over to see what he was doing. “No.”

“Why?”

“I’m not a mother.”

“But you are mother.”

“What does that even mean?”

Billy’s shoulders slumped in defeat. “Okay let me think of another one….Oh!” He typed something before showing it to her. “What do you think?”

She read it and grimaced. “Really?”

“Well do you have any better ideas?”

Agatha snatched the phone from him and tested a few names before finding one that fit. She handed the phone back to him. “There.”

“That’s the first one I wrote?”

“I am a mother,” she argued. “To Senõr Scratchy.”
