“MotherHarkness it is then.” Billy grinned. “Now for a profile picture. Let me go through your photos…”

Agatha quickly took the phone off him. “Why don’t you send over one of your photos of me.”

Billy eyed her suspiciously before picking up his own phone and scrolling through his camera roll.

“Oh, I like this one.” He showed her a picture of her leaning in the dining room doorway with one of her work suits on.

“When did you take that?”

“A few weeks ago,” he admitted. “For snapchat.”

“Why did you put me on snapchat?”

“Only to Eddie.”

Agatha decided to let it slide. She quite liked Billy’s boyfriend, though she had been reluctant to trust him with her nephew’s heart.

“Fine, send it to me.”

“I’ll send a selfie of us too,” he added. “For your first post. Do you want me to show you how?”

“I…”

A notification appeared at the stop:

You have been added to the group: Double date!!!

Agatha moved the phone away, but she wasn’t quick enough.

“You’re going on a…”

“Nope,” she told him, before opening up the message. It was from an unrecognised number, but from looking at who else was in the group, she knew who it was.

ALICE

Hi ladies so we’re thinking of going for a picnic tomorrow. Are you two free?

Agatha ignored the message. It seemed Rio hadn’t told her sister yet, and she was already drafting the email to her lawyer in her head.

“Now,” she said, opening up Instagram again. “Let’s post something?”

Billy stared at her for a moment before nodding and pointing out what she needed to do.

By the time dinner was ready, Agatha had a cute profile picture, a snappy bio and a cute selfie of her and her favourite (only) nephew. She had followed Billy, Rebecca, Jeff, Jen, and a few authors she liked. It actually didn’t appear as fickle as she thought it would be. In fact, she was so engrossed, she had it open at the dinner table.

“Agatha, we have a no phone policy,” Rebecca reminded her. “Put it away or it’s going in the kitchen.”

Agatha rolled her eyes and put it on her lap.

“Leave her be, Mom,” Billy quickly jumped to her aid. “She’s only just discovered social media.”

“Well she can discover it after dinner.”

Her watch vibrated and Agatha tapped her phone, only to see it was a notification from that stupid group chat. She discarded her food again to open it, hoping it would be Rio saying no, saying they weren’t dating, ending this stupid game once and for all.

Nope, it was Jen.

JEN

And another miracle- Agatha Harkness has joined ig

A response popped up as she was reading.

ALICE

Followed you Agatha!!

Agatha checked her Instagram and, sure enough, Alice had followed her. After a moments contemplation, she followed her back.

“Agatha honestly!” Rebecca huffed. “What example are you setting for Billy?”

“That rules are for suckers.”

While her nephew and brother-in-law tried to hide their amusement, her sister wasn’t at all tickled by her antics.

“No more phone!”

Agatha tutted and began stabbing her food with her fork.

Rebecca put down her cutlery and knelt her elbows against the table. “So I was down the grocery store the other day…”

“News of the century,” Agatha sassed, before her wrist buzzed with another notification, then another.

“I bumped into someone.”

“Right.” Agatha tapped on her screen and saw two new notifications:

@poisonhag has followed you

@poisonhag has commented on your post

Great.

“Well aren’t you curious who it was?”

“Not really,” Agatha answered as she opened the comment under her and Billy’s selfie

@poisonhag: cuteness must run in the family 😉

Agatha was going to kill her. Honestly, she was going to…

“It was Wanda.”

Agatha’s head snapped up. “What?”

“She came to drop the kids off at Vis’s place  and decided to pick up some groceries. She asked about you.”

Agatha could feel Billy watching her closely. Concerned. She put on her coldest mask.

“Well I don’t care about her.”

“She asked if you were seeing anyone,” Rebecca continued. “She said she’s not. So I told her you weren’t, and…”

“That’s not true,” Billy interjected, causing all the adults to look at him in surprise. Especially Agatha.

“What are you talking about, kid?” Agatha said with a nervous laugh. “I’m not seeing anyone.”

“Yes you are.”

“No I’m not,” she insisted before looking back to her sister. “What did she say next?”

“She asked me to pass her new number on to you.”

Agatha started stabbing her food again. “I don’t want her number.”

“Agatha…”

“She doesn’t want it because she’s seeing someone,” Billy accused. “I saw her phone. She’s going on a double date.”

“You are?” Rebecca questioned. “Since when?”

“I’m not.”

“Don’t lie.” Billy glowered at her. “Why won’t you tell me? I tell you everything.”

“Because I’m a grown up and I don’t have to do anything,” she shot back.

“That’s not a denial,” Jeff pointed out. Agatha angled her fork in his direction.

“Who is she?” Rebecca asked.

“She’s no one.”

“So there is someone.”

Agatha sighed and sat back in her chair.

“Well Wanda seems interested,” Rebecca added. “And I know things were messy there, but…”

Nope, nope. Absolutely not.

“Okay, Billy’s right. I am seeing someone.”

“I knew it!” Billy grinned. “Who?”

Agatha sucked in a deep breath. She couldn’t believe she was doing this.

“What are you smiling at?”

“Nothing,” Rio insisted, but Lilia wasn’t convinced.

“You’ve been smiling at that phone for 10 minutes.”

Rio scoffed. “No I haven’t.”

Lilia shifted in her spot on the couch and looked back to the TV. “Whoever she is, I’m guessing she’s pretty.”

Rio looked back at the photo: a teenage boy grinning at the camera, with Agatha smiling beside him. The picture of radiance. She bit her lip to stop herself from grinning at the memory of that morning. Even the threat of a lawsuit, the way Agatha leaned over, the way her voice went deep with threat.

Oh she was enjoying this so much.

She just wished she could have seen Agatha’s face when she saw her comment. It served her right for having her profile on public.

She continued to stare at the image until a notification popped up. When she saw who it was from, she closed Instagram immediately.

AGATHA

Have you spoke to Alice yet?

RIO

Still haven’t made my mind up…you gave me until the morning.

It wasn’t a lie. Rio had spent most of the day trying to decide what to do. Though the thought of going to court against Agatha being an entertaining one, she knew the reality of it wouldn’t be so much fun.

AGATHA

Hold off on that. What’s your address?

She bolted upright.

“What’s wrong?” Lilia asked, but Rio ignored her as she hastily typed out her address. She got a reply almost instantly.

AGATHA

Come meet me outside when I text you.

Rio jumped to her feet and daryed towards her room. “I’m heading out for a while.”

“Where?” Lilia questioned. “It’s getting late.”

“I don’t know, but I need to change.”

As adorable as she felt in her comfy pjs, she needed to look good for Agatha. To help with the manipulation, of course. She threw on some jeans and a black hoodie, and applied some light make up. Enough to look good, but not enough to make it obvious that she actually tried.

It took Agatha a while to arrive, and Rio spent most of the wait alternating between pacing the floor and checking she looked okay.

When she finally got the text, she all but ran out the apartment, ignoring Lilia’s shouts to slow down. She made it down to the street and spotted a car pulled up outside: a slick black Mercedes that shimmered in the glow of the streetlamps. Yep, definitely her.

Rio climbed into the passenger seat and greeted Agatha with a wide smile. “You wanted to see me?”

“Want is a stretch.” Agatha indicated to pull out and began driving down the street.

“Where are we going?” Rio asked, not too worried that she was being driven her away into the night by a woman who openly hated her.

“Nowhere,” Agatha answered. “I’ll take you back when we’re done talking.”

“Okay, then what do you want to talk about?”

“Us. This stupid situation you’ve thrown us in. My nephew saw that damn group Alice made and now my family think we’re dating too.”

Rio laughed. She certainly hadn’t anticipated that!

“It’s not funny!” Agatha snapped. “They want you to come round for dinner at some point.”

Rio’s laugh grew louder.

“Will you stop laughing!” Agatha snapped. “It’s not like I wanted this to happen.”

Rio wiped a stary tear from her cheek. “You could have just told them the truth, you know, or come up with a better lie.”

Agatha stayed silent.

“Wait a minute, you want them to think we’re dating.” Rio grinned wickedly. “Oh you little liar.”

“Shut up,” Agatha snapped. “I didn’t have a choice.”

Rio laughed again. “Whatever you say.”

“So I’ll play your little game as long as you keep up the charade when my family is involved.”

“Does this mean I get to meet your beloved nephew?”

“That is to be decided.” Agatha indicated to go down a side street, and they started heading back towards Rio’s building. “Accept the picnic invitation. We’ll take photos, play our parts, then in a few weeks, we’ll break up and I never want to see you again. Do you understand?”

“What do I get out of this?” Rio questioned. “Besides getting to tease you as much as I want?”

“What do you want?”

“You know what I want.”

“No.”

“Then I’ll text Alice right now, and you’ll have to deal with whatever it is you need a fake girlfriend for.”

“Fine,” Agatha huffed. “I’ll do what you want, but after we ‘break up’.”

“Sounds like a good deal to me.”

Agatha braked harshly outside Rio’s building. “I’ll pick you up tomorrow.”

“What a gentleman,” Rio teased as she climbed out of the car. “See you then, lover .”

The moment Rio shut the car door, Agatha sent the car hurtling off down the street.

Rio sucked in the night air and smiled up at the starless sky. Cosmic karma definitely adored her.

The Picnic

Chapter Notes

i can't believe the finale is in a few hours i don't want this show to be over! still, i hope you all enjoy this chapter! i'm half way through the next one so will hopefully post later!

Rio shrugged on her denim jacket and admired herself in her bedroom mirror. Cute jeans, cute top, cute open shirt. Yep. She looked good.

Waving bye to Webbers, she walked out into the living area. Lilia was sat at the table with her cards.

“You look nice,” she commented. “So is this a date?”

“It is,” Rio confirmed with a grin. “A double date.”

Lilia shuffled her cards. “Want a reading?”

Rio was about to answer when she got a message.

AGATHA

Outside

Rio smirked and moved to sit down in front of Lilia.

“How about reading of gifts?” the older woman suggested and Rio nodded.

Lilia lay three cards and turned the middle one. “This is your focal point.”

It was the Ace of Cups.

“Perhaps love, perhaps a fresh start,” Lilia explained. “Perhaps a combination of the two. Eitehr way, it suggests peace in oneself.”

Rio got another text.

AGATHA

Hello??

“Now the gift to give.” Lilia turned over another card. Judgement. “Forgiveness of past mistakes.”

A sharp sound of a car horn cut through the quiet apartment. Rio smirked deviously.

Lilia turned the last card as the beeping continued. “The gift to receive. The Lovers.”

Rio grimaced at that. “Seriously?”

Lilia chuckled. “This card looks very on the nose, but…what the hell is that racket?”

“My date,” Rio answered.

“What are you doing here then?” Lilia questioned. “Go to her!”

Rio waited until she heard Agatha hold down the horn in one continuous honk before getting up. “Right I’ll see you later.”

“Behave yourself,” Lilia called after her, but Rio simply laughed and walked out of the apartment.

When she got outside, Agatha was still pressing the horn, and didn’t stop until Rio was sat in the passenger seat.

“So impatient,” Rio teased, earning a glare.

“Well now we’re late.”

“We’re still 45 minutes early.”

“Well I have to get there,” Agatha reminded her, “and park, and pay for the parking, and find a spot to set up.”

“Alice will be there already,” Rio assured. “She said she’s got the perfect layout planned.”

Agatha grimaced. “This is one of worst day of my life.”

“What are the others?” Rio asked, but Agatha ignored her and sped off down the street.

Despite trying to initiate conversation, Agatha gave her the silent treatment the rest of the way there, only acknowledging her as they were parking up.

“No weird stuff today,” she warned her.

“I can’t help it,” Rio argued. “I’m a huge weirdo.”

“Oh I know,” Agatha assured. “I mean don’t act like you did at the bar.”

Rio batted her eyelashes. “But you said I could tease you as much as I liked?”

Agatha got out of the car and slammed the door behind her. Rio smirked and followed her out of the car, only to find her rummaging in the trunk.

“What are you doing?”

Agatha pulled out a wicker picnic basket before shutting the trunk with another slam. “It’s a picnic, remember?”

Rio moved to peak at what was inside, but Agatha swatted her hand away and strutted off towards the park entrance. They spotted Alice and Jen already sat under a tree, Jen leaning against Alice’s side as Alice draped an arm around her.

Rio stole a look at Agatha before moving to take her hand.

Agatha quickly pulled away from her. “What are you doing?”

“Holding your hand. We’re dating, remember?”

“Is that really necessary,” Agatha argued. “Jen knows I’m not into PDA.”

“But we need to be convincing!”

Agatha grumbled but grabbed her hand anyway. Her hand was warm and soft, and Rio shifted hers to lace their fingers together.

“Happy?” Agatha asked.

“Very,” Rio answered, trying to ignore the way her heart was doing silly little Summersaults.

Jen sat up when she saw them, clearly surprised. “Agatha Harkness all loved up!”

“Shut up.” Agatha handed the basket to Alice. “I didn’t know what you already had.”

“Chips and dip, mostly,” Alice answered. “And some diet cokes.”

Once she and Agatha sat down, Rio crawled forward to help Alice unpack the basket. Fresh pastries, finger sandwiches, those fancy bottles of water. She knew Agatha had a flashy lifestyle, but this was another level of fancy.

“So Agatha what do you do for work?” Alice asked.

“I work in publishing,” Agatha answered. “What about you?”

Alice shrugged. “I bounce around a lot. My last job was working security at a department store, until I got fired.”

Rio knew the story but enjoyed seeing Agatha’s reacting frown. “What? Did you tackle someone?”

“No, we had an event and I slept with the special guest.”

Agatha’s frown turned to a scandalized gasp. She looked to Jen. “Did you know this?”

Jen chuckled. “Yeah, I was there.”

“But…wait you met at that pop up event you did?”

“They more than met that day,” Rio added, and Alice kicked her foot.

Agatha looked to Rio. “You knew?”

“She’s my sister. We tell each other everything, sweetheart. Everything .”

Agatha gave her a tight smile. “It’s a good thing we’re taking things slow then, honey. I don’t think your sister would be able to look me in the eye.”

Jen cleared her throat. “Agatha come find a bathroom with me.”

“But…”

“Now,” Jen said as she stood.

Agatha sighed and patted Rio on the knee. “Excuse us.”

Rio watched her go, her fingertips instinctively brushing the spot that still tingled from Agatha’s touch.

She heard Alice laugh and looked to her, confused. “What’s so funny?”

“You’ve got it bad,” Alice teased.

“Like you and Jen aren’t sickening,” she argued. “And we’re still in the honeymoon phase. You guys have no excuse.”

Alice held up her hands in defence. “Okay, okay. It’s just nice to see you so happy.”

“Yeah, I guess I am,” Rio smiled. She was certainly enjoying herself, anyway.

Alice’s smile morphed into a nervous expression. “I need to talk to you about something.”

“Please tell me you’re not proposing,” Rio half-joked. “You know I support a good U-Haul but that would be too quick.”

Alice chuckled. “No, no. I decided to go to Mom’s storage locker.”

“By yourself.” Rio usually went with her once a year to look through what remained of Lorna Wu’s physical estate: a cube storage locker off the interstate. It was mostly her old 70s garb, some cool and others dated. They each had one of her iconic necklaces too: Alice’s had an orange hexagon pendant while Rio had a Stevie nicks style silver moon. Alice wore hers every day. Rio only wore hers when she could stomach it.

“I want to take Jen,” Alice admitted. “So she can get to see what Mom was like. I went looking for some photo albums to show her, but I ended up finding something else.”

“An unreleased album?”

“No, I found her diaries.”

That was even more priceless. “Have you read them?”

“A bit,” Alice answered. “It’s weird. She should have been the one telling me these stories.”

“In a way she is,” Rio pointed out. “I’m glad you’ve got that.”

Alice gave her a sad smile. “You can read them with me if you want. She was your mom too.”

“When you’ve read them, maybe.” Rio didn’t want to impose. If she had anything like that of her mom, she would hold onto it for dear life.

“Does Agatha know?”

“About your mom or mine?”

“Either?”

“Nope.”

“Rio…”

“We’re having fun at the minute,” Rio explained truthfully. “It’s not time for serious the stuff yet.”

“I don’t know. It seems serious if you’re planning on waiting.”

Rio shrugged. “We’re courting.”

Alice looked at her cynically. “Whatever you say.”

“Jen.” Agatha tried to keep up with her friend as she marched across the park. “Jen, the bathroom sign said the other way.”

“I don’t want to find the bathroom,” Jen huffed. “I’m so mad at you.”

“Mad?” Agatha questioned. “Why? What have I done now?”

Jen whirled round to face her. “What game are you playing?”

“I’m not playing any games,” Agatha lied. “What are you talking about?”

Jen scoffed. “Oh please. Alice loves the thought of her sister being happy so much that she can’t see you’re messing with her.”

“Me?” Agatha questioned, her outrage for real this time. “I’ve done nothing wrong here. You wanted me and Rio to get along, and now we are. I honestly can’t believe this. I can’t win!”

Jen folded her arms. “So you genuinely have feelings for her?”

“Yes!”

“Do you promise?”

“I promise you that the feelings I have for Rio are genuine.”

Technically not a lie. She genuinely couldn’t stand her.

Jen stared her down, but Agatha remind firm in her twisted truth. Eventually, Jen gave up.

“Fine, but stop talking about your sex life with my girlfriend.”

“That is all Rio, and we’ve not had sex yet anyway. And won’t for a while either.”

“Why?” Jen questioned. “This isn’t Downton Abbey.”
”Because we’re still getting to know each other.”

Jen laughed at that. “Okay, look I admire the intention but you and I both know that you two will be pretty much living together this time next week.”

Agatha folded her arms. “We’ll see about that.”

Jen’s smile dropped. “It wasn’t a challenge.”

Agatha held out her hand. “Three weeks.”

“Agatha…”

“Winner wins the satisfaction of being right.”

Jen shook her head in disbelief but accepted her hand anyway. “I think I might have a shot of winning this one.”

“A bit too confident, aren’t we?”

Jen walked past Agatha to head back towards their dates. “I’m telling you this time next week…”

Agatha didn’t respond, just smiled smugly as they returned to the little picnic.

“Hey sweetheart.” Rio patted the space on the blanket beside her. “Come sit.”

Agatha sat and tried not to move when Rio shuffled to lean against her.

“You didn’t get into any trouble while I was gone l, did you?”

“Not at all,” Rio insisted. “I’m your little angel, remember?”

Agatha genuine laughed at that. “More like my little devil.”

Jen made a gagging sound. “Okay you two are gross.”

Agatha met Rio’s gaze and put on her best smile, trying to ignore the genuine pull on her lips when she saw the way Rio’s eyes sparkled.

It seemed they were actually quite convincing.

The Dinner

Chapter Notes

sorry for the delay! the finale really took over my life yesterday! i hope you enjoy this chapter!

Agatha knocked on the apartment door impatiently. Rio had said she wasn’t ready yet and told her to come up, meaning she had to put money in a meter and abandon her car in what was an unsavoury neighbourhood in comparison to her own. She swore if there was a single mark on that car when they got back down there, Rio would be paying for every penny.

The door opened and an older woman with grey curls and flamboyant clothing opened the door. The woman looked Agatha up and down before folding her arms. “You’re Agatha.”

“I am, who are you?”

“Rio’s roommate.”

Of course she was. “Is she ready?”

“Not yet, but you can wait in here.” The woman let Agatha inside before slamming the door behind her. “Take a seat at the table.”
Agatha sat down, and the woman quickly moved to sit opposite her.

“I know who you are.”

“I gathered,” Agatha sassed.

“And I think Rio is making a huge mistake giving you another chance.”

“Funny, my sister feels the same about her.” Agatha countered.

“You hurt her, and I’ll hurt you,” the woman threatened. “Do you understand me?”

Agatha laughed. “Wha-”

“I said do. you. understand. me?”

Agatha avoided the woman’s eyes, keeping her composure the best she could as she nodded.

“Good.” The woman put on a sickly-sweet smile. “You can call me-”

“LILIA!” Rio’s voice boomed from an adjoining room. “IS THAT AGATHA?”

“Yes, she’s here!” Lilia called back.

“Send her in!”

Lilia waved for her to go. “Don’t keep her waiting any longer than you already have.”

Agatha gave her a spiteful smile before marching towards Rio’s room and opened the door.

“What’s taking so…nope absolutely not!”

“Why?” Rio looked down at her outfit. “You said to wear a dress.”

The dress was black, tight, and whole she couldn’t actually see anything, it was obvious she wasn’t wearing a bra.

“Not that dress.”

Rio smirked. “If you don’t like this dress, you won’t like my other ones.”

Agatha sighed. “Where is that blouse you wore at the bar?”

Rio pointed to a mountain of crumpled clothes in the corner of the room. Agatha hadn’t noticed it before; the room was generally just a mess.
“Well you can’t go like that.”

Rio stared her down before smirking and picking a black jumper off her bed. “I wasn’t going to,” she said before pulling the jumper on. “Better?”

Agatha nodded.

“Good,” Rio grinned. “Just let me touch up my make up.”

Agatha sat down on the bed and properly took in her surroundings. The room was very…earthly. Lots of real plants, fake plants, pictures of plants, books about plants- most of which were left open on a desk that was almost hidden by all the mess.

“Is that your laptop?” Agatha stared at the dated machine sat amongst the mess. “It’s ancient.”

“It’s not that old,” Rio dismissed. “And it works fine most of the time.”

Agatha pursed her lips and carried on studying the room, her eyes soon landing on a tank filled with greenery. In it, a small brown creature was climbing on a rock.

“Is that your tarantula?”

“Webbers, yeah.”

“Webbers,” Agatha repeated as she got up to get a closer look. “It’s quite fluffy, isn’t it?”

“She’s beautiful,” Rio said with pride. “Do you want to hold her?”

Agatha quickly moved away. “Not on your life.”

Rio’s reflection grinned at her. “Is the great Agatha Harkness scared of spiders?”

“No,” she quickly insisted. “I just don’t like them.”

Rio put her mascara down and turned to face her. “What do you think?”

Dammit, Agatha thought, she was stupidly annoying beautiful.

“It’ll do,” she said dismissively. “You ready to go?”

Rio nodded and held out her hand.

“No.”

“Come on.” Rio wiggled her fingers. “Let’s get into character.”

Agatha grumbled but took her hand anyway. This was already a disaster, and they hadn’t even gotten to her sisters yet.

Agatha’s family lived in a boring-looking house on a boring street in a boring town in suburbia.
All the lawns looked the same, and they all had the same types of cars and curtains, and Rio guessed every house had the same floor plan.

It was a good thing she was here to liven things up a little.

“Right,” Agatha said as they walked up to the front door. “Don’t touch anything, don’t start with the weird flirting, and don’t antagonize anyone. Well besides my brother-in-law. He’s fair game.”

“Noted.” Rio was definitely not going to follow any of those rules.

Agatha didn’t even have chance to knock before the door flew open, revealing a tall teenage with familiar black curls and a scar across his eyebrow. Agatha’s nephew.

“You’re both here!” He grinned. “Come in, come in.”

Agatha walked in like she owned the place, and Rio tried to enter as confidently as she could. No matter how much she enjoyed messing with Agatha, she was a guest in someone else’s home, and she was raised with some manners at least.

The boy stood before her and held out his hand. “I’m Billy.”

Rio smiled and shook his hand firmly. “I’m Rio.”

“I’m so glad you agreed to come over,” he said enthusiastically. “Mostly so I can tell you some of my best Aunt Agatha stories.”

Rio waited for Agatha to sass the boy, but she didn’t, instead she ruffled his hair and walked further into the house. “Rebecca?”

“In here,” a voice replied down the hall.

Billy signalled for Rio to go ahead, and so she followed Agatha through into the kitchen. There, a brunette woman in a navy dress was stirring something in a large pot (from the smell, she guessed a tomato-based dish) and a man in a cheap suit leaned against the counter looking at his phone.

Both looked up when they noticed them, their eyes going from Agatha, then to Rio, then to Agatha again.

“Rio, this is my sister, Rebecca, and my brother-in-law, Jeff,” Agatha introduced. “Guys, this is Rio.”

Rebecca abandoned stirring to walk towards them, stopping in front of Rio. She was pretty, Rio decided. She didn’t have the same powerfully sharp features as her sister. Her face was softer, lighter, while her deep brown eyes contrasted Agatha’s blue.

“It’s so nice to meet you finally.” Rebecca’s smile was forced. That kind of sickly forced smile that middle-aged housewives seemed to find second nature. “I’m guessing you’ve already met Billy.”

“Yes, though I feel like I’ve met him ten times over,” Rio lied. “Agatha talks so much about him.”

She saw Billy smile and duck his head, while Agatha hid her face in embarrassment. Neither of the boy’s parents looked surprised though.

“Dinner will be ready soon,” Rebecca stated as she walked back to the stove. “Please, make yourself at home.”

“Follow me!” Billy insisted. He led them through to a living area filled with ugly furniture and family photographs. A family home, Rio noted. She couldn’t even remember what one of those felt like.

Billy gestured to the couch. “Please, sit.”

“Chill, kid,” Agatha told him, her signature curt tone softer than usual. She sat down and Rio followed, their legs touching as they settled on the couch.

Billy perched in an armchair. “Rio, Agatha told me you like poisonous plants.”

Rio wouldn’t have put it quite like that. “I find them interesting, yes.”

“Have you seen a belladonna in real life?”

“Seen one? I’ve held one.”

Billy stared at her in awe, while Agatha looked, dare she say, concerned. “Can’t that kill you?”

“I know what I’m doing,” Rio assured. “The leading cause of plant toxin deaths is ignorance.”

“I’m sure it’s the fact they’re literal poison,” Agatha argued.

“We’re not having this debate now, Aggie.” Rio savoured the warning look Agatha gave her at the nickname. “I’m sure Billy has a list of things he wishes to discuss, and I him.”

“Really?” Billy sat up in his chair. “Ask me anything.”

Rio glanced at Agatha. “What is the most embarrassing thing your aunt has ever done?”

A mischievous smile appeared on Billy’s face, and Agatha was quick to point a warning finger at him.

“Don’t you dare.”

Billy was unaffected by the warning and looked to Rio with humour in his eyes. “She dressed as Senõr Scratcy last Halloween and ended up getting so drunk on my dad’s spiked punch that she decided it was a good idea to ride up and down the street on my bike. We found her and the bike in a hedge, fast asleep. My boyfriend had to help me carry her back because my dad had also drunk too much punch.”

“I don’t even want to know what he put in that,” Agatha commented, but Rio just laughed.

“Please say you’ve got photos.”

Billy went to get his phone out of his pocket, but Agatha held up her hand to stop him. “William Kaplan, if you humiliate me in front of my girlfriend, Eddie is finding out about the Thanksgiving incident.”

Billy gasped. “You wouldn’t.”

“You know I would.”

Billy’s shoulders slumped and he put his phone away.

“You’re no fun,” Rio playfully scolded, but Agatha just rolled her eyes.

“So Rio,” Billy said again. “Are you from here?”

“I’m from many places,” she answered. “My childhood was spent moving more than staying.”

She could feel Agatha studying her curiously, but it was Billy who spoke up. “Like where?”

“New York, LA, Miami, Las Vegas, Paris, Barcelona, London, even Sydney for a few months.”

Both aunt and nephew blinked at her in surprise.

“You’ve lived, like, everywhere cool,” Billy commented. “Was it fun?”

Rio shrugged. “Some of it was but living in hotels and travelling here, there and everywhere can be tiring.”

“Why did you move around so much?” Agatha asked, before catching herself. “I mean you told me you moved a lot, but that’s a lot .”

“For my step-mom’s work,” Rio answered. “The good thing about it was me and Alice had some great adventures.”

Rebecca called them through for dinner soon after, with Jeff at the head of the table and Billy sitting opposite Agatha, Rio found herself opposite Rebecca. Their eyes met across the table, and she could see the little housewife mask slipping off to reveal a shadow of distain.

Rebecca definitely hated her.

Jeff luckily was oblivious and began to yapper on about his car as they tucked into to ridiculously good spaghetti and meatballs.

“The mechanic told me it would take more than the car was worth to get the bump out.”

“Why not get a new car?” Billy suggested.

“Because I like the car I have,” Jeff answered.

“Then get the same car?” Rebecca suggested.

“No, I like that car.”

“Pay to fix it then,” Agatha snapped.

“But they said it’s a waste of money.”

Rio but her lip as not to jump in. Though Agatha had given her the green light, she knew Rebecca wouldn’t take it well if she antagonised her husband.

“Why don’t you get a second opinion?” She said instead. “That way, you might have options.”

“Or you could live with the bump,” Agatha added. “That way you’ll always remember to turn when you see the shiny M.”

Rio looked at her in confusion.

“He bumped it in the McDonald’s drive through,” Agatha explained.

“Oh. so it’s not just a bump, it’s a McBump.”

Billy laughed, and she could see Agatha pushing down a smirk. Jeff looked like he was used to being the butt of the joke, but Rebecca glowered at her.

Yep, definite hatred there.

“How does it feel meeting the family?” Jeff asked. “Probably about as strange as it is for us.”
Rebecca elbowed him.

“What, Agatha has never brought anyone for dinner since…”

Agatha held her knife in a dagger stance. “Wanna finish that, Kaplan?”

Rio laughed at their antics. “It’s nice seeing you all. It’s like seeing a bit of her origins.”

“I’m not a superhero,” Agatha sassed.

“I was thinking more supervillain, but whatever.”

Agatha stabbed one of the meatballs with her knife.

“Has Agatha met any of your family?” Billy asked.

“She’s met all my family.”

“No I haven’t.”

“Yes, you have,” Rio insisted. “Alice, Lilia, and Webbers.”

“Who’s Webbers?” Billy piped up again.

“Her tarantula,” Agatha answered, and the boy’s eyes grew in awe.

“Have you held it?”

“She’s too chicken,” Rio answered. “She’s the cutest little thing, too.”

Agatha grimaced.

“That’s no surprise,” Rebecca spoke up. “She’s terrified of spiders.”

“I knew it!” Rio grinned.

“Thanks sis,” Agatha grumbled. “I’m never going to hear the end of this when we get back.”

“You’re never hearing the end of this ever!”

“So you have no other family?” Rebecca asked, and Rio shook her head.

“I’m grateful for what I have.” She reached out and toughed Agatha’s shoulder. “And now I’ve met this one, I have more than I could ever ask for.”

She felt Agatha stiffen for a moment under her touch, but she didn’t move away. Instead, she watched Agatha lift her own hand up, caressing her own delicately. Rio tried hard not to pull away as her touch tingled her hand.

Billy then decided that was the moment to ask if he could go see a concert in the city with his boyfriend, which caused his parents to argue and eventually suggested they take it to the kitchen. It seemed that the change of venue only made them louder.

“Why did you have to ask that then?” Agatha scolded her nephew, who glowered back at her.

“I thought they’d be cooler about it in front of a guest.”

Rio raised her eyebrows. “How bratty.”

“Don’t call him that,” Agatha huffed before glaring at Billy. “Brat.”

Billy bowed his head in shame. “They don’t let me do anything. I want to be able to do things for myself. Everyone else gets to do cool stuff.”

“You’re not 16 yet,” Agatha argued. “You might have to compromise with them on this.”

“I have to compromise everything. You know that.”

Agatha gave him a sympathetic smile. “I know, but it won’t be forever.”

Rio looked between them. There was a story behind this, she was sure what it was.

Billy then put on a smile for Rio. “Do you like music?”

“Doesn’t everyone?”

“Can I show you my record collection?”

Rio looked to Agatha, who nodded. “I would love to.”

Billy led them upstairs to his room. But it wasn’t a room. It was like walking into his mind. Not a surface was left without a trinket, not a wall left without a poster. Even his floor was covered in stuff, from the various shirts that had been thrown in every corner, to the guitar propped up against a set of draws.

“I keep my records here.” Billy pulled out a big metal case from the side of his bed. “I need better storage.”

“You need to clean,” Agatha criticised. “I don’t know whose room is worse, yours or Rio’s.”

“Messiness is a sign of greatness,” Billy sassed back. “Right Rio?”

Rio was only half listening. Instead, she stood in front of one of the many posters, staring up at a face that made her eyes sting with tears.

“You okay, hun?” Agatha asked, moving to stand next to her. If Rio didn’t know any better, she would say she was worried. Agatha Harkness was a great actress, after all.

“I’m fine,” she assured, not looking away from the poster.

“Do you like it?” Billy asked. “I got it at a yard sale. I screamed when I saw it.”

Rio tore her eyes away from the poster to look at him. “You like Lorna Wu?”

“Like?” Billy laughed. “I love her. Agatha bought me her album and I listened to it over and over for weeks. I’m guessing you’re a fan too?”

“Kind of,” Rio answered. “She was my step-mom.”

The room went quiet. She had managed to startle Agatha and chirpy mini me into silence, which she took as an achievement. It didn’t last long though; Billy found his voice quickly enough.

“Did you know this?” he asked Agatha, who shook her head.

“No, I…Wait so Alice is Lorna Wu’s daughter?”

“Yep.”

“How did I not know this?” Agatha questioned.

“You never asked,” Rio answered. “And it’s not something you really bring up. Like ‘hey, sexy lady, my step-mom was a rockstar and she died with my dad in a hotel fire’ doesn’t have a seductive ring to it.”

Agatha just stared at her.

“I’m sorry.” Billy moved forward and engulfed her in a hug. Rio awkwardly patted him on the back and forced a smile when he pulled away.

“It was a long time ago,” she assured. “And no one’s life is perfect.”

“I know.” Billy looked to Agatha, who had started picking up the clothes scattered on the floor.

“I’m going to go tell your parents that I’ll be on standby while you’re at this concert,” she announced. “I’ll be right back.”

Rio watched Agatha march out of the room with a ball of her nephew’s shirts clutched to her chest.

“She doesn’t do emotions very well,” Billy said once Agatha’s footsteps had faded. He sat down on the edge of the bed and Rio sat herself in his desk chair.

“Sorry for going heavy there, kid. I just didn’t expect to see her here.”

“I get it,” he assured. “And I’m glad you shared it with us.”

“You are?”

He nodded. “I think you two are good together.”

Rio raised her eyebrows. “Really?”

He nodded again. “You have more in common than you think.”

Rio frowned and was about to respond when Agatha’s voice summoned them from downstairs.

Billy stood and smiled down at her. “Come on. I think my mom made pie for dessert.

She gave Agatha a little wave before shutting the door and striding into the building. Agatha watched long after she had disappeared from view and leaned back in her seat.

This was the worst idea she’d ever had.

The Shopping Trip

Chapter Notes

hi! thank you all for the amazing comments! this chapter is a bit of filler but i hope you like it! i'll hopefully post chapter 10 later!

The address Agatha had sent her was a posh department store with a red carpet and a doorman. A doorman that was currently looking Rio up and down with suspicion as she loitered outside, her hand holding onto the strap of her college backpack.

“I’m waiting for someone,” she told him. “I’m early because she’s usually early.”

The doorman just continued to stare at her.

“Sorry, I got held up in a meeting.”

“It’s okay. I was early.”

Agatha checked her watch and frowned. “Yes, you are.”

Rio looked to the doorman again. “This is her.”

The doorman tipped his hat to Agatha. “Ms Harkness.”

“Norm,” Agatha acknowledged as he held the door open for her. “This is Rio, my partner.”

Rio raised her eyebrows. That was a new one.

She offered Norm a smile when he tipped his hat to her and followed Agatha inside.
The place was all marble and gold and shimmer. Even the air smelled fancy, but she knew Agatha would at her laugh if she said that. It was all too fancy; she didn’t like it at all.

For some reason, it was very distracting.

She didn’t know why she had even suggested this, though she didn’t know why she suggested taking her shopping either. She couldn’t stand Rio. Just looking at her face made her want to scream, but she couldn’t keep away. A glutton for punishment, she guessed.

She saw Rio peaking over at her. “What you reading?”

“A manuscript, you?”

“My latest report towards my thesis.”

“What’s it about?”

“This report or my thesis?”

“Either or?” Agatha answered. She was sure she wouldn’t understand it, but she was still curious.

“Well this report is about a study I recently took part in about azalea samples that recently put a woman in a coma, and my thesis is related to how easy plant-related toxins can be accidentally ingested.”

“Cheery stuff then?”

Rio shrugged. “What’s yours about?”

“It’s about a guy who wants to be a pianist but can’t because blah, blah, blah.”

Rio put her work down in her lap. “You’re not enjoying it?”

“I’ve been told I’m a harsh critic.”

Rio gasped dramatically. “ No , really?”

Agatha glared back. “You would be too if you had a whole team dedicated to bringing you the best work and all I get is this crap.”

Rio chewed on her pen again. “Are you good at checking grammar and stuff?”

“I was an editor in a past life,” Agatha answered. “Why?”

Rio picked up her report and threw it in the space between them. “Let’s swap.”

“What?”

“If you check that my writing isn’t totally shit, I’ll tell you if you’re being a harsh critic or not.”

“But I don’t know anything about plants,” Agatha argued.

“Oh the information is fine,” Rio said with confidence. “I just want to make sure it structurally makes sense.”

Agatah thought for a moment, Really, she shouldn’t be sharing submissions with anyone, but it wouldn’t be the full thing, and Rio wasn’t an industry spy. She was just a pain in her ass. So she threw it in the middle and they each grabbed their respective works.

Rio flipped through the pages. “Why are the corners all ripped?”

“Senõr Scratchy has a taste for paper.”

Rio laughed and found herself Agatha laughing with her.

They worked in comfortable silence, the only interruption being when Sharon told them it was time they ate some dinner. Agatha asked her to order some pizza and that she could head home. She needed to finish Rio’s report, and they had to wait for Phil to bring the laptop back anyway.

The report was interesting. Some parts went over her head, but she followed most of it. Rio wrote well overall. Some mistakes here and there, and some parts Agatha annotated with suggested structural changes, but it was actually a compelling read.

By the time she was done, they had devoured most of the pizza and Rio was on her second can of coke. She closed it and placed it between them.

“Good work.”

Rio looked up at her in surprise. “Really?”

Agatha nodded. “I left some comments, but it’s good work. What about you? What’s your thoughts?”

Rio closed the manuscript with a slap before handing it over. “You were right. It’s pretentious crap.”

“Thank you.” Agatha drew a dismissive line across the front cover. “That will be going in my reject pile. Probably one of the directors will push it for publishing though. Sometimes I swear I’m surrounded by idiots.”

“Am I one of your idiots?”

Annoyingly, Rio was too clever for her own good.

“You’re a pain in my ass.”

Rio stared at her, and Agatha had the overwhelming need to bite down on her lip. Admittedly, she had been a bit edgy since the changing room. That suit, or more what the suit didn’t cover, was engrained on her brain. God, she wanted to be repulsed by her, truly, but she just couldn’t be. It would be like looking at the stars and denying their glimmer.

Rio shifted closer to her. “Agatha.”

“Rio.”

“I…”

A knock at the door made them both jump, and they both looked to see Phil cautiously enter carrying two laptops. “All done.”

She watched Rio jumped up and took the laptops, her heartbeat racing.

Rio looked over the new laptop and grinned. “This is amazing! Thanks dude.”

“Yes, thank you Phil,” Agatha spoke up. “Please, head on home.”

Phil nodded and quickly retreated.

“This is so cool,” Rio grinned. “Honestly, Agatha, thank you.”

“It’s fine,” Agatha dismissed as she headed back over to her desk. “You best be heading on home now. I still have some work I need to get done here, but it’s getting late.”

“Right. Yeah. Okay.” Rio began gathering her things. “So will I see you tomorrow?”

“I’m quite busy,” Agatha replied. “I’ll talk to Jen about dinner, though.”

“Right.” Rio moved to stand in front of her desk. “Thanks again. Not just for the clothes and the laptop, but for letting me stay. I…”

“It’s fine,” Agatha insisted as she pretended to do work. “Let me know when you’re home.”

“I will.” Rio didn’t move though, just stayed routed to the spot. “So I guess I’ll see you soon?”

Agatha gave her a forced smile and a nod. She kept her head down after that, ignoring the disapproving click of Rio’s tongue, the retreating footsteps, the slight creek of the door.

It was only at the sound of the door slamming shut that Agatha gave up the charade. Letting out a heavy breath, she slumped in her chair.

Just over two weeks, she told herself. Two more weeks and Rio Vidal would be out of her life (and mind) for good.

Jen and Alice had questions, well Alice had questions while Jen demanded to know what she had done. In the end, she left them to their date and ate Lilia’s leftover lasagne before heading to bed.

Reaching to her nightstand, she checked her phone. A couple of ‘are you okay’ messages from Alice, but nothing more.

Opening her chat with Agatha, she typed out a message.

RIO

Can we talk?

She debated sending it, hoping Agatha would have calmed down and that their ridiculous little plan would be back on. But Agatha’s voice echoed in her mind. “We’re done.”

Rio didn’t want to be done. She pushed too far, she will admit that, but that wasn’t any reason for this to be over. For them to be over.

She turned onto her back and stared up at the ceiling. Why the fuck did she do that? Why did she have to wear that stupid dress and ruin it all? There would have been better ways to bring Agatha back after she pushed away. They’d still had about a week left of their deal. She would have gotten her admission, and maybe even an apology. Maybe that would have been enough for her to walk away. Closure for a year of turmoil. This wasn’t. This just made her chest feel hollow.

“She rises!” Lilia teased. “No classes today?”

“I’m not going,” Rio announced as she slumped onto the couch.

“Why not?” Lilia turned to look at her. “Are you ill?”

“No,” Rio answered. “I got dumped.”

“Agatha dumped you?”

Rio nodded. “Last night.”

Lilia tossed the spatula into the sink with a clang. “That bitch! How dare she do that to you again?!”

I was joking around and went too far.” She didn’t want to tell her older roommate they were a few choice words away from having hate sex in a public bathroom. “I mean, sure I may have pushed too far, but I thought that was our thing. I didn’t expect her to react like that.”

Rio folded her arms. “What do you mean ‘ah’?”

Lilia sighed. “Rio, don’t take this the wrong way but you have a tendency to…”

“What?”

“Antagonize.”

Rio stared back at her in disbelief. “When have I even antagonized anyone?”

Lilia laughed. “Oh, come on. For the first month we lived together, I thought I’d let a serial killer move in.”

“I wasn’t that bad.”

“You put ice down my back when I was cooking, you always jumped out at me if I came home after you, you even put your spider in my hair.”

“Tarantula,” Rio corrected.

“And Alice must have nerves of steal because whenever I see her, you’re playing some kind of trick.”

“Sisters do that,” Rio argued. “It’s normal.”

“Okay, what about the time that guy was trying to talk to her at that bar we went to, and you chased him around the place cackling like a witch?”

“Hey, he was making her uncomfortable and I had to step in,” Rio defended herself once again. “And I’d had a few glasses of wine.”

Lilia chuckled and shook her head. “The point is you were nervous about us living together, but even through your…uniqueness, I could tell you liked me enough, and I know you love Alice.”

“I do, but what does this have to do with Agatha?”

“Maybe the reason you’ve antagonized Agatha too much is because you really like her.”

“I don’t know about that,” Rio admitted.

“You’re dating her,” Lilia reminded her. “You wouldn’t be if you didn’t like her.”

If only Lilia knew the full story, Rio thought bitterly.

“I guess,” she shrugged. “We argue a lot, and sometimes she’s a total bitch. Then, sometimes, we just…we have these moments. We just click, and I don’t understand it. I hate her and I…”

Lilia raised her eyebrows. “You what?”

Rio shook her head. “Doesn’t matter.”

“Have you talked to her since last night?”

“Nope.”

Lilia picked up the plates of pancakes. “Call her, message her, or do whatever you kids do. Then come back here, eat your pancakes, and think about how you’re going to get her back.”

Rio eyed her suspiciously. “But you don’t even like Agatha.”

“I don’t,” Lilia agreed. “But for whatever reason, you do and that’s all that matters.”

Rio jumped up and headed back to her room. Picking up her phone, she looked at the message she had left unsent.

Taking a deep a deep breath, she pressed send.

Agatha had been waiting for the elevator when she got the message. She had a nine o’clock meeting with a literary agency across town and was about to spend an hour doing some catch up before her meeting with the execs.

She’d thought it was Billy when her watch buzzed, they’d been talking about his impending concert, so had opened it without thinking.

RIO

Can we talk?

Agatha sucked in a shaky breath. She hadn’t slept much the night before, plagued by images of deep brown eyes, a see-through dress, and a wicked smile.

She had no doubt she’d made the right decision. Whatever it was she and Rio were doing would have always ended badly, and this way she could just get on with trying to forget about her. Still, she could shake a lingering sadness when she thought of her.

The elevator doors open and she climbed aboard. Pressing the number for her floor, she waited until the doors were closed before looking at the message again.

She knew talking was healthy. The school therapist her dad made her see after she finally moved in with him had said it like a mantra. A lot of her youth had been spent hiding herself, and by extension her voice. Since then, Agatha had never shied away from making herself heard, especially to those who didn’t want to hear it.

Rio was different, though. Rio could stand toe to toe with her. Rio could trip her up without her noticing until it was too late. Rio could make her so vulnerable and take the opportunity to rip her heart. And most of all, Rio was a liar.

She also happened to be the one person Agatha had ever felt truly herself with, even if those moments had been fleeting.

No, she had made up her mind, and that was that.

AGATHA

No I meant what I said. We’re done with this.

Agatha made it to her office, dumped her bag by her desk and slumped in her chair. She opened her emails and saw a reminder about the upcoming company function and two attached tickets. She hated those things, but usually she took Jen and they would cause some trouble. This year, Jen would be too busy following Alice like a lovesick puppy. Maybe she could bring Rebecca, or take one of their top authors. That would look good, she guessed.

Her phone buzzed again.

RIO

Please just hear me out

Agatha jabbed back a reply.

AGATHA

I don’t want to hear it.

She put her phone down on her desk and returned back to her emails, only to soon find herself picking it up again.

Opening up Instagram, she searched up Rio’s profile and began scrolling through. Most of it was pictures of plants, all captioned with their Latin names and any other anecdotes she had. There were pictures of her tarantula, of course, and of Alice and Lilia. The photos Agatha stopped on were the ones of Rio, some of her pretending to be moody or scary, some goofy, and others the picture of radiance.

Agatha was beyond denying Rio was beautiful. How could she? If she was a painting, she’d replace the Mona Lisa. If she was a film star, she would be on every screen and magazine the world over. Instead, she was a pain in the ass PhD student who was brilliant and totally infuriating. And she just so happened to drop herself in the middle of Agatha’s life like a goddamn grenade.

She didn’t realise she had been staring so long until a knock on her office door made her jump.

“Come in,” she called.

The door opened and Sharon pocked her head in. “Your meeting is in 5, honey.”

“Yes, yes, thanks,” Agatha dismissed her with a wave. When Sharon shut the door, she stole one last look at her phone before putting it away and gathering her things.

The executives were two floors up, and she ended up stuck in the elevator with an intern that looked like was going to combust out of nerves. Agatha chose to ignore her and pushed by her when the doors opened.

Her watched buzzed with a text- this time from Rebecca.

REBECCA

Jeff wants to go out for dinner next Wednesday for his birthday- he wants you to invite Rio

Of course he did.

AGATHA

It’s a family meal. I can come alone.

REBECCA

It’s not just him who wants him there- your nephew is beside himself with excitement.

Dammit

AGATHA

I’ll ask her.

Great. Just great.

The conference room was already busy when she got there, filled with loud men and women who were trying to put their foot in. Agatha refused to associate with any of them and sat down in the far corner.

She checked her phone quickly as the executives began to file in, only to quickly regret it.

RIO

Just give me 10 minutes please

Agatha put her phone away. It wasn’t even midday, and she needed a drink.

“Before we start,” one of the execs, Mike, began. “I wanted to let you know about a recent acquisition we are in the process of negotiating.”

An impressed murmur rumbled around the room. Agatha rolled her eyes. What had they decided to do now?

“We’re delighted to announce that we are in talks with none other than Maximoff Productions.”

Fuck.

Rio lay on her bed, still in her Pyjamas and eating from a bag of skittles. She was scrolling through her socials, trying to distract herself, but it wasn’t working. Agatha hadn’t replied to her last text, and she had a sinking feeling that was that. Any more would be bordering on harassment, and she didn’t want to do that. If Agatha didn’t want to speak to her, she’d have to accept that was that.

She opened Instagram and saw Billy had posted. It was a selfie of him and his boyfriend with school lockers visible behind them. The caption read: so grateful for my teenage romance.

That boy needed to stop with the sickly-sweet captions, or she’d get a cavity. Still, she liked the post anyway and continued scrolling until a message popped up.

BILLY

hi rio

She froze. What should she do? Agatha wouldn’t want her talking to him, but she couldn’t leave the kid on read.

RIO

Aren’t you in school?

BILLY

yeh in history rn

RIO

Then get off your phone

BILLY

ok

Rio breathed a sigh of relief. That looked to be the end of that. She had moved to Pinterest and was in the middle of adding photos to her deadly nightshade board when she got another message.

“Damn it, kid,” she grumbled but opened it anyway.

BILLY

i just want to say that i can’t remember seeing my aunt as happy as she is rn. i know things are still new, but i hope you’ll come to the meal next week so we can get to know each other more.

She had many questions.

First off, what meal? Had Agatha neglected to tell her about it? Wasn’t the whole point of this to put on a show for her family? Or did she have other motivations Rio didn’t know about?

She tried not to think of the other part. Agatha was a good actor, and the kid just wanted to see her happy. (Maybe she wanted to see Agatha’s happy glow for herself too, even if she hated her lies.)

Then, she had an idea. Opening up the message, she typed back a reply.

RIO
Thanks kid see you when I see you

Right, she decided. Let’s do this.

“I just don’t understand,” Agatha argued as they walked away from the conference room. “Why do we need in-house illustrators.”

“They won’t be in-house,” Mike insisted. “Just under our umbrella.”

“Please, that’s the same thing.”

“Why are you so concerned?” He questioned. “It won’t affect your role at all.”

“I just think it’s a waste of time,” she lied.

“Well the rest of us disagree,” Mike stated. “It’ll be good. You’ll see.”

Agatha watched him head off to his office while she waited for the elevator. How could this even be happening?

She ran through her options in her mind: leave, hijack, or stay. All of which sounded equally as bad as each other. Maybe it was time to set up that indie publishing house she always wanted. even if the pay would be less, and more work, and maybe she’d need to get a smaller apartment.
Still, anything beat having to see Wanda Maximoff’s face every day.

She stepped into the elevator when it arrived and dared to check her phone. No messages from Billy, no messages from Rebecca, and more importantly, none from Rio. She should be relieved about that last one, but it just made her mood even worse.

Once she arrived at her floor, she stormed through the office, ignoring the ducking heads and the bodies diving out of her path. When she saw Sharon loitering by her office door, she groaned. Could her day get any worse?

“What now?”

“You have a visitor,” Sharon said with a smile that was somehow giddier than usual.

“Is it urgent?”

“I’d say so,” Sharon answered.

Agatha grumbled under her breath as she pushed the door open.  She walked into her office with her head held high. Whoever it was that had decided to visit her without an appointment had some nerve, but she was the picture of professionalism.…until she saw who was leaning against her desk.

Yes, her day could indeed get worse.

Rio smiled back at her, two coffees in hand. “Hi.”

The Subway

Chapter Notes

hi guys! i hope this chapter was worth the wait! i'm hoping to post the next chapter on wednesday but it's a chapter i've been desperate to write since i came up with the idea so i want it to be right! still i hope you enjoy this one!

Two things were apparent to Rio when Agatha walked in the door: First (and the most obvious), she was so hot in her work clothes. And second, she looked stressed as hell. Then, when she saw Rio, she was shocked. She stared back at her for a few moments, before her brow set in a frown.

“What are you doing here?”

“I brought coffee.” Rio held up the two iced coffees for emphasis. “I got you this because I didn’t know how long you would be and, well, this can’t get cold. You know, because it’s already cold.”

She mentally kicked herself. Why the hell was she rambling?

“I don’t want it,” Agatha said dismissively. “Give it to Sharon on your way out.”

“No, it’s not…” Rio sighed. “It doesn’t have to mean anything. You’ve bought me coffee twice, and lots of other stuff too which I wish I could pay you back for but it would likely take me like two years if I was lucky. So this is me making us the tiniest bit even. And it’s also an apology. You know, for…the bathroom thing.”

Agatha stared at her again before abandoning her bag on the floor and flopping onto the couch. Rio stayed by the desk, still clutching the coffee cups. What the hell just happened? Had she just broken Agatha Harkness?

She watched Agatha shift to sit up. “Are you actually going to sit down then?”

Rio walked across the room and sat at the other end of the couch. She handed Agatha one of the coffees and watched her bring the straw to her lips.

Agatah took a long sip and looked at it in surprise. “That’s actually not bad.”

“Are you okay?” Rio asked cautiously. “You seem a little…frazzled.”

Agatha laughed at that. “Only a little?”

“So you’re not okay?”

Agatha’s laugh died. “No Rio I am not in the slightest bit okay.”

“Because of me or…”

“Not totally but yes. You are one of the common denominators.”

Rio bowed her head. Though she expected it, hearing Agatha say it still stung. “I’m sorry. I was an ass, and I didn’t mean for any of it to go this far. Last night, or any of it. I was just so angry…”

Agatha closed her eyes. “I know. I was angry too. But last night was a step too far, Rio. You seriously crossed a line.”

“Well maybe it was a line that needed crossing?” Rio challenged.

Agatha looked away from her and sipped her coffee. It seemed that was not a conversation she was willing to have, so Rio tried something else.

“Your nephew messaged me on Instagram.”

Agatha’s head snapped up to look at her. “What did he say?”

Rio got out her phone and opened the app. Pulling up the chat, she handed the phone over for her to read. “Sorry, I felt bad leaving him on read.”

“I don’t think I’ve ever heard you say sorry so much,” Agatha commented as she squinted at the screen. “Your text is so small.”

“I can read it to you,” Rio offered, but Agatha just got up and headed across the room. She picked something up from her desk and walk back over.

Rio watched in awe as Agatha unfolded the item with the help of her teeth and pushed them onto her face.

“No comment,” Agatha warned her as she sat back down. “This is a recent development.”

“Fine, I’ll keep my thoughts to myself,” Rio promised. Though her comments would definitely be complementary. Agatha looked unbelievably sexy in glasses, especially thick rimmed glasses that sat so comfortably on her nose.  She admired this new look as Agatha read through the messages.

“Don’t tell him I told you. I feel bad about it already.”

Agatha frowned again. “Why would you feel bad about it?”

“Because it was private for him.”

“I won’t,” Agatha promised. “I have a list of problems as long as my arm and I don’t need this adding to it.”

Rio took a sip of her drink. “What are your other problems? Well, besides me.”

“I’m not telling you.”

“Hey, you said we were done. I’m a stranger to you now.”

Agatha raised her eyebrows, and Rio realised the ridiculousness of that.

“Okay, but still. I’m all ears.”

Agatha slouched in her seat and took another sip from her straw. “That meal Billy mentioned is for Jeff’s birthday and both he and Billy want you to come.”

“Okay…”

“And we’re done.”

“I’ll come to Jeff’s meal. I’m not an asshole.”

“It wouldn’t be a good idea.”

Rio laughed. “Like any of this has been a good one?”

Agatha looked down at her drink. “I don’t like lying.”

Rio wanted to point out the irony, but it wasn’t the right time to have that argument again. “It hasn’t all been a lie. We act the same around other people as we do when we’re together, just with a few pet names thrown in.”

“A lie is a lie no matter how you sugar-coat it,” Agatha argued.

“Well, we’ve both accused the other of being a liar,” Rio reminded her bluntly. “And everyone else doesn’t know, so what’s the problem? Have you grown a conscience or something?”

Agatha didn’t reply and took a sip from her coffee.

“So is that the problem? Look, cards on the table, I want to carry on. It’s been nice not having everyone think I’m some unlovable weirdo, and I know you’ve had as much fun antagonizing me as I do you.”

Agatha smiled weakly. “It has been a little bit, but that isn’t the point.”

“Then what is?”

Agatha leaned forward and put her cup on the coffee table, before putting her head in her hands. “I feel like my life is falling apart today. The aftermath of last night, this stupid meal, and…”

“And?” Rio prompted.

Agatha raised her head, her eyes fixing on the view outside the window. She stared at it for a while, and Rio was about to ask if she was okay when she finally spoke.

“I found out that my ex…best friend might be joining the company.”

Rio wasn’t stupid. She heard that pause, and it made her stomach twist into a knot. “On a scale of Billy to me, how much do you hate her?”

Agatha pursed her lips. “I don’t know. I kind of hate you both, but I can…Wanda is different.”

Rio clenched her jaw. She definitely hated this Wanda with every fibre of her being.

“An awesome job, a cool family, and an incredibly sexy fake girlfriend,” Rio finished for her. “And a kick-ass rabbit.”

“Why not?”

“Because it’s crazy.”

“Okay.”

“Ignoring it isn’t going to make it go away.”

“I know, but I think it would complicate things more than they need to be.”

Rio knew she was right, and that she shouldn’t want to revisit what would obviously be a bad idea, but taking it off the table entirely didn’t make her entirely happy. Even so, it was a price she was willing to pay to keep Agatha a little longer.

No, she definitely wasn’t thinking about it.

“Well, I’m going to text my sister, and I’m going to skim read my emails.”

“Can’t Sharon do that?”

Agatha shrugged. “I guess she could, but I don’t feel like reading crappy manuscripts right now, and all the talk in the office will be about the merger and I really don’t want to think about it.”

The merger. Wanda. Rio tucked that information away for later.

“Come play hooky with me.”

Agatha shook her head. “I can’t do that?”

“Why not?”

“I’m needed here.”

Agatha Harkness did not take the subway.

“Not since I stopped fetching people coffee,” Agatha clapped back. “It makes me claustrophobic.”

“Why would you be claustrophobic?”

“Because we’re under the fucking ground,” Agatha answered. “And we’re about to be squished into a tiny tin can with a load of total strangers. And I’m pretty sure I just saw a rat.”

She hated the damn subway.

“It’s fine,” Rio assured. “I got you.”

“You’re going to stop the roof caving in and crushing us to death?”

“When has that every happened?”

“First time for everything.” Agatha looked up at the ceiling with uncertainty. All that weight above and they were stuck in a void below. It was simple physics to her.

The train arrived quicker than she expected, and she followed Rio aboard, who pushed through and secured them too seats. Agatha tried to keep herself calm, but as the doors slid shut, and the train began to hurtle forward, she began to feel the telltale symptoms of panic.

She tried all the techniques she had learnt: close your eyes, steady your breaths, tell yourself it’ll be okay, and picture your happy place.

Agatha’s first happy place had been her grandmother’s house, then her dad’s. Then as she got older, her happy place stopped being an actual place, but a person. It had been her grandmother, Rebecca, her first girlfriend, her college roommate (who became her second girlfriend), her dad. Then, from the moment he had been born, it had been Billy.

She pictured him, his curly hair, his wide smile, his moonstone eyes, the scar through his left eyebrow…

The train jolted and her mind reared left.

The sound of beeping monitors filled her ears, the sound of Rebecca’s sobs as Jeff tried to comfort her through his own tears, the rhythmic sound of the machine that was making the chest of Billy’s lifeless body rise and fall. His eyes closed, skin pale, a bandage above his eye, a tube in his mouth as wires and IVs spread from his body like tree roots. And there was nothing she could do, nothing she could say. Her nephew, the light of her life, slipping away…

Something touched her hand, and suddenly Agatha was back on the train.

“Hey.” Rio laced their fingers together and squeezed. “You’re okay. You’re going to be okay.”

Agatha squeezed back and sucked in a deep breath. “Can we get off at the next stop?”

“Yeah, we can get a cab,” Rio promised. “I’m sorry.”

Rio helped her up and guided her off the train, never letting go of her hand. In any other circumstances, Agatha would have yanked her hand away. She’d barely put up with the handholding for appearances sake. It was unnecessary and impractical. Yet as Rio led back up to the world above, it was the one thing that kept Agatha grounded.

When they made it back out into the open air, Agatha pulled her hand away and shoved it into her coat pocket as Rio got them a cab. She watched as Rio spoke to the driver, before opening the back door for her.

“M’lady.”

Agatha shook her head, trying hard not to smile as she climbed in.

“This way.” Rio walked a step ahead of her, and Agatha followed her down the street. Rio led her through the park. It was a decent enough day, not particularly hot but sunny enough. No point in making a show for no one.

“Ta dah!” Rio held up her arms to frame the glass structure before them. “Welcome to the botanical gardens.”

“Yeah, my mom used to read it to me,” Rio answered, her voice suddenly heavy. “Not Lorna, but my actual mom.”

I spent most of my time at elementary school behind everyone else, so I tried to read as much as I could to catch up. I didn’t get to read the Secret Garden until I was in middle school.”
