I couldn’t believe somewhere could be so beautiful. We say so many beautiful gardens all around the world, but that was just magical.”

“Is that when you became interested in plants?” Agatha asked. “

“No, that happened before,” Rio answered. “One of my other favourite gardens is the poison garden at Alnwick Castle. It’s right on the boarder between Scotland and England. Alice and I went on a trip there one summer. She wanted to see the Harry Potter stuff and I went for the plants.”

“What? So it’s like a garden full of plants that could kill you?”

“Yeah, there’s a huge list of warnings before you go in. It’s so cool.”

Agatha had to admit, that did sound interesting. She watched Rio reach down and touch one of the roses.

“They’re coming out bloom,” she commented. “Still beautiful though.”

Agatha shrugged. “Perfection is overrated.”

She leaned down to sniff the flower.

“Stay there,” Rio told her, and Agatha panicked.

“Is it poisonous?”

“No, silly.” Rio pulled out her phone. “It’s a photo-worthy moment.”

Agatha instinct was to be difficult for the sake of it, but she had to admit she was having a good time, and a photographic reminder wouldn’t be too bad. So she moved back towards the flower, savoured it’s scent, before looking up at Rio with a smile.

“That any good?”

“A work of art,” Rio said with a grin.

“Okay, now I need one of you to be fair,” Agatha argued. “Pick a rose.”

“Or we could take a selfie?” Rio suggested. “We don’t have one picture together.”

“We don’t?” Agatha frowned.

Rio shook her head.

“Okay then.” She pulled out her phone and set up the front camera. Rio leaned against her, their cheeks pressing together, and Agatha tried her best to calm the jolt in her heart enough so she could get the right angle.

“Perfect.” She said after a couple of photos.

“I thought perfection was overrated?” Rio teased, and Agatha playfully swatted her arm.

They walked round, took photos and chatted, mostly about plants, but also their interests. It turned out Rio was quite the basketball player, and maybe would have gone professional if she hadn’t spent her childhood on a tour bus, followed by a bad ACL injury in college that put the nail in the coffin. Agatha told her how she’d gone to college with the plan study law but ended up being an English major minoring in performing arts. Rio wanted to see videos of her performances, and Agatha assured her that would never ever be happening.

They were about to head for a coffee when Sharon called. Mike had requested she deal with a situation that had the children’s fiction department at loggerheads, which in translation meant he wanted her to go scare the life out of them and make the final decision of what to do.

And so, they left the gardens, and Rio helped her wave down a cab.

“Do you want to come with?” Agatha asked, but Rio shook her head.

“I’m going to stay and talk to some people I know who work here,” she said. “I saw a few of them watching us, so I might as well get the twenty questions over with.”

“Oh yeah?” Agatha said with a teasing smile. “And what are you going to say?”

“What do you want me to say?” Rio threw back.

“No point in not sticking to our usual story, is there?”

Rio grinned. “My thoughts exactly.”

“Right well, I’ll talk to you later?” Agatah asked, trying not to sound too hopeful.

“Oh you can count on it.” Rio then began to step back towards the garden’s entrance. “See you soon.”

“See you soon,” Agatha repeated, trying hard not to giggle when Rio winked at her, and tried to push down her sadness as she watched her walk away.

Back at the office, the argument happened to be whether to request a plot change in the latest book of their most successful middle-grade series. After some discussion, Agatha said she would look at the data and told them to focus on the upcoming launch of their latest release in the meantime.

She walked out with Sharon around five and dropped her off at the station before driving home. She cooked some pasta and ate it alone as always (technically not though as Senõr Scratchy was also enjoying his nightly feed with an extra leaf of lettuce) and switched on the news, only to quickly tune in to a quiz show instead.

When she’d finished eating, she settled herself on the couch with a book from an author how’d ended their contract with their former publisher. Mike was eager to speak with their agent, but Agatha wasn’t convinced. Senõr Scratchy was also craving attention, so she had him on his mat on the floor, her free hand calmly stroking his fur.

One hour, eight chapters, a re-caged rabbit, and a glass of wine later, she received an Instagram notification.

@poisonhag has tagged you in a post.

Agatha frowned and opened up the post.

There were three pictures, all of her. One of her smelling the rose, another from when she looked up to Rio, and another of her laughing as they walked through the conservatory. She had to admit, she did look good. And happy, despite the day’s events. What really made her smile though was the caption.

The most beautiful flower in the garden (the rose is okay too I guess)

Agatha liked the post and was about to comment when she had a better idea.

She hadn’t posted anything since Billy set up her account, but she pretty much knew what to do. She chose one of the selfies they’d taken and a few most of the gardens and of Rio standing by sculptures. Satisfied with her selection, she wrote a quick caption:

The perfect date with my crazy flower girl

She smiled to herself and tagged Rio before posting it.

Billy liked it first, within seconds, and commented soon after.

@billlykaplann: you two are so cute!

Alice and Jen liked it soon after, and a few others: some work colleagues and old school friends that had found and followed her. Even Sharon commented a little heart in the comments, but none of that mattered. There was one person she was waiting on, and they were taking sweet time to check their phone.

Agatha tried to return to her book, but she was too impatient to concentrate. She felt like a teenage girl waiting for her crush to call, which was definitely not what this was. Not at all.

Then, finally , two notifications popped up.

@poisonhag liked your post

@poisonhag commented: Anything for you, my love

Agatha grinned and liked the comment. My love. That was a new one.

She was about to reach for her book again when she had an incoming call. Seeing who it was, she bit down on her lip as her thumb eagerly answered.

“Hey.”

“Hey,” Rio repeated. “Can you send me the selfie. Like the non-cropped version.”

“Sure.” Agatha put her on speaker phone before manoeuvring through her phone to send the image. “There. It should come through soon.”

“Thanks,” Rio answered . “I’m setting it as my lock screen. Is that okay?”

“Yeah, sure, if you want.”

“At the minute it’s just a photo of some plants so, you know, I thought it would be good for appearances. You can get away with it, because yours is Billy, but…”

“Rio, you can set your lock screen as whatever you want. And how do you know mine has Billy on it?”

“I’ve seen it.”

“When?”

Rio ignored her. “Did you have fun today?”

“Considering we fake broke up, I found out Wanda is probably going to be working with me, and I had a panic attack on the subway, I actually had a great time.”

“Yeah, it’s a great place, and the company wasn’t half bad either,” Rio teased, before her vice became more serious. “Did you get your work emergency sorted?”

“Yeah, but it wasn’t an emergency, but I’ve ended up in charge of a decision I’m not too happy about making.”

“What kind of decision?”

Agatha took off her glasses and put them on her coffee table. With a tap, she took Rio off speaker and brought her phone back to her ear.

“We have this bestselling book about some middle schoolers who find this secret world. It’s getting turned into a movie, and it’s one of our flagship series. Well, the author submitted their draft for the latest book and they’ve had the main character fall in love with her best friend, who is also a girl.”

“Aw baby gays. That’s adorable.”

“Yeah, well everyone is fine with it, but they’re worried it’ll affect how the book sells, and whether the series gets blacklisted by schools and libraries. I think Mike sent me down to make the decision because I’m the token lesbian, but I don’t know what to do. This could cause a lot of backlash and we could lose money, but I don’t know if I can deny some kid the experience of seeing themselves in a book for the first time. If that had been me at twelve, I…”

Agatha stopped. She wasn’t even going to go there.

“I get it,” Rio answered. “ Have you read the other books in the series?”

“Yeah, I was an editor on the first two.”

“So ask for a copy of the manuscript and give it a read. You can’t make a decision on something you haven’t actually read.”

“That’s true.” Agatha thought for a moment. “Then I can justify my decision too.”

“Exactly.”

“Thanks Rio.”

“Hey, I’m not just a pretty face.”

Agatha smiled to herself. It was a very pretty face though.

“Hey Agatha?”

“Yeah?”

She heard Rio moving around on the other end of the call. “You know early when we agreed we wouldn’t, you know…”

Agatha should have known this was coming. “Rio…”

“No, I’m not arguing it,” Rio insisted. “I was just wondering if you wanted to, maybe, go on a fake date with me?

“A fake date?” She tried not to sound too surprised.

“Yeah, just dinner or something. You know, to make things more believable.”

Agatha smiled at that. “Well, we definitely need to be believable.”

“Most definitely,” Rio teased. “How about tomorrow?”

Agatha’s heart slumped. “I can’t tomorrow. Billy has his concert, and I promised I’d be available just in case.”

“Oh yeah, of course.”

She could tell Rio was disappointed, and she was a little bit too. “Why don’t you come over? We could order some food and chat.”

There was a long pause.

“Or we could do it another night?” Agatha backtracked. “We could go…”

“No, tomorrow at your place sounds good,” Rio insisted. “What time do you want me?”

Anytime. All the time. She quickly put those thoughts in line. “Say seven-ish? Do you remember…”

“Yeah, I do,” Rio answered quickly. “So I’ll see you then. I’ll bring dessert.”

“You don’t…”

“Agatha, please let me spend money for once.”

“Okay, okay. So, seven?”

“Seven,” Rio confirmed. “See you tomorrow.”

“See you tomorrow.”

“Bye.”

“Bye.”

“Bye.”

“Bye.”

“….Agatha hang up the phone.”

“Why don’t you?”

Rio grumbled. “Fine, but next time you are.”

The call ended and Agatha bit back a grin. It hadn’t been a totally bad day in the end. Not at all.

The Fake Date

Chapter Notes

hi! thanks for all the comments! they really make me smile! this was meant to be half a chapter but got out of hand, so here we are!

Her apartment was spotless, her kitchen was stocked with drinks and snacks, and she had changed into her best figure-hugging black pants and a low-neck blouse. Still, Agatha was panicking

She didn’t know why. It was just Rio, and they were only getting take-out. And it wasn’t like Rio had never been there before, though last time they had ended up in bed together having straddled, kissed and caressed. That wouldn’t be happening again, but the memory of what almost happened weighed heavily in the air.

Rio pressed the buzzer at five to seven. With a smirk, Agatha spoke through the intercom app on her phone: “Hello?”

“ Let me up, m’lady. I have dessert!”

Agatha chuckled and pressed the button to let her in. She paced the living room, wondering how long it usually took to get up there in the elevator. What if she forgot what floor she was on and got lost? Or if she couldn’t remember which was her apartment. She was sure the republican lobbyist on the floor above would love a chaotic lesbian knocking on his door asking for her. The thought made her smirk, but it worried her, nonetheless.

Soon enough, there was a knock. It turns out, Rio remembered exactly where she lived.

Agatha sucked in a deep breath as she walked over to the door and opened it with a welcoming smile.

Rio stood there, dressed in an oversized grey button up and jeans. It was a simple look, but the way she smiled made Agatha’s heart so jumpy that she had to grip the door frame as not to embarrass herself. Rio’s hands were behind her back, and she titled her head, a cheeky gleam in her eyes.

“Did you know, most cakes are round because in ancient cultures they represent the sun and moon?” Rio brought a small carboard cakebox out from behind her back. “This one is square though.”

Agatha chuckled and stepped aside to let her in, shutting the door behind her. She watched Rio look around the apartment with familiarity as she moved to put the cake box in the kitchen. No sooner had the box touched the counter top did Rio make a swift b-line across the room.

“Well haven’t you got big!” She leaned in so she and Senõr Scratchy were practically nose to nose through the bars of the cage. “How is the bestest rabbit in all the world?”

Agatha walked over and picked Senõr Scratchy out of his cage. “You remember Rio, don’t you?”

She handed him into Rio’s waiting arms, and he was quickly nestled into a hug.

“He does remember me!” Rio grinned. “He’s such a good boy.”

“Of course he is.” Agatha leaned in to kiss his head. “He’s my little ball of peanut butter, aren’t you my sweet boy.”

She could feel Rio staring at her and placed one last kiss to his head before standing up straight.

“What?” she asked when she met her gaze.

“Nothing,” Rio said softly, and it was then Agatha became aware of how close they were now stood. How instinctively she had moved into Rio’s space without even realising. Like it was natural.

Clearing her throat, she stepped back. “What do you fancy for dinner?”

“Whatever you want,” Rio answered.

Agatha thought for a moment. “Pizza?”

“Perfect,” Rio grinned as she rocked Senõr Scratchy in her arms. “Can we get a plain cheese?”

“As long as we can also get a pepperoni?”

“Deal.”

Agatha ordered the food, then walked back over to Rio, who carefully handed over the rabbit.

“He’s cuter than I remember.”

“Yeah, that’s why he gets away with nibbling the corner of every book I read.”

“Wow, you’re lucky,” Rio told the rabbit in Agatha’s arms. “These book nerds are very fussy about their untarnished corners.”

“I’m not a nerd,” Agatha huffed, making Rio laugh.

“Okay, and I’m not a crazy flower girl.”

Agatha hid her smile from Rio echoing her Instagram caption by kissing Senõr Scratchy’s head again. She put him back in the cage.

“So what do you want to do until the food gets here?” Agatha asked. “We could watch a movie or something?”

“Movie sounds good,” Rio answered. “A horror?”

Agatha smiled. “Most definitely.”

After some debate (because of course there would be), they settled on watching Smile . Rio of course found it hilarious, which in turn made Agatha laugh.

They both jumped when the pizza arrived.

Rio paused the movie while Agatha went to answer the door, returning wit two pizza boxes.

“I wish you’d let me pay for something.”

“You paid for dessert,” Agatha reminded her, and Rio pouted but didn’t argue.

Agatha put the boxes down on the coffee table and walked to the kitchen. “What do you want to drink?”

“Are we eating here?”

Agatha looked back at Rio, who stood awkwardly by the couch. “What, do you want us to go eat it on the street?”

“No, I mean on the couch,” Rio explained. “Shouldn’t we eat at the table?”

“We need to finish the film,” Agatha dismissed as she opened the fridge. “Now what do you want to drink?”

No reply.

Agatha looked round again and when she saw her still stood there.

“What’s wrong?”

“So, you know how I love tormenting you?”

“I may slightly recall that, yeah?”

“Well property distinction isn’t my vibe,” Rio looked at the couch, “and I know the moment I start eating on that couch, I’m going to drop something on it and it looks super expensive.”

“It’s fine. I let Senõr Scratchy on it all the time.”

Rio didn’t move and Agatha sighed in defeat. “Pick yourself something to drink and grab me a coke.”

She walked into the bedroom and grabbed one of her blankets. Carrying it back through to the living area, she threw it over the couch, covering the majority of it.

“There. Better?”

Rio nodded and settled down, placing the two coke cans on the table. The moment Agatha opened the pizza, Rio jumped in and devoured a slice before she even had chance to turn the movie back on. They ate their fill between jumping and laughing.

After she’d had enough pizza, Agatha noticed Rio pull the blanket up at her side to wrap around herself. It wasn’t a particularly cold night, but Rio looked so snug wrapped up that she had to do the same.

“Copycat,” Rio teased, before shuffling closer so their side’s touched. Between the blanket and the warmth radiating from Rio’s body to hers, Agatha couldn’t remember ever feeling so cosy.

When the credits rolled, Agatha switched off the film, but didn’t move away.  “What did you think?”

“Good,” Rio answered. “Not great, but it was fun.”

“I agree.”

They sat in silence for a few moments, and the previous cosiness began to feel rather stiff.

“So,” Rio piped up, “what do you want to do now?”

“Do you want a glass of wine?” Agatha asked, “or some whisky?”

“Are you having any?”

“No, but you can if you want.”

“Nah, I’ll just have what you’re having.”

“A coffee?”

“Sure.”

Agatha reluctantly pulled herself off the couch and went to turn on her coffee maker. As she prepared their drinks, she kept stealing glances back at Rio, who was leaning over the arm of the couch, grinning at Senõr Scratchy. The sight made her smile.

“You can feed him if you want?”

Rio looked to her hopefully. “Can I?”

Agatha pointed at the cupboard below his cage. “His feed is in there. Give him a couple of cups full.”

Rio quickly got up and knelt down in front of the cage. Agatha supervised as Rio scooped up some food and carefully poured it into Senõr Scratchy’s food bowl, who quickly moved to tuck in. She repeated the process again before shutting the cage and the cupboard so she could stand back and enjoy her handywork.

“You’re good with animals,” Agatha commented as she finished up the coffees.

“Yeah, my mom always said I had a green thumb. I guess animals come under that too.”

Agatha wondered which mom she was talking about.

Rio moved to sit back down as Agatha carried the coffees over. She held the mug out to Rio.

“Here you go.”

“Thank you, my love,” Rio teased with a wink, and Agatha tried desperately not to blush.  She sat down on the couch, leaning her back in the corner of the couch so she could face Rio fully.

“How’s Alice?”

“She’s fine. She called me not long after we talked last night. She said we’re ‘adorable’”

Agatha grimaced. “I’m not, nor ever will be, adorable.”

Rio laughed. “Please, I have photographic evidence.”

“No you don’t.”

Rio pulled out her phone. “Okay so there’s this one of you pointing at the lilly pads…”

Agatha went to grab her phone, but Rio was quick to dodge her. She hid her phone behind her back and held her finger up to stop her. “Stealing is a crime.”

“I can afford a good lawyer,” Agatha sassed back.

Rio took a sip of her coffee. “Try get it then.”

Agatha put her coffee on the table and slowly crawled across the couch until she and Rio were face to face. “Is that a challenge?”

Rio’s gaze darted all over her face, and Agatha tried to ignore the way it loitered a beat longer on her lips. Eventually, their eyes met, and Rio smirked.

“What if it was?”

Agatha smiled deviously, confident enough that Rio was adequately distracted. She cautiously snuck her hand behind Rio, before quickly snatching up the phone.

“Hey!” Rio went to grab it back, but Agatha jumped up out of her reach. “It’s got Face ID so you aren’t getting in.”

“Like that’s ever stopped me,” Agatha shot back, only for her smile to fade when she saw the lockscreen.

She knew it would be her and Rio. She even knew what picture it was. Still, there was something about seeing it. Seeing them smiling back at her like it was the most normal thing in the world. It made them look almost…real?

Out of the corner of her eye, she saw Rio put her mug on the coffee table. “You okay?”

“Yeah,” Agatha quickly insisted as she handed back the phone. “I like the lock screen.”

She could feel Rio watching her sit down, but she chose to ignore it. Instead, she reached for her coffee and looked out the window.

“It’s dark out there. Billy will be getting out of his concert about now.”

“Have you heard anything?”

“He let me know when he got to the venue, and Eddie is giving him a ride home.”

“Is Eddie his boyfriend.”

“It is,” Agatha confirmed.

“I have to admit, I stalked his profile a little. The post he put on about you being the first one he came out to was beautiful.”

Agatha nodded. She had to admit, she had scrolled through her nephew’s profile when she first got the app, and if the number of posts with her wasn’t heartwarming enough, the photo from his parents anniversary party and the caption underneath almost brought her to tears.

Almost.

Agatha Harkness wasn’t a crier (except when it counted).

“I knew for a while though,” Agatha admitted. “His parents were oblivious, but I could tell. I could see he had the same…” She wasn’t sure how to describe it. The inner turmoil, the feeling like you were being pulled in every direction, the excitement and the fear. She knew the fear the most pf all. “I waited for him to be ready, though.”

“Has he been out long?” Rio asked, and Agatha couldn’t help but laugh. Rio looked at her in confusion.

“He told me a year ago,” Agatha answered.

“Okay…”

Agatha stared at her until the penny dropped.

“Oh.”

“Yeah.”

“So…”

“Yep.”

Rio reached for her coffee and took a large gulp. “Right. Okay.”

“Shall we move on?” Agatha suggested, taking a sip from her own mug.

“Good idea,” Rio agreed. “So what’s the deal with this Wanda chick?”

“You did not just say ‘chick’.”

“What do you want me to call her?”

“Anything but chick.”

Rio frowned in clear annoyance. “Stop deflecting and give me the tea.”

“I already gave you coffee.”

“ Agatha. ”

“Fine. Fine.” Agatha shifted on the couch, tucking her legs underneath her. “We were friends, then we were more, and now we are neither.”

“Interesting.” Rio tilted her head. “Tell me more.”

Agatha sighed. “We met through work. We became best friends. She got married. Her brother died and she…I’m not proud of it.”

Rio stared at her for a moment before bursting out laughing. “Wait, you were the mistress?”

“No, I was not,” Agatah huffed. “They had a trial separation, and she was lonely. We went out one night so she could let her hair down and we…”

“Ended up fucking each other’s brains out.”

Agatha grimaced. “Okay, okay. Anyway, we started just casually…”

“Fucking.”

“Having sex,” Agatha corrected. “Then we started dating. She pretty much lived at my old apartment. Her house with her husband is not far from Rebecca’s, and her office was in the city, so she started staying over because it was easier. She told me he had gone back to England. He’s English but moved over here for college. Anyway, she said she was going on a business trip. She came back a week later telling me they were back together. Three months later, she announced she was pregnant with twins.”

“Fuck,” Rio cursed. “That must have hurt.”

Agatha shrugged. “Worse things have happened.”

“Come on, that must have been one of the worst days ever. Like if you had to pick a top five…”

“A top five worst days? That’s morbid.”

“Hey, I can tell you mine if you tell me yours.”

Agatha shook her head. “I’d have to think about it.”

“I’ll hold you to that.”

“I’m sure you will.”

The truth was, Agatha knew what the five would be straight away, and Wanda leaving her was nowhere close.

“So what is Wanda doing now? Besides invading your workplace?”

“I blocked her on everything, and Jen cut her off too. Rebecca told me she heard the twins were boys, and she bumped into Wanda not long ago. Her and her husband have split up for real this time.”

Agatha noticed Rio’s jaw tighten. “Are you interested?”

“Not in the slightest,” she insisted. “Actually, the whole reason…” She quickly stopped herself. “Never mind.”

“No, tell me!” Rio pleaded.

Agatha considered it for a minute, before deciding she couldn’t lie about it. “Wanda wanted to pass on her new number when Rebecca saw her, and Rebecca wanted me to give her another chance.”

“Huh.” Rio clicked her tongue. “So Rebecca is Team Wanda?”

“No, she just thinks I’m lonely.”

“Are you?”

“How can I be?” Agatha sassed. “Fake dating takes up most of my free time these days.”

That made Rio laugh. “Is that why you said we were dating? Because of Wanda?”

“No, it was because Billy started arguing with his mum saying we were dating, and I just went with it.”

“Because he saw the group chat.” Rio clicked her fingers. “I remember now.”

“And now Wanda has wiggled her way back into my work life, so I’m just as fucked.”

“I love it when you swear.” Rio shuffled closer to her. “And must I remind you that you have an awesome fake girlfriend, so she can fester in the knowledge she let a good thing go.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “You think I’m a good thing?”

“Hey, before things got messed up the first time, I thought you were my dream girl.”

It took Agatha a minute to fully compute what Rio had just said. “Really?”

She nodded. “Then I thought better of it.”

“Oh you did, did you?”

Rio nodded again. “But I can still see why you’re a catch for someone else.”

“I’d say back at you, but only a special person would put up with your nonsense.”

Rio cackled. “You put up with me.”

“Barely.” Agatha quickly checked her watch. “It’s getting late. Do you want me to give you a lift home?”

“Is that you telling me to go?”

“No, no. Just whenever your ready I’ll drive you home.”

“I can get a taxi,” Rio assured. “The kid will be on his way back to the burbs by now. Have a glass of wine with me.”

“Nah.”

“You’re going to wait up until he texts you he’s home, aren’t you.”

“Pretty much.”

“You really are aunt of the year,” Rio teased, at which Agatha nodded. She took great pride in it, in fact.

“Well,” Rio set her now empty mug aside and shuffled so they were once again sat side by side, “I want to share one glass of wine with you tonight, so I guess I’m waiting too.”

“Rio…”

“Come on. It’s Friday, and I’m not having your fifteen-year-old nephew stay out later than me.”

“Okay, fine,” Agatha gave in. It didn’t take much persuading. “What shall we do in the meantime?”

“I don’t know.” Rio’s voice was quiet now, and Agatha was suddenly aware of how close they were. “You tell me?”

Agatha searched her face, and she felt Rio’s search hers. The air between them was heavy. No, magnetic. The pull was too much to fight even if she wanted to. And she wasn’t sure if she did.

Her heart beat fast, her body tingled with anticipation, her eyes couldn’t tear themselves away from Rio’s soft, welcoming lips.

Screw it.

She leaned in, and she saw Rio do the same. Her eyes fluttered closed the moment she left Rio’s breath on her lips. Closer, closer…

BANG, BANG, BANG.

They both jumped apart and look to the door.

“Agatha!”

She was up on her feet in and rushed across the room to yank the door open.

There was her nephew, with a cracked phone in his hand, and his face a mess of tears and eyeliner.

“Billy, what happened?”

He threw himself into her arms. “Eddie and I got into a fight and I threw my phone across the bathroom and he left me there and I didn’t know what to do and I can’t use my phone and I know mom and dad will never let me out the house again and I think me and Eddie are over and I didn’t know what to do and mom gave me the fob for your building…”

“Okay, okay.” Agatha pulled him into a hug, rocking him like she did when he was a small child. He clung to her, crying into her shoulder. “I’ll call your mom and I’ll see what she wants us to do, okay?”

He nodded and pulled away from her, wiping his cheeks with his sleeve. His gaze then travelled beyond Agatha, and he managed a small wave.

“Hi Rio.”

“Hey kid.” Rio patted the spot Agatha had just left. “Come sit with me while your aunt calls your mom.”

Billy nodded and moved to sit down next to her. Agatha gave Rio a thankful look before scooping up her phone and rushing into her bedroom.

Aunt of the year? She deserved aunt of the century at this point.

The Fake Date (Part 2)

Chapter Notes

hi! thanks again for all the comments! i tried to get this chapter done quick but its ended super long so apologies. hope you enjoy!

tw: mentions of childhood trauma, bereavement and homophobia.

Rio sat awkwardly on the couch. She could hear Agatha’s voice coming from her bedroom, and from the sounds of it she was trying and failing to calm her sister.

Billy slumped beside her, sniffling and wiping away at his eyes. His eyeliner was everywhere, making him look like he was cosplaying The Crow. Though he had totally tongue-blocked her and Agatha (because really?!), she couldn’t be mad at the kid. She knew all too well heartbreak sucked.

“My first girlfriend dumped me in McDonalds,” Rio told him. “My mom was doing a two-month residency in Vegas, and we rented a house in the suburbs. I met this girl, and I thought she was some kind of angel. We dated two weeks, then she told me she’d cheated on me with a girl at her school because ‘I’d be gone soon so what was the point in committing?’”.

Billy looked at her in surprise. “What did you do?”

“I threw my milkshake at her.”

“No way!

“Yeah, I think if it happened today there’d a TMZ headline like ‘rockstar’s step-daughter causes havoc in McMilkshake frenzy!’”

That got a laugh out of him. “I forgot you’re kind of famous.”

“Alice is,” she clarified. “I’ll be just a footnote in a biography.”

“You could have been a total nepo-baby if you wanted to though.”

Rio shrugged. “Once me and Alice thought about starting a band. She’s good with keys and I used to drum.”

“Shit,” Agatha cursed. “What happened?”

“She used to like making homemade teas from flower petals. She drank the wrong one. My dad found her when she didn’t pick me up after his weekend. She’d been there a while.”

“These are my favourite,” he told her, and she smiled.

“Mine too.”

“That’s good seeing he gave you no choice,” Agatha commented from cross the kitchen, and Billy bowed his head sheepishly.

“Thanks,” Rio said as she took it.

“You’re welcome, my love.” Agatha kissed the top of her head and sat down beside her.

“You survived a night in the Kaplan house,” Agatha commented. “Well done you.”

“I like them,” Rio admitted. “I’m looking forward to the birthday meal.”

“Well, she definitely likes Wanda now.” Rio hated saying the woman’s name, especially after what Agatha told her the night before.

“She just thought Wanda would be good for me,” Agatha explained. “Rebecca thinks that the route to my happiness will be a picket fence and a load of kids running around, and Wanda has that built-in now.”

“Don’t you want kids?” Rio asked curiously.

“Of course I do, but it just hasn’t happened for me.”

“It still might?”

Agatha shook her head. “I think that window has gone for me, and I wouldn’t want to do it alone.”

“We could have one,” Rio suggested.

Agatha laughed. “What, are we going to get fake married now?”

“No, but we could co-parent? We do make a good team, you have to admit.”

Rio nodded in agreement. “So are you going to buy Billy a new phone?”

“I’m stopping by the Apple Store after I’ve dropped you off.”

“Fucking knew it.” Rio laughed, and Agatha joined in with her.

Soon enough they reached the city, and it wasn’t long before Agatha was pulling up outside Rio’s building.

“Here you are.”

“Thanks.” Rio looked in the back. “Where’s my shirt?”

“I’ll get it dry cleaned and bring it over,” Agatha replied. “Unless you need it soon?”

“No, no, that’s fine. So, I guess I’ll see you Tuesday?”

Agatha nodded. “Enjoy the rest of your weekend and thank you. For helping Billy and helping me.”

“Anytime,” Rio said with a grin. She stared back at Agatha. The morning sun was illuminating half her face in a golden glow, soft and warm against her cheek. She looked so pretty that Rio couldn’t resist.

She unclipped her seatbelt and shot forward, placing a quick kiss against Agatha’s sun-kissed cheek. She watched the other woman blink at her in surprise, and Rio grinned.

Yep, this time she had definitely broken Agatha Harkness.

She pushed open the car door and jumped out. “See you Tuesday.”

Agatha swallowed and nodded. “S-see you Tuesday.”

Rio shut the car door and with one last wave through the window, she headed into her building with a skip in her step. Maybe, just maybe, that date wasn’t all that fake after all.

The Text Chain

Chapter Notes

hi! thanks again for all the comments! each one makes me smile! i hope you enjoy this chapter!

The moment her phone chimed, Rio was wide awake.

It was 8am on a Monday. Usually, she wouldn’t be up for another half hour; she didn’t have to be at the college until 10. Yet in some subconscious part of her resting mind, she knew exactly who that text was from, and that was more than enough to rise her from even the deepest of slumbers.

Reaching for the phone charging on her bedside table, she opened up the message with an untameable grin.

AGATHA

Morning! Just taking your shirt to the dry cleaners. I’ll let you know when it’s done.

RIO

Good morning! You know you don’t have to dry clean it. I just shove it in a washing machine.

Agatha’s reply was almost instant.

AGATHA

I’ll pretend I didn’t know that. And anyway, I’ve just taken it in. Decided to walk to work this morning.

RIO

How long will it take you?

AGATHA

Another twenty minutes. I’m getting coffee on the way.

RIO

From our place?

AGATHA

No, there’s a hole in the wall on my way. It’s not amazing, but it’s hard to mess up black coffee.

RIO

And here I was thinking I’d converted you to an iced coffee girl.

AGATHA

Not first thing in the morning.

RIO

Work in progress then.

There was a pause between the next message, and Rio took the time to get out of bed and head to the bathroom to start her morning routine.

She was wearing an oversized shirt and Agatha’s boxers, a new essential in her bedtime attire, but also it meant she could walk out into the living room without Lilia catching a glimpse of her butt.

Lilia was up, of course, and was in the process of getting the blender out when she approached the kitchen area. “This is early for you,” she commented. Rio shrugged.

“Woke up, so thought I’d start the day a bit earlier.”

Lilia eyed her suspiciously, but before she could say anything Rio’s phone chimed in her hand. Looking down, she saw Agatha’s reply.

AGATHA

Black coffee secured. Now heading to the office. What are you doing today?

RIO

Class, lab time, two hours independent study, then another class. What about you?

AGATHA

Mostly meetings. I’m recommending we leave the book as it is.

Rio smiled. They had discussed it a little the night before. Agatha had messaged her saying she didn’t know what to do. The book was amazing, apparently. The plot was gripping, and the love story was so well written, but the fact remained that it would damage the sales. After some exchanged texts, and a phone call that ended up lasting over an hour, Agatha had decided to sleep on it. Rio had been rooting for her to say yes, but she had to let Agatha make the decision herself.

RIO

That’s great! I think you’re doing the right thing.

AGATHA

Me too. Thanks for the help last night.

RIO

Hey, what are fake girlfriends for?

AGATHA

You certainly are proving yourself useful.

Rio bit her lip.

RIO

Oh you have no idea how useful I can be.

The sound of Lilia clearing her throat brought her back to the present.

“What?”

“I don’t even have to ask who you’re messaging, but will you tear yourself away from that phone for a moment to help me with these smoothies.”

“Can’t we have pancakes?”

“No.”

Rio set her phone aside and got to work slicing up the fruit.

“You two seem to be talking a lot more,” Lilia commented.

“I guess,” Rio said dismissively.

“I can tell just from the way you look at her texts that you’re absolutely smitten, but don’t get distracted. You’re so close to getting your doctorate and I know new relationships are exciting…”

“Agatha knows that,” Rio insisted. “And I’m doing fine. My tutor said I’m far ahead of schedule anyway.”

Rio’s phone dinged and she looked over at it longingly. She heard Lilia chuckle.

“What?”

“You two really need to have sex,” she said. “Before you explode.”

“I’m not that bad,” Rio insisted, but that only made Lilia laugh more.

“Oh please. She sends you a text and you’re practically foaming at the mouth.”

“No I’m not!”

“Just do yourselves and everyone else in a fifty-foot radius a favour and resolve that sexual tension already! Because I swear, if I spend another night having to hear you moan…”

Rio covered her ears. “Lalala. I can’t hear you.”

“Alright, alright.” Lilai held up her hands. “But you get the message.”

Rio dropped her hands. “Great, now I have fruit juice in my hair.”

Lilia laughed again. “I’m not even to say what I was thinking.”

“I think you’re the one who needs to get laid,” Rio accused as she moved to the sink to wash the fruit off her hands. “And for that, you can finish the smoothies by yourself.”

Rio picked up her phone and flopped down on the couch, opening Agatha’s message.

AGATHA

I’ll keep that in mind. Are you still excited for tomorrow?

Rio grinned. She was indeed excited for tomorrow, partly to see Billy and his parents, but mostly because she missed Agatha. It had only been two days, but it felt like weeks.

You’ll learn quickly that there is always drama in this family.

Why not throw my sister and Jen in the mix and see what happens?

A nuclear explosion probably.

Nah that’ll be if we threw Lilia in there too.

AGATHA

And Senõr Scratchy

RIO

And Webbers.

AGATHA

And my assistant.

RIO

A true coven of chaos.

AGATHA

You ain’t kidding .

The bender turned on, loud and sudden.

Rio jumped in her seat, dropping her phone on the couch. She whirled round with a face like thunder. “Lilia!”

Her roommate just smirked. “So tense, and we all know why.”

Rio gave her the middle figure before turned back around and folding her arms. She hated that she was totally right.

Agatha walked through the office with a warm smile, greeting her employees as she walked by their desks. Some smiled back, some offered weak waves, while others just stared. Sharon was the only one who greeted her with equal enthusiasm.

“Good morning, boss,” Sharon said with her usual grin. “You seem happy this morning.”

“I am,” Agatha replied. “It’s a beautiful morning, and I get to come to work to see your wonderful smile.”

Sharon’s smile didn’t faulter, but the slight lift of her eyebrows showed her surprise. “Well I’m pleased to see you in such a good mood. And to make your day even better, I decided to do some baking yesterday.”

“What kind of baking?”

Sharon moved around her desk and brought out three cake tins. “What do you want to start with? Brownies, cookies, or rocky road.”

“Cookie, please.”

Sharon held out the tin and Agatha picked out the one she wanted.

“Thanks.”

“Anytime, sweetie. So now you know how I spent my weekend, what did you get up to?”

“Rio and I ended up staying at my sisters’ on Friday, then I spent most of Saturday trying to find the latest iPhone for my nephew. Why do those things always sell out? Surely, they must know everyone will want it.”

“You and Rio seem to be going strong,” Sharon commented.

“Yeah,” Agatha nodded. “We are.”

“I’m glad.” Sharon patted her affectionately on the arm. “Happiness suits you.”

Agatha gave Sharon one last smile before walking into her office, cookie in hand. She dropped her bag by her desk and placed the cookie on top of her closed laptop. Getting out her phone, she took a picture and sent it to Rio.

AGATHA

Look what my assistant surprised me with.

Rio’s reply came almost instantly.

RIO

Those are so good 😭

Agatha took a bite and took another photo of the cookie.

AGATHA

Can confirm. So very good.

RIO

Stop!!

AGATHA

And she’s made brownies too

She hasn’t!

AGATHA

And rocky road…

RIO

NOOOO!!

Agatha chuckled, wishing she could see Rio’s reactions. She wished she could just see her, in all honesty. It was strange. They had gone days without talking and now even after speaking non-stop all weekend, she couldn’t get enough.

AGATHA

When is that study time you have today?

1-3 why?

Fancy meeting me for 20 minutes around 2-ish? We could walk to the coffee shop and back or something?

Yes please!

Rio waited anxiously in the lobby of Agatha’s work. Her morning class had dragged because she knew most of it already, and the lab was too busy for her to get much work done. What got her through was seeing Agatha, even just for twenty minutes.

Agatha smiled and walked over to her. “Is that my hoodie?”

Rio looked down and cursed. In all the excitement, she forgot she was wearing the hoodie she borrowed Saturday morning.

“Yeah. Sorry I’ll get it washed and I’ll…”

“No, no.” Agatha looked her up and down appraisingly. “Keep it. It suits you.”

Rio grinned, bowing her head in the hope of hiding her blush. “So coffee?”

“Yes, but before I forget.” Agatha reached into her handbag and pulled out a small Tupperware box. “Sharon says hi.”

“Yes!” Rio took the box and ripped the lid off. “No way! I get all three?!”

“Rio, you’re acting like I just gave you Superbowl tickets.”

“Fuck the Superbowl. I’m hungry.” Rio stuffed the cookie in her mouth as they made their way out of the building, shoving the rest in her bookbag.

“How was class?”

“Pointless,” Rio replied, chewing the last remnants of the cookie. “We had a guest lecturer, and he did a presentation about Atropa Belladonna. That’s like the gateway poisonous plant. I knew all about it by the time I was Billy’s age. He could have at least gone with something more obscure. Then the lab was full of master’s students getting an induction. And I’m having to sit through an undergraduate lecture based on the very essay I wrote.”

“The azalea one?”

“Apparently my findings are a great learning opportunity for the undergraduate class, but I’m just there to answer questions and take notes on his observations of my findings.”

“Just wait until you’re the world’s leading expert in poisonous plants,” Agatha told her. “Then he’ll be begging you to lecture there.”

“He’ll probably take credit for that too,” Rio grumbled. “Anyway, enough about me. Have you had your meeting about that book yet?”

“That’s what I’ll be heading back for,” Agatha replied, and Rio could hear an uneasiness in her voice. “I’m hoping I can make a convincing argument.”

Rio stared at her in disbelief. “Wait, are you nervous?”

“Of course I’m nervous. The hopes and dreams of every gay girl in this country and beyond rest on me convincing a room full of straight guys that it won’t flop.”

Rio didn’t envy her. While morals sometimes came into her research, it was never this momentous.

“I wish you could read it, Rio,” Agatha continued. “I mean, I always loved the main character. While I was editing that first two books, I loved her spunk and her drive to get what she wanted. I was a little sad when the third book went to someone else, but by then I had my big office and fancy couch.”

“I do like that couch,” Rio commented as the approached the door to the coffee shop. “But I get it. Sometimes success comes with personal sacrifice.”

“Very wise of you,” Agatha teased as she pulled the coffee shop door open for her.

“I know,” Rio smirked as she stepped inside. “I heard it on a telenovela.”

There was a bit of a queue, but they soon found themselves at the counter.

“Usual?” Agatha asked, and Rio nodded.

“Two iced coffees to go please,” Agatha told the barista, who rung it up.

Rio saw the gleam of the American Express card out of the corner of her eye.

“Nope.” She loaded up her apple pay. “I’m not letting you pay again.”

“Well I’m not letting you pay,” Agatha argued. “I asked you to come all the way out here.”

“I wanted to,” Rio insisted. “Just let me pay. Please?”

“Fine,” Agatha relented, and with a smile, Rio loaded up her Apple Pay and was about to hover it over the reader when a flash of gold beat her to it.

“Agatha!”

“Sorry, I couldn’t help it.”

The barista looked between them with a combination of fear and confusion before rushing to make their drinks. Once she handed them over, Rio took hers and stormed out of the coffee shop.

“Rio wait!” She heard Agatha called after her and, with the stomp of sprinting stilettos, she quickly appeared beside her. “I’m sorry. I just don’t want you wasting your money on me.”

“I wouldn’t be wasting it,” Rio argued. “You treat me so much. I just want to treat you too.”

“What you’ve done for me this weekend alone is beyond what money can buy,” Agatha insisted. “Look, I promise next time I won’t let you pay. I’ll even give you my card so I can’t.”

“Fine,” Rio accepted. Looking down, she noticed Agatha, the iconic leftie that she was, had her drink in her left hand. Rio’s was in her right, meaning their empty hands were just hanging there. Such a shame, she thought.

So, swinging her hand, she casually hooked her fingers with Agatha’s.
She expected Agatha to freeze, even just for a second, but instead she found their fingers fully laced together. They looked at each other and smiled, before enjoying the quiet closeness on their way back to the office.

They stopped outside the main doors and Rio couldn’t help but mourn the end of their little interlude.

“Thanks for meeting me,” Agatha said. “I needed this before I go into the hellmouth.”

“You’ll do fine.” Rio squeezed her hand encouragingly. “And remember, don’t underestimate the sapphic market. We’re a passionate bunch.”

“I’ll definitely keep that in mind.” Agatha lightly swung their joined hands. “I better go.”

“Yeah.” Rio wanted to fall to her knees and cling to her legs, keeping Agatha there with her.

Agatha squeezed her hand in return. “I’ll let you know how it went later on.”

“Yes I’ll be waiting.”

Agatha gave her hand one last squeeze before pulling away. Rio swore she felt the connection break in her soul.

“Bye,” Agatha said as she backed up to the doors.

“Bye,” Rio replied, and watched her go.

Okay, maybe Lilia was right. She was going to explode.

Later, during her designated reading time, Agatha found herself with the now familiar urge to message Rio.

She had wanted to message her as soon as she got out of her meeting, but she didn't want to bother her while she was in class, or straight away when she got home.

It was ridiculous really. Even with Wanda, she hadn't wanted to see her all the time. They only messaged and called when they had to, and never organised to meet each other during the workday unless it was work related. Yet with Rio, it was different. She enjoyed their pointless conversations and random spontaneous meetups, maybe more than she was willing to admit to even herself.

She was contemplating what the message should say when Billy's contact photo filled her screen. Agatha answered it with a smile. "This is a surprise."

"I wanted to test out my new phone," Billy explained. "Thanks again. It's awesome."

"I should hope so. I had to go to five different stores to find one. So, how was school?"

"Okay," he answered, suddenly not so happy. " I saw Eddie."

"Oh?"

"I waved to him, and he turned away."

Agatha hated this. She hated him being so hurt, especially when it was all because of some boy. "I'm sorry, kid, but maybe you'll be able to talk it out with him when it isn't so fresh."

"Maybe, but I've decided I'm going to focus on myself," he insisted. "Like you said, it's worth waiting for the right person."

“Exactly, there’s no rush. You’re barely in high school, and I know you really like Eddie. I really liked my high school girlfriend, but sometimes there’s a reason they’re your first and not your last.”

“I guess. I just wish I could meet my Rio, you know?”

“Your Rio?” Agatha questioned in surprise. “What do you mean?”

“You know, someone who looks at you like you’re the centre of the universe.”

She didn’t reply. She couldn’t reply. She could barely even think.

“Agatha?”

“Hm?”

“You hadn’t noticed that, had you?”

“She’s always looked at me that way,” she quickly dismissed. “She’s just…I don’t know…Rio.”

“Please, you look at her the same. And you always smile at her all gooey.”

“No, I don’t!”

“Liar.”

“Billy!”

“Oh shit, Mom is calling me. I gotta go, bye.”

“Billy, don’t you dare…”

He hung up the phone.

“Fuck,” she cursed to herself, before looking to Senõr Scratchy. “What do you think?”

He stared back her, chewing on something rather frantically.

“What is that?”

She got up to look and saw a piece of paper half dragged into the cage. “Really?” Reaching in, she snatched it off him, assessing the damage. It was the warranty on Billy’s phone.

“You are so lucky I got an email copy,” she said, ripping the paper up and putting it in the bin. “Otherwise I’d be making rabbit pie.”

Senõr Scratchy didn’t care. He knew her threats were empty.

Back on the couch, her phone dinged. Moving over, she was expecting more teasing from Billy, or Rebecca scolding her again for buying the phone. Instead, she was pleasantly surprised.

RIO

Hey how did your meeting go?

Agatha smiled, and she had to admit, it did feel a little gooey.

Rio stared at where her phone rested on the arm of the couch, willing it to do something.

Had she only just messaged her? Yes.

Was she already impatient waiting for a reply? Also yes.

She had watched her phone like a hawk all the way through that dumbass lecture, all the way home on the subway, and Lilia had to tell her to leave it in her room during dinner. Yet, Agatha had not made true on her promise to let her know how her meeting went.

It wasn’t Agatha’s fault. She was a busy lady, and Billy was probably being needy which of course had to be her priority. Still, Rio was desperate to know what happened, how the rest of her afternoon went, what she was up to now.

Any Agatha news was news worth knowing.

Eventually, as she failed to concentrate on the episode of Real Housewives Lilia was currently engrossed in, she bit the bullet and messaged first.

The wait between the outgoing text and incoming reply was not long in reality, but for Rio it felt like an eternity. And when her screen finally lit up, she scrambled for the phone and opened it without hesitation.

AGATHA

Hey sorry I didn’t want to interrupt your class and just got off the phone with Billy. It went well enough. They said yes, but they’ve said it’ll be at my own risk. If it blows up in our faces, my head is on the block.

RIO

Shit that’s a lot of pressure on you.

AGATHA

I can handle it. The author has also threatened to terminate her contract if the story is changed, so they didn’t have much of a choice.

RIO

Can she do that?

AGATHA

The bidding for the first book was extremely competitive. Mike made a drastic call and said we’d publish and not take the rights. It worked, but now we’re always on a knife edge.

RIO

You should pouch her and start your own publishing house.

AGATHA

Please, I’d end up bankrupt in a week.

RIO

The bank would be too scared of you. They’d just give you more money.

AGATHA

And if that didn’t work?

RIO

Then your crazy fake girlfriend would be there behind you with a pair of scissors.

AGATHA

How was class?

RIO

Dumb. He totally messed it up and didn’t even put in the important stuff. Some of the undergrads were so stupid too.

AGATHA

Not long now until you’ll be Dr. Vidal. Don’t forget that!

Rio smirked. She was now determined to get Agatha to call her that in person.

RIO

How’s Billy?

There was a long pause between replies, and Rio became worried. Had something happened? Had he forgiven that boy? She bit her thumbnail nervously.

“Stop doing that,” Lilia scolded. “It’s a bad habit.”

Rio stuck her tongue out at her and returned to watching her phone. When Agatha’s reply came through, it was lengthy.

AGATHA

He’s okay. He loves the phone I got him, even if Rebecca is furious. She’s told me I spoil him too much, but he needed a phone. Even if it’s just for safety reasons. He called me to test it out, so all seems to work. Good job really. Senõr Scratchy ate the paper copy of his warranty! I asked him how school was and he told me he waved at Eddie and that boy turned away from him. The nerve! If I lived closer, I’d go round to his house and settle this myself.

Rio couldn’t help but laugh, earning a confused look from Lilia.

RIO

Are you going to offer his aunt out for a fight?

AGATHA

It would hardly be fair. I’m surprisingly quick.

RIO

Oh I have no doubt 😉 excited to see you all tomorrow!

AGATHA

Me too

Before Rio could respond, another message popped up.

AGATHA

After they’ve all gone home, can we go to a bar to talk?

Rio’s stomach dropped. Shit, shit, shit. That was never good.

RIO

Is something wrong?

Thankfully, Agatha’s reply was swift.

AGATHA

No, it’s all good, and it’s nothing bad. At least I hope not. I’d just like to talk about us.

RIO

Us?

AGATHA

Yeah. Like what we are to each other now. If that’s a conversation you would like to have, that is?

Rio’s heart did backflip after backflip, and she didn’t even try to contain the grin .

RIO

That is definitely a conversation I’d like to have.

AGATHA

Great, I think there is a bar around the corner from the restaurant. We can walk there after.

RIO

Sounds perfect!

“I don’t even have to ask who you’re texting,” Lilia commented. “That stupid smile tells it all.”

Rio stuck her middle finger up at her, but didn’t deny it. She wished the hours between then and the following evening would disappear. So she could finally see Agatha again and, finally , admit what was now too powerful to ignore.

What could possibly go wrong?

The Birthday Meal

Chapter Notes

hi! thank you again for all the comments! they have made the last couple of days bearable! i hope you enjoy this new chapter!

Agatha had cleared her afternoon schedule. She was going to get her hair done, and had already arranged to pop buy a few stores in search of a new outfit, right down to what was underneath. She just had to get through the morning first.

The anticipation for the evening was near unbearable. She was looking forward to the family meal, no doubt, but she just needed to get Rio to that damn bar. To finally make sense of what was happening between them. Agatha just hoped they were on the same page. She didn’t know what she’d do if they weren’t.

Her desperation for the evening to arrive was making the morning drag. It seemed recently her work had been a hindrance rather than a passion, and as she sat in her office drafting her out-of-office email, she wondered if this was just a rut, or had she just  become distracted by other things. Or rather someone.

Her phone vibrated on the desk, and when she looked at the notification, she smiled.

RIO

Hey are you still picking me up?

AGATHA

Yes 7pm sharp!

RIO

Great! How’s your morning going?

AGATHA

Much better now I’m talking to you.

RIO

Smooth. Very smooth

AGATHA

I do try. What are you up to?

Rio’s reply came in the form of a photo. She was in her room, Agatha could tell, wearing a black sweater with her hair loose in its usual way. Her head propped up by her arm, which seemed to be propped up by her desk. Those brown eyes. That smile. She was the truest beauty Agatha had ever seen.

RIO

Study day so I’m writing more towards my thesis what about you?

Agatha decided two could play at that game. Opening her front camera, she adjusted her chair to get the best lighting. She took a few and sent the best one.

AGATHA

Just at work.

Rio’s reply arrived very quickly.

RIO

💗💗💗💗💗

RIO

You need to warn a girl! I almost fell off my chair because of how hot you look.

Agatha bit back a giggle.

AGATHA

Could say the same about you.

RIO

I can’t wait to see you later.

AGATHA

It won’t be long. Can I pick you up from your apartment instead of outside?

RIO

Such a gentleman

Agatha smirked.

AGATHA

Oh honey I’m no gentleman

RIO

Good I was almost disappointed.

That had her biting her lip again. God, she couldn’t wait until seven.

Her hair appointment went without a hitch, and her shopping trip was…fruitful. She took the time to change, applied her make up perfectly and sprayed a ridiculous amount of perfume on. With Senõr Scratchy fed, and her apartment clean (just in case), she headed down to get a cab.

During the short ride to Rio’s apartment, Agatha couldn’t help but feel a little nervous. What if Rio didn’t like her outfit? What if the meal went to shit? What if she messed up their talk at the bar? And what if Rio didn’t want her?

The worries evaporated as the cab pulled up outside Rio’s, replaced with the overwhelming desire to see her fake girlfriend as soon as possible. She offered the driver a generous tip if he waited for her, which he was eager to take, and walked into the building as fast as her stilettos would allow. She got up to Rio’s floor, sped down the corridor to her apartment door, and, sucking in a deep breath, she knocked.

Lilia opened the door and, unlike the last time she came face to face with Rio’s strange roommate, the woman greeted her with a genuine smile.

“Ah, the princess has arrived.”

Perhaps she did look like a princess that evening. She’d decided to abandon her usual suits for a hip-hugging black dress that even had the sales assistant stumbling over her words. Her hopes were for it to have a similar effect on her date for the evening, but she knew that would be unlikely. Rio always had something to say.

“Is she ready?” Agatha asked, and Lilia laughed as she shut the door behind them.

“It’s been like Project Runway in here, but I think she’s just about ready.”

Lilia walked over and knocked on Rio’s bedroom door. “Your girlfriend is here.”

“Just coming!” Rio’s voice carried through the door.

Lilia walked back to Agatha with a knowing smile. “I hope I don’t see her back here tonight.”

Agatha tried to hide her shock at the woman’s bluntness. “I’ll try my best.”

They both looked to the bedroom door as it creaked open, and Agatha swore her heart stopped.

Rio, in a black three-piece suit, no shirt or tie, one hand in her trouser pocket and the other pushing a strand of straightened hair behind her ear. Her lips were painted red, her eyes framed by dark eyeliner and shadow, and she shined with a glow that no make-up could ever replicate.

Agatha could only stare as Rio looked her up and down with a grin.

“Holy shit you look good.”

Agatha swallowed and tried to snap herself out of whatever trance Rio had put her under. “You look amazing.”

“Yes, you both look good,” Lilia agreed. “Now can you both go and enjoy yourselves!”

Rio walked forward and held her arm out to Agatha. “M’lady.”

Agatha smiled and linked their arms together, the touch electric and addictive. God, she couldn’t wait to get to that bar.

Rio couldn’t help but state. The fresh curls in her hair, her sharp lipstick, and the dress…well that was outright sinful.

"I didn't know you had a suit like that," Agatha commented as they walked from the cab to the restaurant.

"I didn't know you had a dress like that," Rio mirrored back, making Agatha smile.

"I guess we've both full of surprises then."

Rio grinned deviously. "You have no idea."

The restaurant wasn’t as ridiculously fancy as she expected, but it was enough to make Rio glad she made an effort. The Kaplans were already sat at their table, and Billy jumped up so fast Rio thought he was going to go through ceiling. He gave Agatha a hug, before ingulfing Rio in one that was just as enthusiastic.

“You both look amazing!” He got his phone out of his pocket. “Stand together. I want a photo!”

They moved close together, and Rio placed a cautious hand on Agatha’s back. She knew they had been less tense when it came to touching, but what she didn’t expect was for Agatha to hook her hand on her waist and press their sides firmly together.

They smiled at the camera as Billy took the photos, and Rio tried her best to breathe normally. God, what Agatha did to her was downright torturous. She needed to take Lilia’s advice, and soon.

“Step back so I can take some full-body ones,” Billy instructed and Agatha put her free hand on her hip, still keeping Rio close.

“We may look like models, kid, but we’re not.”

“But…”

"Billy, let them sit down," his dad said playfully, and Billy relented.

Agatha moved to sit next to Rebecca and Rio took the seat opposite beside Billy. She knew Agatha had done that on purpose. Though Rebecca had greeted her with a genuine smile, Rio knew she still hadn't completely won her over.

Jeff sat at the head of the table, smiling with birthday glee.

"Happy Birthday Jeff." Agatha reached into her back and slid over a small black box with a matching bow. "This is from us."

Rio gave Agatha a confused look, which she just shrugged at. It seemed their fake relationship was at the shared gift stage.

Jeff pulled open the box and pulled out a silver watch. “Woah, this is cool!”

Billy looked over and his eyes widened. “Don’t they cost…”

Agatha and Rebecca gave him a warning look.

Jeff put the watch on and admired it with a smile. “I love it. Thanks, ladies.”

“You’re welcome,” Agatha responded, and Rio nodded along.

“Yeah, happy birthday, Jeff. Thank you for inviting me to celebrate.”

“Hey, like I said on Saturday, you’re pretty much joining family now,” Jeff insisted. “Figured we best start the birthday traditions now.”

Rio looked to Agatha, who seemed totally unfazed by her becoming an honorary Kaplan. In fact, she seemed quite pleased about it from the soft smile on her face.

God, Rio just wanted to reach over and kiss her.

Rebecca opened the wine menu. “Since I’m driving tonight, you ladies need to have a bottle of wine for me.”

“I’ll have a glass of whisky,” Agatha responded. “I don’t want a repeat of your birthday.”

“What happened?” Rio asked, and Billy burst out laughing.

“Agatha had too much to drink and said she always wanted to…”

“One more word and I’m taking that phone back,” Agatha threatened, which affective ended the conversation.

“What about you?” Rebecca looked to Rio hopefully, but she shook her head.

“Wine makes me crazy.”

Agatha tilted her head curiously, but Rebecca just tutted.

“You two are boring.”

“I assure you we’re far from boring.” Agatha winked at Rio, and she had to bow her head to hide her blush.

The meal went by in a blur of chatter and laughter. Rio could see why Jeff liked the place- the food was unreal- but it was the company that did it for her.

Jeff was throwing out dad jokes left right and centre which Agatha heckled from her end of the table. Rebecca was also surprisingly witty, and Billy was, well, Billy. He was indeed in love with his new phone, and had insisted on taking some selfies, and got Agatha to take a proper picture of them both as his mom ‘made every photo look weird’.

They were a quirky family, she had to admit, but a loving one. It had been a long time since she experienced that. Sure, she had Alice, but sometimes a family of two was just as lonely as a family of one. Being an honorary Kaplan was nice, even just for the night.

“Dessert!” Billy announced once their table had been cleared. “We need to have dessert.”

“We have cake at home,” his mom argued.

“But Agatha and Rio won’t get any!” Billy looked between them. “Don’t we need to have dessert?”

“I’m stuffed, kid,” Agatha admitted, but Rio shrugged.

“I’m down if you are.”

Billy grinned. “Okay, Rio is officially the cool aunt.”

“She’s not even your aunt yet,” Agatha argued.

“Semantics,” Billy dismissed. “She’s still cooler.”

“Of course I am,” Rio teased, sticking her tongue out at Agatha, who simply raised an eyebrow. She was amused though. Rio could tell by her eyes.

“You can’t have dessert and cake,” his mom told him. “That’s too much sugar.”

“But mom…”

“Why don’t you share mine?” Rio suggested. “Then technically it’s not two.”

She looked to Rebecca for confirmation, and she nodded. Billy grinned and grabbed the dessert menu. “What are you getting?”
