Her sister laughed. “You know why.”

Agatha opened her mouth to respond, to question exactly what Rebecca meant, because surely she didn’t mean…because that would be ridiculous. Even in the timeline of their fake relationship, it was too fast. Moving in would be too fast. THAT would be absolutely stupid, and reckless, and…why was she arguing with herself?

Before she could make that argument to her sister, Billy came barrelling into the kitchen.

“Agatha, you need to take over. Rio is too good at Mario Kart.”

Rio’s evil laugh echoed through from the living room. “You will never defeat me, Harkness!”

Agatha tossed the dish towel aside. “Oh, we’ll see about that, Vidal.”

Rio won. Rio won every single race. Rebecca was in shock, Billy in awe, and Agatha…Agatha was not pleased.

“Oh come on, sweetheart,” Rio said as they drove back to the city. “So you lost? Billy said you’ve lost plenty of times before.”

Agatha shot her a glare before fixing her eyes on the road again.

“Yeez,” Rio spoke up again. “I didn’t know you were such a sore loser.”

“And you’re a sore winner,” Agatha accused. “You laughed in my face.”

“Please, you were all fighting talk until I hit you with that banana.”

“I just don’t like losing,” Agatah huffed. “Sorry for not being a perfect person.”

“You’re perfect to me,” Rio quickly protested. “Like I’m in awe of you.”

Agatha’s lips curled at the edges. “Dork.”

“Geek.”

“I love you.”

“I love you too.”

“Are you sure you can’t stay at my place?” Agatha asked. “I’m sure Lilia will be fine.”

“I’m sure, but maybe next time she goes on a date, we could spend the night at my place? You know, just for a change?”

“I don’t know. I don’t like leaving Senõr Scratchy alone all day and then all night.”

“Bring him,” Rio insisted. “He needs to meet Webbers anyway. Seeing as they will be stepsiblings at some point.”

“I’m not being stepmom to a tarantula,” Agatah protested. “You know how I feel about spiders.”

“Arachnids,” Rio corrected. “And I know, but we come as a package deal. I’m not too keen on fluffy animals, remember? But I love Senõr Scratchy.”

“You just don’t like them,” Agatha pointed out. “I hate spiders.”

“Because of your mom?”

“I don’t want to talk about it tonight.”

“Okay,” Rio accepted. “But I’d like to know some time. I’d like to know everything about you.”

Agatha smirked. “So I can’t have any secrets?”

“I thought you told me them all?”

“I have one.”

“You do?”

Agatah nodded.

“What?”

“I can’t tell you.”

“Please?”

“Nope.”

“Why not?”

“Because it’s a big secret.”

“Pleeeease.”

“No.”

“Please, please, please, please, please, ple-”

“I want a baby with you.”

That managed to shut her up.

“No right now,” Agatha clarified. “But some day. I want them to look just like you, and for them to love plants just as much as they love reading. And to be totally in awe of Grandma Lorna, and adore their cousin, Billy. That’s my secret.”

Rio remained quiet, and Agatha dared to steal a glance her way. Her girlfriend’s eyes were wide, her body tense and mouth agape. Shit, shit, shit.

Agatha sighed, stopping at a red light. “I’m sorry, I shouldn’t have…”

“Can’t we have one right now?”

Luckily her foot was on the brake, otherwise she’d have caused an accident. “We can’t have a baby right now, Rio.”

“Why not?” Rio questioned. “It’s a long process. We might as well start it now.”

“So you want a baby?”

“I really want a baby, especially with you.”

“You need to finish your PhD.”

“The baby is more important.”

“The baby will wait,” Agatha told her. “You need to graduate.”

“Okay, so after graduation…”

“We can revisit the conversation,” Agatah suggested, moving to the gas as the lights turned green. “Discuss our options.”

“Fine,” Rio accepted. “You need to accept my first-born son though.”

“I’ll think about it,” Agatha replied, knowing she was never going anywhere near that damn spider.

She pulled up outside Rio’s building, like she had done so many times before. Each time had been harder to say goodbye, but this was the worst.

“I’m going to miss you,” Agatha admitted. “I’ll call you when I get home.”

“We could sleep on call?” Rio suggested. “Then it’ll be like I’m there.”

“No, it won’t.” Agatha couldn’t pretend. It wouldn’t be anywhere close to the same.

Rio leaned over and kissed her softly. “I’ll see you tomorrow?”

“You can count on it.” Agatha kissed her one more time and watched sadly as Rio climbed out of the car. “I love you.”

“I love you too,” Rio grinned, before she headed off inside. Agatha waited until she had totally disappeared from view before driving away.

Making her way through the city traffic, she tried to think of other things. She was due some Senõr Scratchy time, and she was in the middle of a good book, and she and Rio were going to speak over the phone. But she wouldn’t be able to touch her, hold her, see her smile in real time.  And she was scared. Scared of sleeping alone. She didn’t want the nightmare. She didn’t want to be back in that cupboard again. She didn’t want to wake up panicked and alone.

She was a few blocks away when her phone rang. Glancing at her central console, she saw it was Rio. She quickly answered.

“Hey, I’m not home yet. Just give me five…”

“ Agatha ,” Rio’s voice escaped the car speakers in nothing more than a whisper. “Are you still close?”

Worry shot through her. “Yes, why?”

“I need you to get back here now. Please, I need to get out of here.”

Agatha didn’t hesitate. She did a u-turn, flipping off those who beeped her, before racing back towards Rio’s apartment.

“What happened? Are you safe?”

“I’m fine, but please hurry. I’ll meet you out front.”

By the time Agatha pulled up, Rio was racing out of the building and swiftly jumped into the passenger seat.

“Go, go, go.”

Agatha sped off. “Are you okay? Are you hurt? Do we need to call the police?”

“I’m fine,” Rio insisted. “Traumatised, but fine.”

“What happened?”

“It was awful, Agatha. I walked in, and I thought I was home alone because all the lights were off. Then I saw there were clothes all over the floor, and I thought Lilia had just had a bit of a wardrobe disaster, but there was like this really ugly grandma sweater that I knew Lilia wouldn’t even think of wearing. And then I heard it.”

“Heard what?”

“The moaning.”

“What?!” Agatha slammed on the breaks, earning another beep from the car behind. “Rio Vidal, I though you were in danger! I’ve broke a dozen traffic laws to get back to you, and it was all because you heard you roommate have sex.”

“It wasn’t sex,” Rio insisted. “They were fucking. Like dirty fucking.”

Agatha shook her head and started driving again. “So? Lilia was having a good time. Need a remind you how loud we can be?”

“There’s loud, and there’s loud. ”

“It can’t have been that bad.”

“ Yes, baby you’re doing so good! Just give it to me, baby! Give it to me!”

“Okay, I get the picture.”

“No, you don’t,” Rio insisted. “That was just Lilia. Her date was screaming…”

Agatha wished to could erase this knowledge from her mind. “Right, well, we’re going to my place now so you can just forget it ever happened.”

“I will never forget,” Rio responded dramatically. “I’m serious, Agatha. I don’t think I can ever have sex again.”

“Woah, woah, let’s not be too hasty there,” Agatah quickly jumped in. “I’m sure you’ve heard people moaning before.”

“Not like that! And not when I live with one of them!”

“So because you heard Lilia have sex, we’re never going to have sex again?”

“Yes.”

“Right.” Agatha didn’t know what to say. Her brain was totally frazzled. “We can still cuddle though, right?”

“Maybe,” Rio answered. “We’ll see.”

Once at Agatha’s apartment, Rio played with Senõr Scratchy, before she decided she wanted an early night. Agatha let her get ready, pretending she wanted to finish a chapter of her book. Instead, she stood looking out at the city, contemplating the conversations that had transpired that evening. About their future homes, their future children, and the ring. She couldn’t forget about the ring.

Her grandmother's ring had been in the Harkness family for years, given to her grandmother by her grandfather. She had worn it every day since their engagement to the day she was sent off to the funeral home. Agatha had kept it safe, planning to give it either to her future wife, or to Billy to give to his future partner, until it became very apparent it would not be appropriate for her nephew’s future spouse.

Rio, however, had the perfect hand for such a gem. A green emerald encased on a gold band. It was like it had been made for her. Maybe it had been, all those years go. Perhaps, as it was passed down from Harkness to Harkness, it was always destined to be on the finger of one Rio Vidal.

Before Agatha could think more of it, her loves voice cut through the apartment.

“Come on, I want to cuddle.”

Agatha smiled to herself and switched off the light, making her way to her bedroom. Rio was already snuggled in bed, looking at her over the blanket. She made quick work of getting ready, before joining her under it.

“Better?” Agatha asked as Rio instantly nestled in her embrace.

“Much.” Rio answered, resting her head on her shoulder. “I love you.”

Agatha placed a gentle kiss against her crown. “I love you too.”

They didn’t have sex. They just slept. Agatha had no nightmares. Instead, she dreamt of emeralds, happy tears, and a breathtaking smile.

The Date (Part 1)

Chapter Notes

hi guys! sorry this has taken forever! now I'm nearing the end i'm trying to make sure every plotline is fulfilled so i can't just free-write like i used to. i'll try get chapter 30 (!!) up asap. thanks for all the comments and kudos and i hope you all enjoy!

It was Friday, and Rio was so excited.

She was meeting Agatha after she finished work and they were going out for a romantic meal. Just them. A proper date.

Going on a first romantic date after confessions of love and talk of babies was not usually how it worked, but it had worked for them. Still, Rio wanted to have this romance. Wanted to show off their love and share a bottle of champagne between courses and staring lovingly into each other’s eyes.

Agatha had picked the place, but had sent over the details to check it was okay. It was expensive, but not ridiculously so, and the food looked amazing. What Rio loved about it, however, was that her amazing, gorgeous, absolutely perfect girlfriend had found a botanical themed restaurant, complete with indoor shrubs and in-theme cocktails. Pair that with the excellent company and the inevitable late night they’d have when they made it back to Agatha’s apartment, and it was set to be the most perfect evening.

After a morning of classes and lab work, Rio returned to her apartment with an excited spring in her step. Lilia was at the dining table, doing her daily readings.

“You seem happy,” she commented. “Of course you are. I haven’t seen you in days.”

“Well you would have if you hadn’t brought your date home on Wednesday.” Rio was still totally grossed out. Luckily her aversion to the act itself had passed by the next morning, when Agatha ‘accidently’ brushed her inner thigh while they were cuddling.

Lilia chuckled. “It seems we’re going to be like ships in the night from now on. Speaking of which I won’t be here tomorrow night. Think you can convince Agatha to stay over? I don’t trust that new guy down the hall.”

“He’s a veterinarian.”

“He’s a suspicious-looking veterinarian.”

“Fine, I’ll ask her. She will want to bring Senõr Scratchy though. He’ll stay in my room.”

“Who is Mister Scracthy?”

“Senõr,” Rio corrected. “He’s her rabbit.”

“She has a rabbit? Like a bunny rabbit?”

“Yes, an actual animal.”

Lilia laughed. “I’d have thought Agatha would be more of a cat lady.”

“Hey! One, there’s nothing wrong with cats, and two, I don’t like the insinuation behind that at all.”

“Wow, defensive much,” Lilia teased before shuffling her cards. “You know, we only have two months left on our lease.”

“I thought we had the option to renew?”

“We do, but I just wanted you to know, I won’t be offended if you want to back out?”

Rio frowned. “Why would I back out?”

“Because you’re in love.”

Rio waved her off. “Agatha and I discussed it, and we’re going to get our own place at some point, but until then we’re having our separate homes. Our own spaces.”

Lilia let out a loud laugh. “You don’t even have your own personal space at the moment.”

“Do you see Agatha here? No.”

“Because she’s at work,” Lilia reminded her. “Where you have been studying all week.”

Rio crossed her arms. “How do you know that?”

Lilia looked back to her cards. “Lucky guess.”

Before Rio could question her, her phone dinged in her pocket. She pulled it out, seeing it was Alice.

ALICE

Need to talk. Can we meet for coffee?

Rio’s heart dropped. No, no, no. Not today. Please, not today.

RIO

I need to finish some work then I’m meeting Agatha.

It was only half a lie.

ALICE

Please? It’s important. I can meet you at that place near your apartment? Or are you at Agatha’s?

Rio relaxed a little. She seemed more eager than demanding, but she couldn’t be sure.

RIO

Okay but not for too long.

ALICE

Give me 20 minutes!

Rio sighed and stuffed her phone back in her pocket.

“You okay?” Lilia asked.

“Yeah, I’m going to meet Alice.” Rio shrugged it off. “She needs to talk to me. Probably about Jen or something.”

“Well that’s nice, isn’t it?”

“Yeah.” Rio forced a smile before rushing off to dump her stuff in her room.

After a quick check-in with Webbers, she headed off to the Starbucks round the corner. It wasn’t too far, wasn’t too fancy, and was Rio’s second favourite coffee shop. She wondered if she should take Agatha there sometime, but if this what about what she thought it was, the place would be forever cursed in her mind.

Alice was already there, sat at a table in the corner with two iced lattes. Rio approached with caution, tensing when their eyes met. Then her sister smiled, and she allowed herself to relax.

It wasn’t that. It was okay.

“Hey.” She slid into the seat opposite and took a sip of her drink. “Vanilla. You know me too well.”

Alice chuckled. “I should hope. We did grow up together. So, you’re seeing Agatha later?”

“Yes,” Rio grinned. “We have a dinner date. How’s Jen?”

“She’s flying home tomorrow. She wants a double date when she’s back. Next week sometime, though. We’ll be, erm, otherwise occupied this weekend.”

“I bet you will be.” Rio couldn’t imagine what she’d be like if Agatha went away on a work trip. She’d need a week in bed to make up for it. Perhaps even more. (Though if Agatha ever went on a work trip, she would just hide in her suitcase and go with her. That way they could have their own lover’s retreat on the company’s dime. HR would definitely hate them for that, but it would be so worth it).

“Agatha makes you happy, doesn’t she?”

Rio frowned at the question. “Of course she does. Why are you asking that?”

“I’m happy you finally met someone, and at the same time as me! Mom always said we always did everything together.”

Rio smiled, recalling how her stepmother found great joy in the sisterly bond that had formed quickly between them. She didn’t remember much from her time before…when she only spent every other weekend and holidays with them. What she did remember was the excitement to see Alice again, and how sad she always was to say goodbye. After, they weren’t apart for the following twelve years, even longer if you counted going to college on the same campus. Or when they lived two blocks away from each other in equally shitty apartments, or when Rio ended up sleeping on her couch for over a year. Even now, here they were, dating best friends.

Alice was her one constant, and the thought of losing her was too much to bear.

“Speaking of Mom, I need to talk to you about something.”

Dread filled her again. Oh God, had she…

“I’ve started writing her memoir, autobiography. Whatever. I’ve just written the first page, about what I knew about her early years. Her journals don’t start until her teens, but she told us both plenty of stories.”

Rio nodded, instantly relaxed. Crisis averted. “Like the time her mom got mad at her for spending her birthday money on a Beatles LP.”

“Yeah. You know, the story of the American-born daughter of immigrants that did everything to just get by, and she used her love for music to make up for that sacrifice.”

Rio had always been a bit scared of Lorna’s parents. They treated her the same as Alice, but while Alice fit the good girl mould, Rio had always thought of herself as a bad boy, and would spend a lot of time at the receiving end of Mrs Wu’s disapproving gaze. Sometimes though, she caught a smile, and Rio suspected her step-grandmother secretly found her rebelliousness funny.

“Mom made sure we’d never go without, like her family often had to,” Alice continued. “I miss her, and Dad. I know you do too.”

Rio nodded. She missed them every day.

“Especially recently now that I’ve met Jen,” Alice continued. “I wish they could have met.”

“Yeah, I wish they could have met Agatha. Though I’m pretty sure her and Billy would just fangirl.”

“They were in the same room once, though,” Alice reminded her. “When Agatha saw her in concert.”

That was true. It wasn’t a meeting, per say, but they did breathe the same air for two hours.

“I wonder what show it was,” Alice mused. “Maybe we were there too.”

“It was when she and Rebecca were teenagers, so we must have been.”

“Find out which one and I’ll check. I still have the archive from Mom’s old tour photographer.”

“The chances of you spotting Agatha in the crowd is next to nothing.”

“But there’s still a chance.”

“I guess.”

“I think we still have those photographs you took when Dad bought you that camera.”

Rio hid her head in her hands. “Please don’t remind me. I think it was some kind of baby crush on that photographer. I followed her everywhere.”

“No wonder none of us were surprised when you got a girlfriend.”

“I think you were the surprise.”

“Oh please, I was little Miss Biker Jacket and shirts from Hot Topic. Who looked at me and thought heterosexual?”

Rio shrugged. “We thought you were just grunge.”

Alice shook her head, taking a sip of her drink, before regarding Rio seriously once more. “Will you read what I’ve written at some point. You know, to make sure it’s not total crap.”

“Sure, and I’ll get Agatha to look too. She’s got an eye for the written word.”

“Great and maybe you could help when we get to her meeting Dad. You know as much as that as me. Maybe more.”

“No, you’re her daughter.”

“So are you.”

“Not really.”

“You are in the way that counts.”

“I know, but it’s not the same,” Rio told her. “Just…remember what I said…”

“I know, I know. Leave your mom out of it. I’ve not even read that far yet, anyway. Dad and Mom have only just met. They were so smitten. I had to skim over the sex stuff, though. It’s so gross.”

Rio put her head in her hands. Twice in one week. She’d been traumatised twice in one week.

Agatha hummed to herself as she worked. She couldn’t wait for that night. She couldn’t wait to see Rio. That was what her life had become now: wishing away the hours until she saw her incredible girlfriend. Partner. Fianc-no, no, no. She wasn’t thinking about that again. Though her mind seemed to be leading her back there at any given opportunity.

There was a knock on her office door, and Agatha called for them to enter. When she saw it was Mike, she took of her glasses and smiled stiffly.

“Are you here to tell me I need to write my resignation?”

“Wanda still wants you,” Mike told her. “But I’ve buffered her with interns for now.”

“Thank you. Is that all, or…”

“Are you bringing your partner to the gala?”

Agatha frowned. “I am, and if that’s a problem…”

“No, it’s no problem,” Mike quickly insisted. “We need two more people on your table, is all.”

“My table?”

“There’s a knicks game on and some of our partners have tickets. It means we can invite a better mix of people though.”

“Well Sharon can have one.”

“She already has two spots at your table.”

Agatha raised her eyebrows. Was Sharon bringing one of her kids or did she have a date?

“So do you think you can fill the spaces?”

“I can fill them,” Agatha assured. “I’ll confirm and send it over.”

“Excellent. Thank you, Agatha.”

She offered him another tight smile which she dropped the moment he was out of the door. Since the whole Wanda mess, she decided she hated everyone (except Sharon, of course).

Her laptop chimed and she popped her glasses back on to read the incoming email.

Wanda Maximoff

Hi Agatha,

How are you?

W

Agatha glowered at her screen as she typed back.

Agatha Harkness

Leave me alone.

The reply came quickly.

Wanda Maximoff

Do you really want me to?

Agatha Harkness

Yes.

Wanda Maximoff

I stopped by your office last night after you left. Your girlfriend is very pretty.

Agatha clenched her teeth together. She deleted the emails and slammed her laptop shut. She looked at the photos on her desk. The new ones, of Rio and Billy, and herself but those two took up all of her attention.

She was tempted to still write her resignation. To give up her apartment and go more in with Rebecca. To write and try make something for herself away from all this mess, until she and Rio could find a place of their own.

Yet she needed the money, she needed the stability. She’d gotten all this all by herself, and she needed a better reason to throw all it away than an annoying ex. So she continued with her work, and watched the clock tick by.

Soon enough, it was five, and Agatha told Sharon to head on home.

“What are your plans tonight?”

“I’m seeing a friend,” Sharon answered as she gathered her things. “What about you?”

“About to get ready for date night.”

“Oh that’s so darn lovely,” Sharon grinned. “You two are so good together.”

“I know,” Agatha grinned. “Now you go start your weekend.”

Once Sharon was gone, Agatha changed into her date outfit. It was nothing special, a pantsuit she had gotten for some kind of corporate event, but she knew Rio loved her in a suit. After sprucing up her make up and wafting herself with the perfume that she also knew made Rio go crazy, she headed out.

As she waited for the elevator, she got a message.

RIO

Downstairs, my love

Agatha smiled as she stepped forward into the opening elevator doors.

AGATHA

See you soon, my love

Alone in the elevator, her mind wandered back to that old wedding ring chestnut again. She could imagine it easily on Rio’s hand. She could see it glistening on Rio’s finger when she pushed her hair out of her face, could see it against their pillows at sunrise, could see it in every photo and precious moment they’d share thereafter.

Perhaps it wasn’t too early. Maybe when you meet the right person, time doesn’t matter. She knew she wanted to spend the rest of her life with Rio. That was what mattered.

She stepped out of the elevator, adrenaline coursing through her. She spotted Rio instantly, like always, but she also saw she wasn’t alone.

And Agatha saw red.

Rio waited for Agatha, excited but also nervous. She’d put on her best little black dress and done her makeup dark and sharp, but she worried it wasn’t enough. It was stupid, really. She knew Agatha loved her, but she wanted to take her breath away. She wanted that night to be perfect, down to even the smallest details.

“Wow,” a familiar voice called out, “you look a million dollars.”

Rio looked and saw the redheaded woman from the elevator approaching her. She greeted her with a smile. “Thanks. I’m meeting my girlfriend.”

“She’s certainly going to be pleased to see you.” The redhead looked her up and down. “She’s one lucky lady.”

“I’m the lucky one,” Rio insisted. “She’s the best. Oh, and here she is now.”

Rio smiled when she saw Agatha approaching, only to frown when she was the thunderous expression on her girlfriend’s face.

“Agatha, what’s…”

Agatha stood between her and the redhead. “Back off.”

“Agatha, what the hell?” Rio questioned. “We’re just talking…”

“Yeah Agatha,” the redhead said with a smirk. “No harm done.”

Rio frowned. What was going on?

“You.” Agatha jabbed a finger in the redheads face. “Be quiet.” She the whirled round to face Rio. “Do you know who she is?”

“Yeah, well kind of. We’ve met a few times,” Rio asked, looking between them. Why the hell was Agatha acting like this? And why didn’t she like this wom…

Oh.

Oh fuck.

Rio glared at the woman. “You’re Wanda.”

“And you’re my ex’s new squeeze. Rio, isn’t it?”

“How do you know her name?” Agatha demanded.

“Office gossip. You never got someone fired for me, Agatha. I’m offended.”

“Don’t talk to her.” Rio stepped up next to Agatha. “How long did you know who was?”

“As soon as I saw you,” Wanda admitted. “I’d recognise Agatha’s ugly hoodies anywhere. Though she never let me wear one. You really are special.”

“Just leave us alone, Wanda,” Agatha snapped. “We don’t want anything to do with you.”

Wanda looked Rio up and down. “She is pretty, Agatha. I’ll give you that.”

“What’s that supposed to mean?” Agatha demanded.

“Just an observation,” Wanda answered. “Seems to me like you’re having a mid-life crisis with some charity case.”

Agatha surged forward, and Rio was only just quick enough to pull her back.

“Agatha, don’t. She’s not worth it.”

Agatha shrugged Rio off, before storming out of the building, interns jumping out of her path before she shoved the doors open and disappeared into the night.

Rio turned to Wanda. “Happy now?”

“Not really,” Wanda admitted. “The love of my life is running around with a college student. Kind of takes the joy out of things.”

Rio stepped closer. “You listen to me. She isn’t yours. She’s nothing to you now. We’re happy. We’re making plans. You don’t have a place in that.”

Wanda raised her eyebrows. “Oh, don’t I?”

“No,” Rio answered swiftly. “Now if you’ll excuse me.”

With one last glower, she rushed out of the building to catch up with Agatha.

Their perfect night was ruined.

The Date (Part 2)

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! thanks for all the comments and kudos. i hope you like this new chapter! and don't worry even though i'm wrapping things up we still have plenty of chapters to go!

“Agatha!”

She heard Rio’s voice behind her, but she didn’t stop. She charged down the street with her head held high, her jaw set tight as her long coat fanned out behind her. She hated Wanda. She hated her before, but she really hated her now. Playing games with her was one thing, but playing games with Rio? THAT was crossing the line.

“Agatha!” Rio reached her, gripping her arm as she caught her breath. “Agatha, stop for a moment.”

“I can’t.”

“Agatha please!”

That got her to stop.

“She had no right to talk to you.”

“She has no right to talk to you either,” Rio replied. “I can’t believe I was so stupid.”

“You’re not stupid. I should have shown you a photograph or described her. I knew she could be a little unhinged at times, but this? Tricking you? It’s beyond...”

“It’s crazy stalker shit and it needs to stop. Can’t you report her for harassment or...”

“Nothing will happen. She’s too important to the company. Before I could deal with it but this, the emails...”

“What emails?” Rio frowned.

“She emailed me today, told me she’d been in my office and seen a picture of you.”

“Agatha, this can’t continue.”

“I know.” Agatha ran a stressed hand through her hair. “I’ve had enough of it all, but I can’t leave. I can’t just abandon all my hard work because my ex is a crazy fucking…”

Her anger got the best of her, and she kicked a nearby trash can.

“Okay, okay.” Rio took her hand. “Look, it doesn’t matter. I’m fine, okay? A little creeped out but I’ll be fine. No need to beat up an innocent trash can.”

Agatha looked away with shame, but Rio quickly cupped her cheeks.

“Hey, look at me. Whatever happens from now on, we’re a team. Us against the world and that includes your crazy ex.”

“I just hate that this is affecting you now.”

“It was always affecting me,” Rio admitted. “She’s trying to steal my girl.”

“She never will,” Agatha swore. “Still, I hate being the one bringing baggage into this relationship. First my mom, now Wanda…”

“Please, I have loads of baggage,” Rio insisted. “They just all happen to be dead.”

“Morbid,” Agatha responded and Rio laughed softly.

“You bring the drama, I bring the macabre.”

Agatha chuckled. “Complete with a tarantula.”

“And a scheming bunny.”

Agatha grumbled. She still hadn’t totally forgiven Senõr Scratchy, but it was hard to be mad at someone so adorable.

“So shall we go have the most perfect evening ever?” Rio suggested. “Seeing as you look so handsome.”

“Yeah, I’m fine,” Rio replied, but the way she clutched the laptop to her chest said otherwise. Agatha’s bullshit senses were tingling.

“Is there something on that laptop you don’t want me to see?”

“N-no.”

Agatha stood up and held out her hand. “Give it to me.”

Rio hugged it tighter. “Why?”

“Because you’re hiding something, and I want to know what.”

“It’s nothing bad,” Rio insisted. “I mean it might look bad, but its not. I promise.”

Possibilities raced through Agatha’s brain, from elicit chat rooms to a secret criminal empire. “I’d like to see for myself.”

Shoulders slumped in defeat, Rio handed over the laptop. Agatha opened it, finding it had been locked.

“Password?”

Rio mumbled something she couldn’t quite make out.

“Sorry, what?”

“Agatha123, with a capitol A.”

Agatha shook her head as she typed in the password. Her finger hovered over the enter button. A part of her didn’t want to know, to carry on ignorant bliss, but she knew she couldn’t. She clicked the button, and an image filled the screen.

An image of her and Wanda at an event. The ‘Writers of the Future’ gala if she wasn’t mistaken.

Her heart sank. “Oh, my love.”

Rio dropped down defeatedly to sit on the edge of the bed, and Agatha moved to sit beside her, the laptop resting in her lap.

“Honey, why were you looking at this?”

“I found it by accident,” Rio admitted. “I was looking up Wanda. I know it was stupid, and now I wish I never had, because now all I can think about is that stupid photo.”

Agatha looked at the photograph with a frown. “Why?”

“Because you look so happy there, and so glamorous, and Wanda is so successful and beautiful that, I don’t know, I don’t quite feel eno-”

“Don’t you dare finish that sentence,” Agatha told her. “You’re more than enough, Rio. You’re everything.”

“But I’m not,” Rio said so harshly it made Agatha flinch, and when she looked into those beautiful brown eyes, she found them glazed with tears. “Maybe one day I’ll be a semi-successful botanist that’ll make an okay salary and will be remembered in a hundred years as a footnote in my stepmother’s wiki page. Wanda, she has all these awards…”

“Her company almost went bankrupt three times when we were together, and she had to borrow money to keep it afloat. Most of those awards are thanks to people she’s worked with, not herself, and most importantly I don’t love her. I love you. I’m stupidly in love with you. We could have nothing, and I wouldn’t care.”

Rio gave her sceptically.

“Okay, maybe I would care, but you know what I mean.” Agatha looked at the photo. “That was one photo from that night. I don’t even remember what we found so funny, but I do remember the blazing argument we had on the way home and that I slept on the couch for two nights after.”

“What was the argument about?” Rio asked, at which Agatha laughed bitterly.

“At that point, we were arguing over everything and anything. I think it was the time I put my hand on a woman’s forearm. An old work friend, no less.”

Looking back, she couldn’t blame Wanda for wanting to leave. She perhaps wanted to as well but was too settled to admit it even to herself. That was no excuse for her betrayal though, nor her recent behaviour.

“I’m terrified of losing you,” Rio admitted. “I don’t know how to live without you anymore.”

“That’ll never happen.” Agatha took her hand and squeezed it tight. “Nothing will break us apart. I won’t let it, and you know how stubborn I can be.”

Rio chuckled, before looking up at her with uncertain eyes. “Agatha?”

“Yes, my love?”

Rio stared at her for a moment, her mouth slightly agape, prepared to say whatever words that had stuck themselves in her throat. Then, like a flick of a switch, she smiled widely and reached over to close the image tab of the search engine.

“What film shall we watch?”

The Meetings

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! thanks for all the comments and kudos! hope you enjoy this new chapter! still ill so sorry for any mistakes.

Agatha was beginning to hate Mondays.

For starters, it meant her uninterrupted time with Rio was over, which always sucked. Then there was the backlog of emails that she was beginning to task Sharon with more often than not because she had lost interest in reading them all, and the fresh pile of manuscripts that were mostly below par…

Oh, and she had to see Wanda Maximoff. That was the main issue.

That Monday morning there was a meeting between all the top players. Unfortunately, she made the cut.  She arrived at the conference room early and made herself a coffee, before selecting a seat at the far end of the table. Her plan was to nod along and bite her tongue long enough to get through the hour without a formal complaint being made about her attitude.

She’d been told she was one strike away from a mindfulness course and that was NOT happening.

More people started filtering in soon after, choosing to sit either at the front, eager for brownie points, or in the happy middle. Some tried to sit by her, but she shot them a glare and they quickly left her alone. She hated them all with a passion simply for the fact it was 9am and they weren’t her girlfriend.

To her, that was a good enough reason.

Wanda arrived surprisingly (annoyingly) promptly, and the air shift in the room upon her entrance. Everyone else looked at her adoringly, eager to earn the attention of the company’s new golden girl. Yet, of course, Wanda only had eyes for her. Their eyes had met almost instantly, but Agatha had quickly looked down at her phone.

Rio had a meeting with her thesis advisor that morning, and she didn’t want to bother her, so instead she shot Jen a message.

AGATHA

Come up for air yet?

JEN

You’re one to talk! I can’t wait to catch up. When are you free to go outfit shopping for Friday?

AGATHA

Rio and Alice have an appointment Wednesday, so tomorrow? I’d say we could get dinner all together after, but we’re going to Rebecca’s.

JEN

Why don’t you and Rio come round to mine on Wednesday then? I’ll do one of my famous tapas and wine nights.

AGATHA

Famous is pushing it, but fine.

JEN

Great, I’ll message in the chat later for tapas suggestions.

AGATHA

Rio will want dino nuggets

JEN

Wtf?

She saw a flash of red in her peripheral vision, and looked up to see Wanda had taken the spot opposite her. There were still plenty of extra seats, much better for someone who will most likely be at the centre of the meeting’s agenda. But no, she had to sit right opposite her with those pesky green eyes and irritating smile, which only grew when Agatha glared at her.

Before she could attempt to speak to her, however, Wanda’s attention was pulled elsewhere.

“Hey Wanda, did you have a good weekend?”

“I did, thank you.” Wanda’s voice was so sweet it made Agatha want to gag. “Did you?”

“Yes, just same old same old,” the person, a manager in another department whose name Agatha hadn’t bothered to remember, continued. “Did you get up to anything?”

“It was my weekend with the twins, so we had some quality time at the zoo.”

“Oh, that sounds amazing! How old are they?”

“Three in a few months.”

Agatha blinked. Had it been that long already?

“That’s adorable!” the busy-body manager gushed. “What are their names? Did you give them matching ones?”

Wanda chuckled. “No. Seeing as there were two of them, we decided to name one each. Their dad wanted to name one after his dad, so he named one Tommy.”

Agatha tried not to listen. She had guessed long ago, when she gave a fuck what Wanda was doing, that one of her twins had to be called Pietro, in honour of her brother. She didn’t need that confirming. Instead, she checked her news app and took a sip of her coffee.

“And what name did you choose?”

“Billy.”

Agatha jolted in her seat, chocking on the hot liquid stuck in her throat.

Everyone looked her way, both in confusion and concern. Everyone except Wanda. No, she had the infuriating ability to keep her face totally blank to the rest of the world, while allowing Agatha to read it like a book.

This one spelled amusement, and Agatha wanted to punch her in the face.

Yet she couldn’t. She had to play ball.

And so, she put on a look of exasperation and held up her phone. “Ain’t the news just crap these days.”

Rio sat awkwardly in her chair, watching as her advisor read over the new draft of her thesis.

Doctor Odinsdottir was the best lecturer in the college, if Rio said so herself, though she had been taking a break from academia to work on a new project that took her back to her native Scandinavia. Yet, despite her sabbatical, the acclaimed botanist had insisted on still being Rio’s thesis advisor.

Most of the time, they spoke over teams or by email, but the proclaimed professor was back in town for a while and wanted to meet face to face.

Though Rio had always gotten on well with the professor, and had thrived under her mentorship, she was still nervous. Nervous she would disappoint her somehow. That it wouldn’t be good enough and the person she had looked up to for almost ten years would see her as nothing but a failure.

Hela leaned back in her chair and closed her laptop, before meeting Rio’s anxious gaze with her masterful poker face.

“Well?” Rio prompted. “Is it okay?”

Hela tapped her fingers against the top of her laptop. “Is it okay? No.”

Rio’s heart dropped. She knew it. She’d let herself slip. Lilia had warned her. Agatha had warned her. She had been too busy masterminding a fake relationship and falling in real love with her fake girlfriend that she’d let all those years of work fall to the wayside.  That was it. It was ever. She’d never graduate. She’d never work in botany. She’d never…

Hela’s lips grew into a smile, a mischievous gleam glistening in those ice blue eyes.  “It’s great. Seriously, I’d even be proud of writing this.”

“Really?”

Hela nodded. “I can’t wait to show this to my colleagues. Seriously, this could lead to some groundbreaking stuff.”

Rio couldn’t help but grin. “That’s amazing, Hela. Thank you.”

“No, thank you. And I must say, it reads really well. No spelling mistakes at all.”

“My girlfriend makes me read it to her and she tells me when things don’t sound right,” Rio explained. “She doesn’t get the scientific stuff, though. She’s more on the artsy side.”

Hela smirked. “A girlfriend? About time. What’s her name?”

“Agatha.” Rio got out her phone and showed off her phone screen. “She works in publishing.”

“She’s a catch, but is treating you okay?”

“No complaints at all.”

“I’m glad.” Hela then opened the laptop again and began tapping away at something. “I have to give you something to work on, so I’ll give you one piece of advice. A way to make this stand out from the rest.”

Rio leaned forward. “Tell me and I’ll do it.”

“Add that personal touch.”

“That what?” Rio frowned.

“Remember when you were in freshman year and you came to me wanting to join my already full class?”

Rio remembered. She had been so desperate to join the class that she had sought after the professor during her office hours to plead her case. It had taken some persuading, but Hela had eventually agreed, and when she finished top of the class by a mile, she soon became Doctor Odindottir’s little protégé.

“You came to me, and you said you wanted to join the class,” Hela recalled. “You told me how interested you were, and I was a little disappointed you had been shut out, but most of the class were juniors and seniors. I couldn’t move heaven and earth so an eager freshman could sit lost at the back. Then you told me your name, and I asked you…”

“You knew what happened to my mom,” Rio concluded. “And you asked me why I wanted to take this class after that happened to her.”

Hela nodded. “And what did you say?”

Rio swallowed harshly. “I wanted to make sure no one made that mistake again.”

The professor leaned back in her chair. “There you go.”

“I don’t understand?”

“Your research has a reason, a purpose in the grand scope of things. Yet sharing what this means to you, sharing how this could prevent such a horrible thing from happening again. I think that would be…”

“Exploitative?” Rio suggested. “I have to be honest, I don’t feel comfortable with this.”

Hela held her hands up. “I’m just giving a suggestion. And it’s not exploitative. It’s real, and it’s what makes you a good botanist. Because for you, this is personal.”

Rio considered the professor’s words. She understood, of course she did, but the thought made her stomach lurch. It just didn’t…she didn’t…it was too complicated.

“Just think about it,” Hela suggested. “Shall we meet against next week? Perhaps grab lunch?”

Rio nodded. “Lunch sounds good.”

“Can you believe her?”

“I certainly can’t,” Sharon replied. “What a strange young lady.”

Agatha had been in a fowl mood after the meeting. The events before it even began had already soured her, yet the meeting ran over by half an hour which had meant more time under Wanda’s beady gaze. The moment it ended, she bolted out the door without pleasantries or decorum, stomping through the corridors like an intern’s worst nightmare.

Sharon, in her wisdom, had decided a walk would do some good, and they could pick up some lunch along the way. Agatha had bit her tongue for a while, but by the time they’d picked up their boxed lunches (Agatha got a Greek salad and a sandwich for Rio in case she showed up), she desperately had to tell someone what happened.

It seemed her assistant was the perfect sounding board in the absence of Rio, though in a way she was glad her girlfriend wasn’t there. The Wanda stuff was clearly getting to Rio, and Agatha needed to blow off steam before she told her.

“I don’t know what to do,” Agatha said as they stood in the elevator on their way back to the office. “I hate her so much, but I’m stuck with her here.”

“Have you looked for another job?” Sharon suggested. “Surely another publisher would snap you up?”

They would. She got calls all the time trying to scout her, but why should she leave? She had worked her way from the very bottom to get where she was, and why should she leave because Wanda was a clingy little bitch?

“I’m not leaving,” Agatha said with her head held high. “This is my company. I’m not letting it go without a fight.”

Sharon gave her a sympathetic look. “Honey, sometimes letting go of something is better than letting it drag you down. It’s taken me way too long to realise that.”

Agatha didn’t respond, and instead watched the digital display go up and up.

When they made it to their floor, they walked side by side across the floor to their office space. Once they got there, they were surprised to find a pretty brunette loitering by Sharon’s desk.

Agatha smiled and strode ahead, balancing the food in one hand so she could pull Rio into a one-armed hug. “What a wonderful surprise, my love. How was your meeting?”

“Good,” Rio replied. “Well, mostly. What about you?”

Agatha pulled a face, and Rio seemed to read it. She nodded in understanding.

“We need to talk then?”

“Seems so. I got lunch.”

“And I got drinks.” Rio nodded to the three identical iced coffees on Sharon’s desk. “Care to join the venting session, Sharon?”

“Oh no, dear,” Sharon replied as she went to unbutton her coat. “I have a lot to get on with. Agatha has already filled me in on her side of things, anyway.”

“She’s a good listener. She even lets me finish a story without stupi….” Agatha stopped, watching as Rio’s eyes widened, a look of horror appearing on her face. “Rio?”

“We need to talk,” Rio took the food from her and grabbed her arm, pulling her towards the office door. “Bye Sharon.”

“But your coffees!” Sharon protested, and Agatha managed to swipe them up as she went.

Once in the office, Rio dragged Agatha across the office, as far away from the door as they could get. She dumped the food on the coffee table and began to pace the length of the window.

“What is wrong with you?” Agatha scolded while putting the drinks down also. “Why are you being weird?”

Rio ran a stressed hand through her hair. “I’m freaking out. Oh God, this is…oh my God…”

“Rio, speak,” she demanded.

“You know when I heard Lilia having crazy screamy sex with her new hook up?”

“How could I forget? You almost gave me a heart attack that night.”

Rio waved her off. “Remember when I said there was a granny sweater on the floor?”

“Vaguely.”

“Well Sharon is wearing that exact same sweater right now!”

Agatha frowned. “So Sharon shops at the same place as Lilia’s mystery woman?”

Rio just stared at her.

The penny dropped.

Agatha’s hand shot up to cover her mouth. “No!”

“Yes!”

“So she and Lilia are…”

“Having sex.” Rio nodded. “And I fucking heard them!”

Another wave of horror washed over Agatha. “Sharon is the screamer?!”

Rio grimaced. “This is a nightmare! I’m never going to be able to look at her the same again.”

“Me neither,” Agatha admitted.

They stood there in silence, the new information slowly sinking in…

Then, they burst into hysterics.

“It’s not funny,” Rio said though her own laughter. “Please, Agatha, I’m traumatised!”

Agatha sat on the arm of the couch, wiping tears from her eyes. “I’m sorry, Rio, but this is the funniest thing ever.”

“It’s not! I thought Sharon was straight?”

“Sharon herself probably thought she was until Lilia came along,” Agatha mused. “Good for her, I guess.”

Rio nodded in agreement. “Lilia is happy too. It seems like our love just keeps bringing people together. First Jen and Alice, and now Sharon and Lilia.”

“Jen and Alice don’t count. They had no idea we’d met. And if you say it’s that damn invisible string again, I’m kicking you out.”

Rio pouted. “You said you liked Folklore?”

“Shut up and let’s have lunch.”

They settled on the couch, Rio inhaling her sandwich before Agatha had barely got the lid off her salad.

“So how was your meeting with your advisor?”

“It went well. Hela said…”

“Hela?” Agatha raised her eyebrows. “You’re on a first name basis with your professor?”

“Don’t get jealous. She’s married, and I only have eyes for you, my love.”

“Better stay that way, too.”

Rio smirked with amusement. “Anyway, she said my work is good. Really good. There wasn’t any criticism, really.”

“That’s amazing!” Agatha leaned over and kissed her cheek. “So you’re done?”

“No, I still have some data to add, and I…Hela wants me to add something else to it.”

“Oh?”

Rio played with the sandwich wrappings in her lap, and Agatha instantly knew something was up.

“Rio?”

“She wants me to put in about what happened to my mom.”

Oh.

“And you don’t want to?”

Rio shook her head.

“Then don’t.”

“But she said it could make a big difference. I mean, I thought about it on the way here and people are going to heed to the advice knowing it’s been given by someone…” Rio looked down at the wrappings again. “I just don’t want to open all that up again.”

“I understand,” Agatha reached out and squeezed her hand. “No matter what you decide, your thesis is going to save lives, and I couldn’t be prouder to call you my partner.”

“Partner?” Rio’s eyes gleamed. “So I’m not just your girlfriend anymore?”

“You’ve never been just anything to me.”

Rio lifted their joined hands and kissed Agatha’s knuckles, agreeing without the need for words. “What about you? How was your meeting?”

“Besides Wanda casually dropping she named one of her demon spawns after my nephew? Pretty boring.”

Rio dropped her hand. “She what?”

Agatha nodded. “I couldn’t believe it. Why the hell would she do that? I mean it’s a common name, but the coincidence…”

“Was she even close to Billy?”

“No, and that’s what makes this even worse.”

“What’s her game?” Rio questioned, and Agatha shrugged.

“Who knows? But I’m not playing. I just want to focus on the good things, especially my super girlfriend who’s going to take the world of botany by storm.”

Rio smiled, before leaning over to pick at Agatha’s salad. “What’s in this anyway?”

“You don’t know what’s in a Greek salad?”

Agatha had another meeting, but she insisted Rio stay and pointed her towards the staff library on the other side of the floor. It had everything from unabridged editions to advanced reader copies of the company’s best work.  Rio would rather pass the time reading Agatha’s masterpiece, but that was safe in her room under the watchful guard of Webbers, so she had to settle for lesser works.

She was reading the back of one when she heard a voice behind her.

“I enjoyed that one. The twist at the end kept me up at night, though.”

Rio turned to see Wanda stood by one of the other bookshelves, a confident smile gracing her lips.

How she hated that woman’s stupid face.

Rio turned away from her and put the book back.

“Are you mad at me now?” Wanda asked. “We got on so well before.”

“I didn’t know who you were then,” Rio reminded her. “But you played on that, didn’t you?”

“I don’t play,” Wanda replied, at which Rio scoffed.

“Please, all you do is play games.” She turned to face her again. “Like naming your kid after Billy? What? Was Aga thor too on the nose? Or Harker? You could have gotten away with that.”

“Forgive me that I wanted to have something of hers,” Wanda snapped. “I was grieving. I was lost. I made a mistake, and I love my boys, but I never meant to lose her.”

“But you did lose her,” Rio confirmed. “And that sucks for you, but it’s over. Leave us alone.”

“I can’t.”

“Yes, you can.”

Wanda folded her arms. “Could you walk away from her?”

“This isn’t about me.”

“Answer the question,” Wanda pressed. “You say you love her so much, can you honestly say you could walk away from her and never look back?”

Rio tried to stare her down, but her gaze soon dropped to the floor.

“Exactly,” Wanda spoke up again. “You can’t judge me for loving her when you do exactly the same.”

“The difference is I wouldn’t hurt her like you did,” Rio snapped. “I never ever would.”

The amusement had dropped from Wanda’s perky facade, revealing the true face that lay beneath. One that was cold and pained and ruthless. She stepped up to Rio, their identical height making her wild eyes impossible to avoid.

“You don’t want to push me, Rio.”

“And you don’t want to push me,” Rio countered, pure rage causing through her. “You have no idea what I’m capable of, Wanda.”

“Is that a challenge?”

“It’s a threat,” Rio told her. “Leave us alone.”

With that, she grabbed a random book off the shelf and stormed off. She heard Wanda laughter echoing far behind her.

“Nice talking to you, Rio. See you next time.”

The Suit

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! thanks for all the great comments and i'm glad you all appreciated the greek salad reference! hope you enjoy this new chapter!

Agatha decided to take the day off from work. She needed a break from that place before she committed a homicide.

She noticed Rio was off after she got back from her meeting and it had taken much persuading when they got back to the apartment for her to voice what happened. To say Agatha was angry would be an understatement. She was ready to track Wanda down there and then, but then Rio had asked if they could cuddle and watch a movie, and who was she to refuse?

So, instead, she focused on other things. She woke up snuggled with her beautiful girlfriend, had a shower together that was steamy in more ways than one, went to a café for breakfast, and walked Rio to campus before heading off to meet Jen for their shopping visit. Pure perfection.

Or so it was.

Jen waited until they were in the store, searching the racks of dresses and pant suits for the gala that Friday, before she decided to start her meddling.

“So, you, Rio, sex. Discuss.”

“As crudely as you put it, yes. She’s the best I’ve ever had in every way.”

Jen patted her on the back. “I’m so happy for you!”

“Thank you.” Agatha felt a smile pull at her lips. “We’re happy too. If I can only get rid of Wanda, then we’ll be just grand.”

“I can’t believe the audacity of that bitch,” Jen huffed. “I can’t wait to see her on Friday. I’m going to spill red wine down her dress.”

“Dance with me, my love.”

Rio smiled and took her hand gladly. She allowed Agatha to lead her back onto the dancefloor, and as firm hands grasped her hips, she hooked her hands behind her girlfriend’s neck, letting her sway them to the music.

“I saw them once,” Agatha said over the music. “They’re one of my favourite bands.”

“So you don’t just like it because of TikTok?”

“What?”

Rio chuckled and shook her head. “I love you.”

Agatha grinned. “I love you too.”

They shared a sweet kiss, and Rio savoured it as if it was her last. She never took a moment with Agatha for granted, but she wanted to cherish this one more than usual.

When they pulled apart, she found Agatha’s eyes studying her face. “Is everything okay?”

“What do you mean?” Rio kept on a smile. “I’m great.”

“Are you sure?” Agatha pressed. “Because you and Alice have been acting kind of weird. Jen and I are a bit worried.”

“Don’t be,” Rio quickly insisted. “We’re fine.”

“Are you su-”

“Did you mean what you said before?” Rio asked. “About wanting to be Mrs Harkness-Vidal?”

“Rio, we’re already planning to have kids. Of course I want to marry you.”

“Then let’s do it.”

Agatha blinked at her. “What?”

“Let’s go get married. Right now.”

“Are you joking around? Because that isn’t funny.”

“No, I’m serious,” Rio insisted. “Let’s get married.”

Agatha stared at her for a moment before shaking her head. “No, Rio. Somethings not right and you’re not telling me.”

“So you don’t want to marry me?”

“I never said that.”

“Then let’s go.”

“Rio…”

“Well, well, well,” a familiar voice said beside them. “Aren’t you two just adorable.”

Rio tore her eyes away from Agatha to shoot Wanda a fiery glare. “Get lost.”

Wanda gasped in offense, placing a hand over her heart. “Excuse me for wanting to make conversation with my colleague and her partner.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Wanda, we’re dancing.”

“It’s a social event, Agatha,” Wanda pointed out. “You need to socialize with people other than your friends and…her.”

“Wanda,” Agatha warned. “You said you weren’t going to do this tonight.”

“Like she ever wasn’t going to,” Rio grumbled.

Wanda pursed her lips. “How about we talk somewhere more private?” She stole a disgusted look at Rio. “Minus the date.”

Rio scoffed. “That’s so not happening. So do you mind getting the fuck away. We’re busy here.”

Wanda looked Rio up and down. “I’m sure you are, dressed like that. Practically draping yourself over her like a wh-”

Rio pulled away from Agatha. “You want to finish that sentence?”

Agatha yanked her back. “Just ignore her.”

“Ignore her?” Rio questioned, loud enough for people to look their way. “I’ve had enough of her bullshit, Agatha. I’m so fucking done with it.”

“Me too,” Agatha agreed in a quieter tone. “Just not here, honey. Please.”

Rio relented and put an arm around her. “Let’s get out of here.”

They started to walk off, and Rio couldn’t wait to leave. To get out of that damn gala, away from Wanda and the secret she now shared with her sister. Back to Agatha’s, where she was safe. Where the outside world didn’t matter. Where it was just them, and nothing else.

Besides Scratchy of course, but he was no trouble.

She was so close to walking away. So close to the end of a horrible night. But that fucking voice had to pipe up again.

“You know, she was never embarrassed of me.”

Rio swirled round. She couldn’t help herself. She just saw red.

It was like she was in her body, but unable to control it. One moment she had her arm around Agatha, and the next she was storming back. She saw her arm swing, before feeling the sharp collision of her fist against Wanda Maximoff’s face.

Wanda fell to the ground with a thump, accompanied by gasps from all around. The music cut off, and suddenly the room was still.

“Rio!” Agatha raced to her side. “Are you okay?”

Rio raised her hand and saw she’d cut a knuckle. Shit, shit, shit.

Her gaze fell to the ground, where Wanda lay, clutching her cheek.

People came running over, kneeling beside Wanda to check she was alright. The suits came running through, all startled and confused. One of which was Mike the Sleezebag.

He knelt beside Wanda like a fucking knight and took her hand. “Wanda, are you okay?”

“Do I fucking look okay?!” she cried. “That mad bitch hit me!”

Mike stood and looked to her, then to Agatha. His face was set in a stern glower. “What the hell is this?”

The panic hit her like a freight train.

She’d messed up again.

She’d done something bad.

She needed to leave.

She needed to run.

And so, she did.

“Rio!”

Agatha raced out of the doors after her. She’d left the scene behind without a thought. She didn’t bother with their coats, or bags, or anything. All that mattered was Rio. Her lovely, caring, compassionate Rio who was in total crisis.

She managed to catch up with her on the sidewalk, grasping her by the shoulders. “Rio, wait.”

Rio pulled from her touch quickly but didn’t run. She faced her, cheeks stained with tears.

“You need to go back inside, Agatha.”

“I’m not going anywhere.” She moved to step towards her, but Rio staggered backwards. Agatha held up her hands. “It’s okay, Rio. You’re with me. We can fix this. Everything will be fine.”

It was a lie. There was no good way of fixing this other than begging Wanda to not press assault charges. The rest, well, the rest didn’t matter in that moment. Only Rio mattered.

Fresh tears fell down Rio’s face. “You don’t understand, Agatha. I’m bad. I’m really bad.”

“No, you’re not,” Agatha insisted. “You did what I’ve wanted to do for weeks. We get mad sometimes, and it was just a punch…”

“No, you don’t understand .” Rio’s breathing got heavier, her body shaking with the tidal wave of tears that took over her. “I’ve always been bad.”

“No, you ha-”

“I didn’t mean to,” Rio sobbed. “You have to believe me, Agatha. I loved her. I loved her so much. I didn’t mean to hurt her.”

Agatha frowned. “Honey, I don’t understand. Are we still talking about-”

Rio hugged her arms around herself and sobbed impossibly harder. “I thought they were pretty flowers.”

Agatha was completely lost. “Honey, what flowers?”

“She always used pretty flowers. She looked so sad that I was going, and I wanted to make her smile. I put them in the pot when she wasn’t looking. I wanted it to be a surprise.”

Oh.

Agatha understood.

Tears prickled her eyes. “Oh, honey.”

“I didn’t know what it was, Agatha. I didn’t. I didn’t. I didn’t.”

“You didn’t,” Agatha agreed, taking a step forward. “You didn’t mean to. I know you didn’t.”

She reached for Rio, but she flinched away.

“Agatha, I can’t. I can’t.”

“Let’s go home,” Agatha encouraged, trying to stay calm while her heart beat hard in her chest. “Let’s talk properly there.”

“I’m bad,” Rio said again. “I’ve ruined everything.”

“You haven’t ruined anything,” Agatha insisted. “I love you. Nothing else matters.”

Rio stared at her for a moment before shaking her head. “No, no, I can’t. Agatha, I can’t…”

“You can.” Agatha reached forward to touch her arm, to take her hand. “I lo-”

Rio pushed her away. “No!”

Agatha fell backwards.

She tried to brace herself with her hand, but the fall was too harsh. A sharp pain ran up her arm.

“Fuck!” She tried to sit up, but she couldn’t. The pain was too much.

Rio stood over her, eyes wide with horror. “Agatha…”

“Agatha!” A rush of footsteps approached them, and soon Jen was stood between them.

“Get the hell away from her!”

“Jen!” Agatha cried, her voice mingling with Alice’s identical cry.

Rio staggered backwards. “I’m sorry. I’m sorry, I’d never…”

“Bullshit!” Jen snapped. “I saw you! You pushed her!”

“Jen, no,” Agatha tried to sit up, only to wince again. Jen whirled round to look at her, while Alice knelt at her side.

“Is it your arm?”

“I’m fine.”

“You’re hurt.” It was a statement, not a question, but Agatha still shook her head.

“I’m fine.” She looked up to Rio. “Rio, I’m fine.”

Rio stared at her, her face etched with a sadness to pure for her to stomach.

Jen stepped up to Rio. “You get the hell out of here right now!”

“Jen, no. She didn’t…”

But it was too late. Rio darted off, faster than before, disappearing into the night.

“Shit!” Alice jumped to her feet and raced after her. “Rio!”

Jen moved to kneel beside Agatha. “Let me help you up.”

Agatha slapped her hand away. “You’ve done enough, Kale.”

More footsteps approached, and Lilia and Sharon came into view. Sharon was beside her in an instant and helped her sit up. “Are you hurt?”

Agatha went to say no, but Jen beat her to it.

“She’s hurt her left hand.”

Agatha glared at her, only to wince when Sharon touched the hand in question.

“Oh Agatha, I think we need to get you to a hospital.”

“No, Rio…”

“I’ll go find them,” Lilia insisted, stepping to the curb to hail a taxi. “But you need to get that checked.”

Sharon wrapped an arm around her. “It’ll be okay, sweetie. It’ll all be okay.”

Agatha let the tears flow. In that moment, she couldn’t see anything being okay ever again.

The Day After

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! sorry again about the last chapter! i'm afraid this is another angsty one, but i hope you enjoy anyway.

Her wrist wasn’t broken, just a bit of bruising and some muscle strain. The doctor said she was lucky. A fall like that could have ended with her snaping her arm.

Agatha didn’t feel lucky. Not at all.

“I’ll make you something to drink,” Sharon said as she and Jen followed Agatha into her apartment. “Then why don’t you get into bed?”

Agatha didn’t respond. She had her phone to her ear. The line rang and rang, but Rio didn’t pick up. She cursed under her breath and ended the call. “Pick up, Rio. Please.”

“Agatha, come sit down,” Jen pleaded. “You’ve still hurt yourself.”

Her wrist did still hurt, but it was nothing compared to the pain in her heart.

She glared at Jen. “Call Alice.”

Jen frowned. “Why can’t you?”

“Because you’re the one who got us into this mess,” Agatha snapped.

“Me? What about your psycho girlfriend?”

“Don’t call her a psycho!”

“She pushed you!”

“It was an accident!”

“Okay, enough.” Sharon stepped between them. “Jen, call Alice and see what’s happening. Agatha, please just sit down for two minutes.”

Both women did as they were asked, and as Jen stepped into the bedroom to call her girlfriend, Agatha accepted the cup of hot cocoa Sharon handed her and slumped onto the couch.

Sharon sat beside her and placed a comforting hand on her shoulder. “I hate seeing you so sad.”

“I hate being so sad,” Agatha admitted. “Thanks for looking after me.”

“You don’t have to thank me, hun.”

Agatah looked down at her cup of cocoa. “She won’t answer my calls, Sharon. I don’t know what to do.”

“Just give her some time to cool off. She loves you so much. She’ll call you back and all this will be sorted.”

Agatha looked up at her hopefully. “You think?”

Sharon nodded. “You two belong together. You’ll find a way back to each other.”

Agatha smiled. “Our invisible string.” She looked to Sharon and saw she was confused. “It’s something Rio says. She says we were always tied by a string that led us to each other.”

“Then have faith it’ll work again.”

Jen walked back into the room. “Alice said that Rio is fine and resting. She’s going to keep me updated. She said to give them space.”

Agatha took a sip of her cocoa. It was still too hot, but she didn’t care. She enjoyed the burn.

“Maybe you should get to sleep,” Sharon suggested. “Let yourself rest, so you can look at everything fresh in the morning.”

Agatha shook her head. “I don’t think I can.”

Rio hadn’t slept.

Alice had tried to calm her down. She’d insisted on taking her back to her apartment and snuggled up on the bed with her. Like they did when they were kids.

Alice kept saying she was sorry, but Rio didn’t speak. She couldn’t. Her whole life had fallen apart in the space of ten minutes and now she had nothing.

In the end, she pretended to sleep. She just lay there, numb, listening for the door. Wanda was going to call the police if she hadn’t already. She was sure of it. A part of her hoped she would. She just wanted it all to be over.

It was early morning when the knock came, and Alice jumped off the bed to answer it. She heard Lilia’s voice in the living room and Rio sat up in time to see both women enter the room.

“Hello you.” Lilia sat on the bed and held out her little purse. “You left this.”

Rio took the bag with a weak smile. “Thanks.”

“You’re welcome.” Lilia looked between her and Alice. “Now, will one of you tell me what the hell went on last night.”

“It’s really complicated,” Alice began. “A lot happened, and I don’t think one thing, or person, was totally to blame for what hap-”

“I killed my mom.”

Lilia eyes snapped to her. “What?”

Rio sucked in a sharp breath. “She put flowers in her tea. You know, to make an infusion. She was good with plants. She grew all kinds for people to buy, and I’d help her in the nurseries when I was with her. It was all at the back of our house. She’d gotten a bit of money in the divorce and bought some land. She always told me to explore but to stay out of the little greenhouse. It was important I didn’t go in there.”

“My mom wrote that she was growing plants for a local college lab,” Alice added. “Things weren’t as strict back then. Not as much red tape.”

“Anyway, there were these white flowers. I used to look at them through the glass, but the door was always locked, so I could never go in. Anyway, Mom was getting me ready to go to my dad’s and, I don’t know, I guess she was sad. She hated it when I left. I wanted to cheer her up, so I went to find her some flowers. The greenhouse must have been open or something, I can’t remember, and I got the plant and managed to throw it in the tea she was brewing on the hob.”

Lilia reached out to take her hand. Rio braced herself and continued.

“I got a nasty rash over my hands and my dad took me to hospital. The doctor gave me some stuff to help but told my dad to keep me away from poisonous plants. He got mad that my mom had let me near them, so went to confront her. That’s when he found her.”

“Oh love.”

“My dad and Lorna put two and two together, so asked me if I’d put anything in the tea. I said yes, but I was too little. I didn’t understand what I’d done. They decided to keep it between them, so I wouldn’t have to live with the guilt. Then when I was fifteen, we were on tour, and we got taken on some nature walk by our hosts. Alice and I were messing around, and I fell into some poison ivy. Lorna insisted I see a doctor, and while I was there, he noted I had a similar case in my notes from when I was six. By then, I didn’t remember that. I was too little, but I remembered that weekend. I remembered my mom had died because she ingested large quantities of Lily of the Valley. I researched it, and touching the roots cause irritation. I confronted my dad about it, and he told me the truth.”

“And you’ve had to live with that?” Lilia asked. “All these years?”

Rio nodded. “I was already interested in plants, but then it became my mission to educate people. To stop another little kid being able to do what I did. I know it can never make up for what happened, but I was trying. I really was. I hated myself, and I did for so long. I can’t change what I did. I wish I could. I wish I could more than anything.”

Lilia reached over and pulled her into a hug. “I know, my dear. I know.”

“And now I don’t know what to do.” Fresh tears began to fall. “Alice found out through Lorna’s journals and we talked about it last night…”

Lilia looked to Alice. “You couldn’t have just spoken to her another time?”

Alice hung her head in shame. “I’m sorry. I know I reacted badly. I just…what bothered me more was that she hid it from me.”

“Of course she hid it,” Lilia snapped. “And now look what you’ve done.”

“She didn’t do anything,” Rio insisted. “I did. I killed my mom. I kept the secret. I punched Wanda. I…I hurt Agatha.”

“No, you didn’t,” Alice insisted. “We all saw you were just trying to keep her back.”

“Jen didn’t.”

“Well Jen is an idiot,” Alice stated firmly. “I love her, but she was out of line.”

“No, I…”

“I think everything got way out of hand last night,” Lilia settled, before pointing to the bag. “Now, that thing has been going off like crazy, so you better check it.”

Rio opened the bag

53 missed calls from Agatha

AGATHA

Rio answer your phone!!

AGATHA

Rio please I’m really worried

AGATHA

I love you please talk to me.

“Jen said she’s back home but wants to see you,” Alice told her. “She’s totally fine.”

“There you go,” Lilia grinned. “Call her back and everything will be alright!”

Rio stared at the messages, and a sickening feeling rose in her gut. Perhaps Agatha was okay now, but how long would that last? She was a disaster. A cursed disaster who just seemed to do nothing but hurt the people she loved most. And she loved Agatha more than anything.

She couldn’t do this.

She opened Agatha’s contract information and scrolled down to find those harsh red letters: Block Caller. Rio pressed the button before tossing her phone aside.

“Rio!” Alice gasped. “Why did you do that?”

“I can’t be near her.”

“You can’t just shut her out,” Lilia argued. “You need to just take a moment and…”

“I’ve taken enough moments,” Rio insisted. “I hurt her. It’s over.”

“Rio…”

“No,” she snapped. “It’s done.”

Alice and Lilia shared a concerned look, but didn’t argue. Not that it would have made a damn bit of difference.

She would never hurt Agatha again. This was her way of making sure of that.

“Rio!” Agatha banged her fist against the apartment door. It was mid-morning, and her patience had worn thin. “Rio, open the door and speak to me, right now!”

She tried the phone again, but it wasn’t even connecting now, and her texts kept bouncing back. Which either meant she’d busted her phone, or she’d blocked her. She suspected the latter, and Agatha wasn’t having it.

She slammed her hand against the door. “Rio, if you’re going to break up with me you can do it to my face!”

“Agatha?”

She looked round to see Lilia approaching her from the stairs.

“Lilia, I need to speak to Rio.”

“She’s not here,” Lilia told her. “She’s at Alice’s.”

“Right, what’s her address?”

“I can’t tell you.”

Agatha folded her arms. “Why not?”

Lilia’s shoulders slumped. “Come inside.”

Agatha followed her into the apartment and stood by while Lilia put away her coat away, before they both sat at the dining table.

“Is she okay?” Agatha asked first.

“She’s…it’s a lot, Agatha. Years of pain and hurt have just collapsed onto her. She needs time.”

“I know, Lilia, but I need to see her. She won’t talk to me, and she’s blocked my number. I just want to be there for her. I mean, we’re pretty much engaged. She can’t just ghost me like this!”

Lilia gave her a sad smile. “I know you want to see her, and Alice and I think she’s making a mistake, but she thinks that…she doesn’t want to hurt you. This is her way of making sure of that.”

“But she’s hurting me now!”

“I know, but she’s so low she can’t see straight. Just be patient. Perhaps she will see reason once things calm down. Has there been any news about Wanda?”

Agatha shook her head. That side of things had also been radio silent.

“Lets hope it stays that way.” Lilia reached for something at the end of the table “Now, I believe this is yours.”

It was the manuscript. The manuscript Rio had amended, with a promise for the future scribbled on the front. A future that may no longer exist.

Tears stung at her eyes. “I love her so much, Lilia.”

“I know, my dear. I know.”

Agatha headed back to her apartment and decided to call Rebecca. Her sister answered after two rings.

“Hey, how was the gala?”

Agatha sucked in a breath. “Rebecca, can I stay at your place tonight?”

“Why? What’s wrong?”

A tear trailed down her cheek. “I think me and Rio broke up.”

“Oh.” She heard her sister rummaging around on the other end. “I’ll come pick you up.”

“No, Rebecca.”

“You’re not driving all that way on your own. Just get yourself and that rabbit of yours ready, okay? I’m setting off now.”

“Thanks, Rebecca.”

“Anytime,” her sister insisted. “Now go pack a bag!”

Rebecca arrived quicker than she expected, greeting her at the front of the building with a big hug. “My big sister.”

Agatha grimaced and pulled away. “I may be heartbroken, but we’re not doing that.”

“Fine. Look, I hope you’re not mad, but I didn’t come alone.”

“What?” Agatha watched as the passenger door opened and Billy jumped out. He raced around the car to hug her tight.

“I’m sorry,” he said into her hair. “I overheard Mom on the phone, and I had to come get you.”

Agatha closed her eyes and held him tight. This was the hug she needed.

Alice ordered take-out, but Rio couldn’t eat. All she could do was stare at the TV, her eyes not comprehending what was on it. Her mind was too busy torturing her.

Agatha in her gala suit.

Agatha in the botanical gardens.

Agatha smiling down at her as she straddled her waist.

Agatha with Senõr Scratchy.

Agatha stepping up at the coffee shop to save the day.

Agatha laid on the sidewalk, pain etched on her face.

Rio blinked the memories away and checked her phone. Lilia had messaged her, asking if she was okay, and Jen had sent a half apology, half telling off message that she chose to ignore. As she read through an email from the college about lab protocol, an Instagram message popped up.

From Billy.

Rio tensed. Why had he messaged her? Did he know?

“Hey, you okay?” Alice asked beside her.

“I’m fine,” Rio insisted, before opening up the message.

BILLY

Why won’t you talk to Agatha?

Rio bit her lip, trying to think of the best way to explain this to a teenage boy. In the end, she used the cop-out.

RIO

It’s complicated.

His reply came quickly.

BILLY

You promised you wouldn’t hurt her.

RIO

I didn’t mean to.

BILLY

I really liked you. I thought you’d make her happy. Now you’re ghosting her? Why would you do that?

A tear trailed down her cheek.

RIO

I don’t want to hurt her anymore.

BILLY

I hate you.

She tried to reply, but Billy had blocked her account.

Rio searched up Agatha’s account. Her girlfriend hadn’t used it much, but there were enough photos on there for her to look at.

She didn’t bother with the ones of them together. She didn’t want to see her own face. Instead, she looked at the pictures she knew Billy had made her post. Selfies of them together, Agatha the proud aunt beside her much-loved nephew. Rio looked at both of them. She loved Agatha, but she’d grown to love the Kaplans too. Especially Billy.

Another person she’d now hurt.

Rio put her phone aside and looked to Alice. “I made a mistake, didn’t I? I should have called Agatha back.”

“You still could.”

“I don’t want to hurt her.”

Alice rolled her eyes. “For fuck sake, Rio. Enough. You know the way you hurt people most? This avoidance shit. Thinking you’re sparing their feelings by keeping something from them or keeping yourself from them. You love her, she loves you. She clearly wants to see you. Fucking call her.”

Rio looked at her phone. “Okay, you’re right.”

“Exactly! Call her now!”

“I will. After whatever this is. Is that Tom Cruise?”

“You’re not even watching,” Alice accused. “I could hear your brain ticking from over here.”

“Okay but just give me a minute. I need to think of what I’m going to say.”

“Fine, but the more you put it off, the harder it’ll be.”

Rio knew this was going to be hard either way, but she’d push through it. For Agatha, even if it was to hear her voice one las time.

Agatha sat on the floor in her sister’s guest room. The room she had once lived in for weeks, months even. Back then, she spent a lot of time in that very spot, the cool floor stabilizing her panic. Those days had been so uncertain, from not knowing if Billy would ever wake up to wondering if he would ever remember them again.

This time, she was nursing an aching heart.

Rio. The one person she’d ever given her whole heart to, her whole body, her whole soul. The love of her life. Her entire future. And just like that, she’d ran away.

Agatha had tried to understand it all. Her panic, Wanda, the truth about her mom…

Just thinking about that last part made her feel sick. She could picture the photograph in Rio’s room of her and her mom. Tiny Rio, with her little grin. Tiny Rio, who made a mistake, and now Big Rio was breaking at the seams.

She wanted to be there for her, to hold her. To stay by her side, for better and for worst. But Rio had pushed her away, had put up a wall of people and technology to her from getting close.

Agatha wanted forever, but in that moment, she would take ten minutes. To talk, to try persuading her not to give up, or at the very least to say goodbye.

There was a light knock at the door. She smiled, knowing exactly who it was.

“Come on in.”

The door creaked open, and Billy slipped inside, already in his plaid pyjamas. She guessed by the way he tiptoed that his parents had gone to bed, and really, he should be at least pretending to sleep in his own room.

He went over to wave at Scratchy in his cage, before sitting on the floor beside her. “You okay?”

Agatha shrugged. “What does okay even mean?”

“I don’t know,” Billy admitted. “I used to say it a lot after the accident. It’s easier than being specific.”

“Yeah.”

“No word from Rio?”

She shook her head. “I’ll wait a little longer.”

Billy bowed his head. “I hate her.”

“No, you don’t.”

“I do. I told her so.”

Agatha sat up. “What? When?”

“Instagram.”

She’d forgotten about that!

She went to get up, to grab her phone, to send another message, but Billy touched her arm.

“Please don’t.”

Agatha frowned. “What do you mean?”

Billy fished out his phone and opened his camera roll. “I screenshot our conversation before I blocked her.”

He showed her the screen, and Agatha read over the messages. “Billy, you shouldn’t get involved.”

“I know, but I hate seeing you like this. I don’t want you with someone who can just cut you off like this. Like Eddie did to me.”

“Rio isn’t Eddie.”

“No, she’s worse.”

Agatha frowned. “How so?”

Billy looked to her, his eyes glistening with tears. “Because she didn’t just make you love her.”

“Oh Billy.” She wrapped an arm around his shoulders and pulled him close. “I’m sorry.”

“You have nothing to sorry about.”

“No, I was ridiculous. I shouldn’t have let you two get so close so quickly.”

“You thought she was the one,” Billy argued. “Right from the beginning. I could tell!”

Agatha sighed. She wanted to scream the truth. That it hadn’t been real, until it was. Yet she could see he was upset, and she hated to see him like this. The look on his face brought back memories of searching the streets at 2am and consoling him as he cried and cried.

It was that look that ignited a fire inside her.

“Well, if Rio wants to ghost me, I’ll ghost her back.”

“Agatha?” Billy sat up. “What do you mean?”

Agatha reached for her phone and opened Rio’s contact details. She hovered her thumb over the block button, the image of Rio’s sweet smile flashing before her eyes. It hurt like a knife through the chest, but instead of sorrow, the pain turned to anger.
