She pressed the button, before blocking her Instagram also, cutting off Rio completely.

Agatha held her head high. Two could play at this game, and she would always win.

Rio threw her phone down. The call had cut off. She knew what that meant.

Sitting on the floor at the foot of Alice’s bed, she leant her head back against the mattress.

She’d waited too long, and now it was done.

The Locket

Chapter Notes

hi everyone. i want to say thank you to all the nice comments people have left on this fic. for those of you who i know from twitter/x/whatever, you'll know why i've taken a while to update this fic and i thank you all for your support.
i hope you enjoy this chapter.

Agatha entered Mike’s office with a black coffee in her hand and her head held high. Despite the fact she had barely slept for three nights and that her heart felt like a brick weighing down her chest, she went in with a strong front. After all, she was ready for a fight.

Mike was sat at his desk, reading something on his computer. He looked up when he heard her enter and gestured to the seat opposite him. “Agatha, please sit.”

Agatha sat down, putting her coffee on the desk before her. “Well, come on then. Tell me how this is going to go.”

Mike sighed and sat up. “Agatha, I know this wasn’t your fault, but something needs to be done.”

“I know.”

“It was a physical assault.”

“I know.”

“Is that all you have to say?”

Agatha shrugged. “I don’t know what you expect me to say.”

Mike shook his head. “I don’t understand what’s going on between you and Wanda, and I’m sure there was some reason for Friday’s ruckus, but what your girlfriend did....”

“She’s not my girlfriend,” Agatha said quickly. It was the first time she’d admitted it to someone else, and to herself. It hurt more than she thought it would. “Not anymore.”

Mike blinked at her in surprise before smiling. “That’s brilliant news!”

Agatah folded her arms. “Me breaking up with my serious partner is ‘brilliant news’?”

Mike held up his hands. “Forgive me, but I’m glad. After all, the board is not too happy about all this. It’s nice to see that you are putting the company first. ”

Agatha wanted to cry out and say it had nothing to do with the fucking company, that she had been ready to stay with Rio through thick and thin. That she would have packed her office up that morning and left without a second thought. But Rio pushed her away and seeing Billy so upset had been the last straw. She couldn’t cause him, or herself, anymore heartache.

Yet while Rio had taken Agatha’s heart, she had not taken her mind, and she was too smart to miss an opportunity that would go in her favour. And so, she forced a smile.

“Of course,” she lied. “Anything for the company.”

“Wanda has been gracious enough not to press charges, but she has asked that Rio be banned from the building. She has also asked for a meeting with you and the board later to discuss the steps forward. You can tell them of this new development then.”

Agatha kept up her fake smile as she stood from her seat, picking up her coffee with one hand, while holding out the other. “I will be there.”

“Great, I’ve already sent the details to your assistant,” Mike shook her hand firmly. “I’m pleased, Agatha. Truely.”

“Me too,” Agatha lied once more. “Onwards and upwards, as they say.”

Rio was awoken by a loud bang at her bedroom door.

“Rio Vidal, get up!”

Rio groaned and checked her phone. It was barely past nine!

“What’s wrong with you?” Rio called back, burying her face back in the pillow. The door swung open, and Lilia stormed her way inside.

“I’ve had enough of this moping.” She pulled the sheets off her. “Get up.”

“Hey!” Rio jumped out of bed. “Lilia, what the hell?!”

“You can’t just stay in bed all day, Rio. I know you’re upset, but you need to do something about it or learn to get on with it. Either way, I have nowhere to be today, and I will spend it keeping you out of that bed.”

Rio grumbled and stormed out of her room. She made her way into the living area and laid herself out on the couch instead. Lilia followed and stood before her, hands on her hips.

“Aren’t you meant to be meeting your thesis advisor today?”

“I’ll cancel.”

“No, you won’t. You’ll go and get the feedback you need to finish this degree. And I want to you to talk to Agatha today as well. This ridiculousness between you two has gone on long enough.”

“How?” Rio questioned. “She blocked my number.”

“You know, before the days of cell phones, we did this magical thing called talking face to face.”

Rio sat herself up. “What if she doesn’t want to see me?”

“Then make an excuse. Don’t you have some of her stuff here?”

“Not much.” Rio thought over what she had. Lilia had already told her she gave Agatha back the script. That left some clothes she’d ‘borrowed’, the key to her apartment, and her grandmother’s locket.

“Drop whatever you have off to her after you see your advisor and use the excuse to talk with her. Take it from an old wise lesbian; even if you can’t salvage anything from this, you need closure.”

Rio didn’t want closure. She wanted everything back to the way things were. If she kept her cool, if Alice hadn’t said anything, and Wanda hadn’t been a total bitch, they’d still be happy. Perhaps they’d have even talked about what the amendment she made, and their future would well and truly be underway.

Yet she guessed Lilia was right. She needed to get out of this limbo, for both their sakes.

“How about a reading?” Lilia grabbed her card and made Rio move up to sit beside her. She shuffled the cards before laying three face-down on the coffee table.

“The past.” Lilia turned over the card and revealed The Tower Reversed. “You had this before.”

“A great change,” Rio said bitterly. Things had certainly changed a lot since then.

“Now the present.” Lilia turned over the card. “The Star. A message of hope, optimism, and offers guidance to the future.” She turned the last card and smiled. “I hoped as much.”

Rio looked at the card and frowned. “The lesbians again?”

“The Ten of Cups,” Lilia corrected.

“Will you tell me what it means now?”

Lilia shook her head. “The only way you will know is if you acknowledge the past and take hold of the present.”

“You’re a crap psychic.”

Lilia chuckled. “We’ll see about that.”

Rio pulled herself up from the couch. “I best get ready. Professor Odinsdottir won’t like it if I’m late.”

“Take my advice,” Lilia told her. “You’ll regret it if you don’t.”

Rio headed back to her room. She needed to get dressed…and maybe put together a bag.

Wanda Maximoff appeared late morning, slipping in when Agatha had asked Sharon to get her some paperwork from upstairs.

Agatha wondered how long she had waited for the opportunity to strike. After all, Mike was likely all too happy to inform his new favourite colleague of their conversation earlier, and she could imagine her ex was of so delighted by the news.

Wanda entered wordlessly and sat in the chair opposite her, her hands in her lap. While she looked the same as always, Agatha did spot a bruise under her eye that her make-up couldn’t quite conceal, the only proof of what transpired three nights before.

Agatha ignored her, choosing to instead focus on her emails. After a while, however, her intense stare was grating her too much to concentrate. She took of her glances and levelled Wanda with a glare.

“Come to gloat?”

“No,” Wanda answered. “I came to see if you were okay.”

“Why do you care?” Agatha snapped, only for Wanda to give her an exasperated look.

“You know why, Agatha. And I wanted to tell you myself that I don’t intend to go file any charges against Rio. I know from personal experience that losing you is punishment enough.”

Agatha said nothing. She refused to discuss any of this with her. The silence didn’t seem to put her off though.

“I know this is fresh, and you’re still processing everything, but I would like to remind you again that you have other options.”

Agatha sat up. “Wanda, I’m not talking about this again so please get out of my office.”

“You have a ready-made family waiting, Agatha. Me and the boys. Our boys.”

“They’re not mine, Wanda. Their Vis’s. You know, the guy you cheated on me with.”

“Biology doesn’t matter. They’ll love you. We can have cute family days out and boring days when we’re just dropping them off at school before work and have family vacations and spent the holidays with your sister’s family. Billy will love having two little cousins, I’m sure.”

“Enough,” Agatha snapped. “Wanda, I’m really not in the mood for this.”

“Let’s go for dinner tonight.”

Agatha scoffed. “I’m not going to dinner with you.”

“I’ll let you consider it,” Wanda countered. “I’m eager to move things along, Agatha. You need to consider the idea that all this unfortunate business may have led you right where you were always meant to be. With us. With a family who’ll love you deeply.”

Before Agatha could respond, the door to the office flew open. Sharon ran in, pointing her finger at Wanda accusingly. “She snuck in! I’m calling security!”

“It’s okay, Sharon. Ms Maximoff was just leaving.”

Wanda sighed and got to her feet. “Just think about it, Agatha. It can just be dinner.”

Once she left, Sharon folded her arms and looked at Agatha. “You’re not going on a date with her, are you?”

Agatha shook her head. “No, Sharon. I’m not.”

“Good, because I’m still rooting for you and Rio.”

Agatha offered her a weak smile, before holding out her hand. “Is that the paperwork?”

Sharon nodded and handed it over.

“Thank you.” Agatha flipped through the pages. “And Sharon?”

“Yes?”

“Please don’t talk about Rio. Not today, anyway.”

Sharon nodded in understanding. “I’ll be at my desk if you need me.”

Agatah watched her go, waiting until the door shut before tossing the paperwork on her desk and leaning back in her chair. She looked at the photos on her desk. The ones of her, Billy and Rio. She wanted to crawl into the photos and stay there forever, back when everything was good and happy.

She wanted Rio. Her Rio. The Rio who’d never do this to her. A Rio that she guessed never existed in the first place. And if that was the great love of her life, then she decided it would be the last.

Agatha Harkness was done with love, and she would show the board just how committed she really was.

By the time Rio got to the café, Hela had already ordered them a selection of desserts to share.

“I have a sweet tooth today,” she explained. “And thought this would be fun.”

Rio nodded before taking a sip of her coffee. She wasn’t in a fun-having mood.

“So,” Hela began again. “How’s the thesis going?”

“I’m not putting my mom in it,” Rio told her quickly. “I’d rather get a lower grade then bring all that up again.”

Thankfully, Hela nodded in understanding. “I appreciate that. I must say though, Rio, you look tired. Please say you’re not overworking yourself. The thesis in its current state will get you your doctorate without a doubt.”

“It’s not that,” Rio assured. “I…me and Agatha broke up. Or at least I think we did. We haven’t spoken since Friday. She’s blocked my number. Well, I blocked hers first but…it’s a long story.”

“It always is,” Hela said lightly. “Have you tried speaking to her face to face?”

“I’m going to try after this,” Rio admitted. “I don’t think it’ll do much good, but I have some of her stuff, so I guess that’ll get my foot in the door.”

Hela whistled. “You must have done something really bad, Vidal. I’m almost impressed.”

Rio looked down at her lap. Oh, she had no idea.

“Well,” her professor continued, “this may not be the most opportune moment, but I did hope to discuss something with you before we get fully into thesis talk.”

“Okay?” Rio had to admit she was intrigued, if not a little bit nervous.

“You know I’ve been working back home writing my piece on native Scandinavian plant-life and their development. Well, I’ve found some samples of a mutated variation of digitalis purpurea. I was wondering if you would like to come work on the research with me?”

Rio blinked at her in surprise. “Come with you? You mean go to…”

“Norway, yes. You could finish your thesis out there, and arrangements can be made for you to be back to defend it and to graduate. I wanted to offer it to you anyway, but I knew you were unlikely to leave your partner for months on end. However, if that is in fact all over and you need to get away, we can fly out on Friday.”

“Friday? Like this Friday?”

Hela nodded. “I’ll need an answer by tonight so I can make all the arrangements. I’ll respect you decision either way, but I’d like it if you came. I think we’ll make a good team, you and I.”

Rio nodded in understanding, and as Hela began to chatter about how the trip could further benefit her thesis, her gaze dropped to the floor. To the beat-up duffle bag filled with Agatha’s things.

Agatha.

She couldn’t just leave. That had been her problem since the beginning. If only she hadn’t left that morning a year ago, and if she’d had pushed through her panic Friday night and stayed by Agatha’s side. Yet perhaps this was the guidance Lilia had talked about. The universe was guiding her forward, to a future she didn’t want, but would keep her moving. It would help others, prevent more families falling apart like her own, and stop another kid becoming as fucked up as she was. It would give her purpose, even if life would never be as colourful as it was before.

It was like she was at a crossroads, one path clear and the other blocked by thorned vines that would cut her limb from limb, though it led to the greater treasure. Norway was her escape, her getaway car. A path forward she didn’t have that morning. It was the clear way. The easy way.

Yet Rio knew she had to push through the thorns, even if it tore her apart in the process.

Agatha had been reading yet another mediocre manuscript when Sharon stepped sheepishly into her office.

“Agatha, I need to talk to you.”

“What’s up?” Agatah took off her glasses. “Is everything okay?”

“You know you said you didn’t want to talk about Rio? Well, I kind of need to right now.”

Sickening worry filled Agatha like a flood. “Is she hurt? What happened? Is she okay?”

“She’s fine,” Sharon quickly assured. “She’s just, well…”

“Spit it out, Sharon.”

“She’s downstairs.”

“She’s what? ”

“In the lobby,” Sharon specified. “Security stopped her. Mike got her banned from the building, but she’s insisting to see you.”

Agatha jumped to her feet, adrenaline shooting through her as she went to leave her office. “I’ll deal with this.”

“Agatha, just keep calm,” Sharon called after, but Agatha didn’t listen. She stormed towards the elevator, ready for whatever battle waited for her at the bottom.

Rio was stood by the main doors, talking to one of the security guys. She seemed calm, a huge contrast from the last time Agatha saw her: all wide eyed and frantic, like a cornered animal. Yet when their eyes met, she saw the anxiousness in her lov-no, ex’s eyes.

“What are you doing here?” Agatha demanded, before dismissing the security guys. They backed off, knowing her reputation enough to trust she would handle the situation better than they ever could.

“I wanted to see you,” Rio answered. “To talk with you.”

“Well, you should have thought about that before you ran off and blocked my number!”

Rio hung her head in shame. “I know and I tried to call you later on, but by then, you’d blocked me back. Which I totally understand, I do. I just I…I didn’t want the last time I saw you being that night. Not with…all that happening.”

“So that’s it?” Agatha questioned. “Are we just…done?”

“I don’t know,” Rio replied. “Do you want us to be?”

Agatha didn’t answer. No, she didn’t want them to be done. She wanted to kiss Rio there and then and hold on to her forever. Yet things were complicated. With Billy, with work, with the entire nature of their relationship.

“I don’t know,” she answered honestly. “I still love you, but I’m angry.”

Rio nodded in acceptance. “I get it.”

“Rio, I…”

“Agatha, it’s fine. I did this and I’m sorry. I truly am. I hate myself for hurting you, and I understand why you may never be able to forgive me.”

“My wrist is fine…”

“I’m not just talking about your wrist.” Rio looked down at her feet. “Look, this probably isn’t the best timing, or maybe it is, I don’t know, but my thesis advisor has asked me to come join her research lab in Norway. If I go, I leave on Friday.”

Agatha’s anger returned full throttle. “So you’re running away from this? From me?”

“No, no,” Rio quickly insisted. “Agatha, if there is even the smallest possibility that we can even just become friends, I’ll stay. Without question. But if you want me out of your life, then consider it done.”

Agatha didn’t know whether to drop to her knees and beg her to stay or throw it right back in her face. She chose not to respond at all, and Rio seemed to get the message, as her shoulders slumped in defeat.

“I need to give an answer by tonight. I’m going to go think it over for myself. Just let me know if you…Just know that I’ll love you no matter what you decide. If anything, I’m just glad I got to see you again, even if it is for the last time.”

Agatha wasn’t sure what to say. Her words weighted heavy on her chest, suffocatingly so.

“I brought you your stuff.” Rio held out a battered duffle-bag.  “I fixed the locket for you.”

“Thanks.” Agatha reached for the bag, their fingers brushing as she took it. Her fingers tingled with their warmth, and she wondered if that was the last time they’d ever touch.

She could see tears in Rio’s eyes, but she smiled. Not brightly, or happily, but lovingly. The kind of smile that comes with a goodbye.

“Before I let you go, I just want to say that the time we spent together was the happiest I’ve ever been. You’re amazing, Agatha Harkness, and I hope you have the most amazing life.”

Agatha watched her leave, watched her walk by the windows in the direction of the subway station. Watched her wipe her cheeks with the back of her hand, before disappearing out of view. A tear trickled down her own cheek, but she quickly brushed it away and headed back to the elevator.

Once she made it back to her office, she placed the duffle bag on her desk. She had plenty of Rio’s stuff too. Mostly clothes and toiletries scattered around her apartment, and of course the photograph Alice had given them. She hadn’t wanted to move any of it, a part of her enjoying the illusion that Rio was still there. That she had just popped out and would be back with smiles and kisses at any moment. Unhealthy, she knew, but it brought her a small amount of comfort.

Off the top of her head, she couldn’t recall what she could have left at Rio’s. After all, she had only stayed there once, and she was certain she took everything home with her. Intrigued, she pulled open the zip to see what was inside.

On top was the set of keys she had given Rio a matter of days ago. Agatha picked them up and looked over the rabbit keychain, smiling softly. She wondered if Rio would have given her a spider one if she ever got a key for her and Lilia’s place. Though, knowing Rio, she’d give her multiple keychains, each as ridiculous as the last.

The rest seemed to be hoodies and shirts, some Agatha wouldn’t have cared to lose, or even noticed they were gone. One made her pause though. Her Fleetwood Mac t-shirt. She held it up to look at it properly. Memories flashed in her mind to that night over a year ago. When Rio emerged from her bathroom wearing it, how she had laid out on the bed in it waiting for her, how it rested between their chests as they kissed. How Agatha had brushed her hands against the soft material as they snuggled into each other to sleep, both believing they were at the start of something special.

Agatha brought the material to her face and inhaled deeply. There was the underlining scent of her detergent, but the rest was all Rio. She hugged it to her chest and closed her eyes. In her mind, she was about to wake up that Friday morning with Rio in her arms, and it was all just a bad dream. Everything was fine. Everything was good. Everything was how was it should be.

She kept the t-shirt in her lap as she pulled the last pieces of clothes out, leaving only a jewellery box at the bottom. She recognised it was the one she had given Rio’s apartment keys in. A slight smile crossed her lips; Rio had wanted to keep the locket safe.

Opening the box, she found the locket resting safely inside. She picked it up and turned it over in her hand before opening it up. Something pink fell onto the desk. Agatha frowned. There hadn’t been anything in it before?

She picked the flash of pink up from her desk and examined it closely. It was withered and drying, but she could see what it was. A rose petal, at least a week or so old. She chuckled and shook her head. Only Rio would put a random flower petal in an antique locket.

She put it back and fastened the chain back around her neck, the locket clattering against the flat metal of her half-heart necklace that had taken its place. She reached up to touch them both, wondering what she should do. Whether she should call or not call. Whether she should try or if she should just let her go.

Before she could make up her mind, there was a knock at her door, Sharon’s voice quickly following. “Agatha, your meeting with the board is in five minutes.”

With a sigh, she shoved the clothes back in the duffle and got to her feet. “On my way.”

The Decision

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! apologies for the emotional rollercoaster. i hope you enjoy this new chapter!

Agatha walked towards the conference room, her heart thumping hard in her chest. She tried to focus on the meeting, on her job, on the career she had spent years carefully crafting. Yet all she could think about was Rio.

Rio leaving.

Rio in Norway.

Rio so far away that she’d never see her again.

The thought alone physically pained her. Yet could she really ask her to stay? To give up on an amazing opportunity to say with her, even though neither of them were sure what they were anymore.

She was almost at the conference room door when she heard someone call out her name. She looked round to see Wanda rushing towards her.

“I’m glad I caught up with you,” Wanda said once she reached her. “We can walk in showing a united front.”

Agatha ignored her and walked towards the conference room door, her jaw clenched tight. When they reached it, Wanda stood in the way with an irritating smirk on her lips. .

“I was wondering where that awful locket went.” Her eyes narrowed. “What’s that other necklace you’re wearing?”

Agatha covered the broken heart with her hand. “Rio got me it.”

Wanda hummed. “I’ll get you a better one.”

Agatha bit her tongue and reached for the door handle. “Shall we?”

With a smirk, Wanda stepped aside, and Agatha let herself into the room.

The board was already in the room when she entered, with Mike sat in the middle. She sat down in the first available seat, while Wanda quickly perched in the one opposite her.

This was going to be torture.

“Agatha,” Mike began. “How are you?”

Agatha shrugged. “Been better.”

Mike nodded in understanding. “Well, to keep everyone updated, you and I had a discussion this morning regarding the incident on Friday night. However, an hour ago I was alerted that Miss Vidal had been stopped by security downstairs. Care to explain her reason for being here?”

“She just brought me something,” Agatha answered, but she could see by the expressions of the board that it wasn’t an adequate answer. She didn’t have to say more, though, and she wouldn’t. Especially not with Wanda watching her so intensely.

Her hand reached for her locket, running her thumb over the cameo image. She could lie, come up with an excuse that would satisfy the board and keep her ex at bay, but her mind wasn’t in the room. It was wherever Rio was, wondering if she’d made her own decision yet.

“Well, regardless of that,” Mike continued, “Agatha told me something this morning which I believe will reassure us all that we can maintain a positive working environment, while also showcasing Agatha’s unrelenting loyalty to this company. I for one believe it shows she has exactly what it takes to be considered for a more senior role within our ranks.”

All eyes fell on Agatha, awaiting her to explain this precious piece of information, while Wanda and Mike looked on expectantly.

“Rio won’t be a problem,” Agatha answered simply. “For any of you.”

“How can you assure that?” A member of the board shot her a disapproving glare. “You’ve brought your dirty laundry here once, so why not again?”

“Agatha, tell them what you told me,” Mike prompted with an eager smile. “Right when I raised similar concerns.”

Agatha looked around the room. If she was honest, her decision had been made long before she entered the room. Before she left her office. Before Rio walked away from her in the lobby. A glance at Wanda Maximoff’s smug face gave her the push to see it through.

“I told Mike that Rio and I are no longer together,” Agatha answered, taking in the grin that appeared on Wanda’s face before raising it with a devious smirk of her own. “Which I intend to rectify as soon as possible.”

Seeing Wanda’s face drop was satisfying beyond words.

“What?” Mike questioned. “Agatha, I thought we agreed this was the best for the company?”

“Well, it’s not what’s best for me. I love Rio and there’s nothing anyone here can do about it.” She looked back at Wanda, who’s entire face seemed to have tightened with anguish.

“This is highly unprofessional,” Mike told her sternly. “How can you possibly expect to work here, with Ms Maximoff, and still remained involved with her?”

“Oh, I don’t intend to.”

Mike frowned. “Don’t intend to what?”

“Work here.” Agatha got to her feet. “Consider this my resignation.”

They called after her, of course they did, but Agatha walked out of the room with her head held high, a huge weight off her shoulders.

She headed back up to her office, saying hi to Sharon as she passed, before setting to work gathering her things. Luckily, she hadn’t brought many personal items (it was meant to be a productive space not a cosy one) but there were still some odd things floating around.

She tipped out a file box and got all the toiletries Jen had gifted her out of the bathroom, as well as the scented candles she had placed on the coffee table. She cleared her desk draws, before picking up the one item that mattered: the photo frame. Agatha looked at it and smiled, before wrapping it in one of her hoodies and shoving it in the duffel bag.

Once she was all packed up, she put her handbag over one shoulder, the duffle over the other, and carried the box with both hands as she left her office for the last time.

Sharon was stood by her desk nervously. “How did the meeting go?”

“Good,” Agatha answered. “I quit.”

Sharon’s eyes widened, before her face split into a huge grin. “Good for you!”

Agatha was about to respond when she heard stomping feet heading their way. They both looked down the corridor to see Wanda Maximoff charging towards them.

Sharon reached for the phone, but Agatha shook her head. No, this she was facing head on.

“What the hell was that?” Wanda demanded. “You can’t just quit, Agatha.”

“I can and I did.”

“You’re seriously throwing away all you’ve worked so hard for to be with her ?”

“Oh stop pretending to care about my career,” Agatha snapped. “If you did, you wouldn’t have pushed your way in here like a fucking parasite.”

“I only want the best for you, Agatha,” Wanda insisted. “And I know that’s being here with me. I’m the only one who understands you. Who understands your drive and ambition. You won’t find anyone better for you than me.”

“I already did,” Agatha answered with conviction. “In a coffee shop a year ago. She’s worth more to me than any of this.”

Wanda laughed bitterly. “How can she be? She’s nothing.”

“She’s a soon to be doctor of botany,” Agatha corrected with a pride. “With a gorgeous smile, ridiculous sense of humour, and the biggest, warmest heart I’ve ever known. From the moment I saw her, she was the one. I didn’t know it at the time, but I do now.”

“She’s still nothing,” Wanda insisted. “And she’ll be worth even when I get her arrested for assault.”

“Then I’ll report you for harassment,” Agatha levied. “Let’s see how that goes down for you.”

Wanda’s eyes widened. “Agatha, you know that’s not true. I love you.”

“Said by every true stalker,” Agatha sassed.

“Agatha please,” Wanda begged. “Just think about this. Is this what you really want?”

“It is,” she answered without hesitation.

“But…”

“Goodbye Wanda.”

“No, Agatha…” Wanda tried but Agatha walked right past her towards the elevators. She had barely stepped inside the metal box before someone else rushed in. She expected it to be Wanda, and readied herself for another fight, but instead she was met with Sharon, wearing her coat with her handbag comically full.

Agatha frowned. “What are you doing?”

“Leaving,” Sharon answered as the doors slid shut. “I’m your assistant. Without you, I have no job.”
Her heart dropped. She had been so caught up with emotion that she didn’t consider… “Sharon, I’m sorry. I didn’t think!”

“Oh, none of that.” Sharon waved her off. “I’m happy you finally stood up for yourself. And I think you’ve made the right decision. You’re far too good this place, and I for one am looking forward to a bit of a break to spend time with my girlfriend.”

“Girlfriend now?” Agatha teased. “Do I need to get you a bi flag pin?”

“Do you have a lesbian pin?”

“Of course not,” Agatah lied. In fact, she had several. “Are you sure you’re alright? Money wise…”

“I have Todd’s pension to keep me going,” Sharon assured her. “Though you must promise me if you need another assistant, I’ll be your first choice.”

“I wouldn’t want anyone else,” Agatha said truthfully. She would miss having Sharon with her most days, though if all went well there may be some hilarious double dates in their future. Not that she was allowing herself to be too hopeful.

“So what are you going to do?” her now former assistant asked. “Tell her you want to be with her?”

“I guess?” Agatha shrugged her shoulders. “She said she was going to go think things over. I just hope we’re still on the same page.”

“Are you going to call her?”

“No,” Agatha answered. “I know exactly where she is.”

The botanical gardens became Rio’s special place when she moved to the city. She and Alice went the first time, wanting to explore more than the typical tourist traps. Of course she was going to love it, there was no doubt, but as they wandered through the carefully crafted gardens full of the finest and most beautiful plants, she felt so peaceful and safe. Despite being in the middle of a bustling city, with people walking through chattering while children ran around enjoying the adventure, her mind just seemed to drown out the noise. She could think, really think, about things she often struggled with.

She went there two days after her parents died. Alice said she needed to be alone for a while, so she went there to process. It didn’t make the pain go away, because nothing could, but it helped her make sense of things in her head. Since then, whenever something happened, she went there. Like when she was decided whether to do her PhD, and when she was debating to answer Lilia’s roommate ad, or when the hot lady from the coffee shop had ghosted her for no reason (though that turned out to be a classic case of bunny sabotage).

And so she figured it was the best place to go to think about what she should do next.

She wanted Agatha. No doubt that trumped everything else. Yet she knew that was unlikely. The security had stopped her for a reason, and it wasn’t because Agatha told them to. That totally wasn’t her style. Which meant it was an order from somebody else in the company, most likely Mike, definitely encouraged by the red devil herself. Which would make them being together even more difficult than it already would be.

Rio knew how important the job was to Agatha. Though she had been complaining about it lately, she knew Agatha took great pride in all she had achieved in her career, and she couldn’t expect her to just throw all that away. Not after she had treated her so poorly.

The real question was did she actually want to go to Norway? Hela had talked a lot about Oslo, and Rio had to admit she was intrigued, but could she just leave like that? She didn’t want to lose her apartment, and the thought of leaving Alice and Lilia behind was a hard one, let alone leaving behind Webbers! Oh no, how could she?

(There was also Agatha. Even in the future when they were done for good, Rio knew she would always hold on to that hope. A hope that one day they’ll see each other in the street and end up going for coffee for old times sake. How they’d end up rekindling their romance and become a story of love defying all odds. Of that invisible string bringing them right back together where they both belonged).

Yet Hela’s offer was an opportunity others would dream of. To work on the ground, exploring plant life in a totally different environment and examining this newly found specimen. It sounded exciting, but she didn’t feel it. Perhaps it was broken heart, or perhaps she simply didn’t want to go. Even if it would distract her from her current pain.

She stood in the grand Victorian greenhouse, studying the white petals of the bloomed flower before her. So lost in contemplation that she didn’t notice someone had moved to stand beside her.

“What’s that one called?”

Rio swore she imagined the voice. Swore her mind playing tricks on her, and she would look and see someone else stood there, totally unaware of the deep pain their words had unintentionally caused. Yet as she looked beside her, and her brown eyes met glimmering blue, there was no denying it.

Agatha Harkness, live and in person.

“Stewartia ovata,” she answered, her voice slightly shaken. “Or Mountain Camellia, if we use the most common term.”

“Well, we certainly wouldn’t want to do that,” Agatha replied, and Rio couldn’t help but chuckle.

“How did you know I’d be here?” she asked curiously.

“Last time we were here you said this was your place to unwind. This and basketball, but I figured this would be the place. Though I have been walking round the gardens for about twenty minutes looking for you. Why is this place so damn big?”

“You could have just called me,” Rio reminded her. “I unblocked your number.”

“I know,” Agatha admitted, “but I figured this would be more romantic.”

Romantic? Rio’s heart leapt. That sounded good…right?

“Agatha, I…”

“No,” Agatha stopped her. “You got to talk earlier. Now it’s my turn.”

Rio swallowed nervously, before nodding.

“Well, I meant what I said earlier. You hurt me, Rio. You can’t just push me away like that. I was so worried, and I was confused, and it was like a living hell. But I guess I understand. The way I see it, communication has always been our issue, and the times we work, when we really work, are when we actually talk to each other. Face to face. No notes or messages or calls. Just you and me. So here it is. Rio Vidal, I think you should go to Norway.”

Her heart dropped. No, no, no. This couldn’t be it. Not over some stupid trip she wasn’t sure she wanted to go on anyway.

She went to argue, but Agatha held up her hand to stop her. “It’s a huge opportunity, and you should grasp it with both hands. Your work is important, and this could be huge for your career.”

Rio bowed her head sadly. She guessed she was right, even if she hated it.

“But if you asked me what I want you to do,” Agatha continued. “Well, that would be a totally different answer.”

Her head shot up. She thought she understood, but she had to be sure. “Y-you want me to stay?”

“Of course I want you to stay, you dork. I love you.”

Rio couldn’t help but grin. “I love you too.”

“But you can’t stay for me,” Agatha insisted. “We’ll make it work. We can call, and facetime, and I can come out to visit? I mean, I don’t want to assume, and I know we have a lot to talk about. A whole lot. But do you still want to try?”

Rio couldn’t help it. She leaned forward and placed a quick kiss to Agatha’s lips. Oh, how she missed those lips. This kiss deepened, enough to make her breathless. She never wanted to wait this long to kiss her ever again.

When she pulled back, Agatha’s cheeks had an adorable red hue. Rio couldn’t help but be proud  of herself.

“That a good enough answer?”

Agatha nodded, clearing her throat. “Yep, got it loud and clear.”

Rio smiled, but the niggle of doubt in the back of her mind made it fade. “How is this going to work?”

Agatha shrugged. “We’ll work on it together.”

“But your job…”

“Not an issue.”

“It’s not?”

Agatha shook her head.

Rio frowned in confusion. “But how?”

“Simple. I quit.”

Rio’s eyes widened. “You what? ”

“I wasn’t working there anymore, not after everything. I should have quit the moment Wanda started meddling or at least tried doing something to stop her. I’m sorry I let it go so far.”

Rio nodded in understanding. “And I’m sorry for punching her.”

Agatha smirked. “Are you really?”

Rio laughed. “Okay, maybe not, but I’m sorry it caused you trouble.”

“Well now I’m free of her and that place, and I’m now totally available to visit you in Norway all the time! Maybe I could stay for a few weeks at a time? I don’t want to leave Scratchy for too long, but I’m sure Billy would love having him, even if it means plying his dad with allergy medication.”

The thought of having Agatha totally available to her was indeed an enjoyable one, though not entirely practical. “But what are you going to do? Find another job?”

Agatha shrugged. “I have a lot of savings, and I have connections that I can use to get some freelance editing gigs. Maybe I’ll even work more on The Witches’ Road?”

“It is very good,” Rio insisted. “I’d like to read it again sometime.”

“That can certainly be arranged,” Agatha teased, and Rio couldn’t help but blush. This woman was something else.

“Shall we go somewhere and talk?”

“That sounds sensible,” Agatha agreed, stepping in the direction of the exit. “You coming?”

“Hold on.” Rio pulled out her phone. “I just need to do something first.”

“Don’t keep me waiting, Vidal. I’m ready to enjoy unemployment.”

Rio shook her head at her antics before typing out a message.

RIO

Thanks for the offer, but I can’t leave right now.

A reply came quickly.

HELA

You two worked it out then? I’m glad! Maybe you could fly out for a week or so soon instead? Bring that girl of yours along. I’d like to meet her.

RIO

Count on it!

“Honey?”

Rio smiled as she pocketed her phone and took hold of her hand. “So, coffee?”

Agatha smiled. “Coffee sounds good.”

The Next Steps

Chapter Notes

hi everyone! i can't believe this is the last chapter! honestly, i can't believe i started this fic while the show was still airing and now it's done! i hope you enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Coffee went well.

Rio had been worried, despite the hopefulness of their conversation in the conservatory, but it had thankfully worked out just fine. They had been honest, and some parts hadn’t easy, but they decided a plan going forward.

They would still kiss, still hug, hold hands, have their little nicknames, and still say ‘I love you’ (Rio had been very insistent on that and Agatha didn’t argue with her). But they’d pause any talk of marriage or babies, would try not to see each other every day, and absolutely, positively NO sex. And they were adamant, confident even, that they would have the determination and willpower to see that plan through.

In fact, they were so confident that Agatha asked if she wanted to come say hi to Senõr Scratchy.

And after her rabbit cuddles, Rio had been confident enough to ask if she could grab a few of her things to take back to her apartment.

And they were confident enough to both go into the bedroom to collect said items.

All it took was for them both to reach for the same thing at the same time, and the next thing Rio knew, they were both tangled in the sheets, breathless and grinning like idiots.

Perhaps no sex was an unachievable goal.

They ended up spending the rest of the week in and out of bed, only really being apart when Rio had to go to classes or the lab. Rio counted that as not being together all the time…right?

The future, however, was still up in the air. Mostly due to the fact Agatha seemed to be enjoying her unemployment a little too much. Not in the traditional sense of rotting on the couch or doomscrolling TikTok all day. No, no. She had instead channelled her managerial energy into being an active friend, sister, aunt and, most of all, a very devoted girlfriend.

That morning, Rio woke to the smell of brewing coffee and pancake batter. She smiled to herself, snuggling against her pillow.

“Something smells good babe!”

Soon enough, the bedroom door opened, and Agatha wandered in. Her perfect hair and powerful pantsuits had been replaced with unruly waves and baggy t shirts. Still stunning, just relaxed and totally free.

The only downside was they were the t shirts Rio liked to steal, but she had discovered her girlfriend had a secret stash of plaid shirts, so had successfully stolen one of those the night before instead. After all, a girlfriend shirt was a girlfriend shirt no matter the style.

Agatha stood by the side of the bed, smiling down at her. “Good morning, my love.”

“Good morning,” Rio grinned, still cuddled up in the sheets and the oversized shirt. “What time is it?”

“Just before eight. I was letting you have a few more minutes.”

Rio smiled up at her. “Why don’t we use those few minutes to cuddle?”

Agatha chuckled. “We both know if I get back in that bed, we won’t be leaving it again.”

“Sounds good to me.”

“Up. Come on.”

Rio rolled out of bed, quickly running up to press up against Agatha as they walked out of the bedroom. “But we can share a shower, right?”

“I already have that in the schedule,” Agatha assured, and Rio grinned. She was quite enjoying this side of Agatha.

After breakfast, a long shower, and a quick change, Agatha drove Rio to the college.

“Do you want me to come pick you up?” she asked as she parked outside the science building.

“I’ll be fine,” Rio assured. “I’m meeting Alice a few blocks from here, anyway.”

Her sister had messaged the night before asking if they could meet up. They hadn’t spoken much since the weekend before, and while her sister had looked after her, comforted her, practically scarped her off the metaphorical floor, they hadn’t properly talked. Not about the past, the present, or the future.

(And if Agatha’s side of the phone calls were anything to go by, Jen didn’t want her friend having anything to do with her, let alone her girlfriend.)

Baby steps, Rio told herself. It’d all work out somehow. It had to.

“Shall I meet you back at my place?” Agatha suggested. “You have your key, right?”

Rio held searched her backpack and pulled the set out by the silver rabbit. “Good to go.”

“Excellent.” Agatha leaned over and placed a soft kiss to her lips. “I’ll see you later.”

“See you later, my love.” Rio pushed open the car door and climbed out. “I love you.”

“And I love you.” Agatha smiled, a smile so bright and free that Rio just wanted to climb back into the car and kiss her silly. “Now go before you’re late.”

Rio blew her a kiss before rushing up the steps of the science building, a giddy grin on her face.

Agatha arrived at the Kaplan residence around mid-morning.

With her husband at work and her son at school, Rebecca always loved it when she had time to stop by during the day, and had been excited when she rang the night before asking if she could swing round the following morning. Only when she got there, Agatha found only one of the Kaplan boys was where they were meant to be.

“I’m ill,” Billy insisted from where he sat at the breakfast table. “I threw up last night.”

Agatah grimaced. “Gross, kid.”

“Or so he says.” Rebecca eyed her son suspiciously. “Eitherway, his school has a 24-hour absence policy for sickness, real or not, so here he is.”

Agatha smirked at his deviousness. “Are you sure he’s your son and not mine?”

“He’s all me,” Rebecca insisted, placing a kiss to the top of her son’s head as she walked past him to the fridge. “You’re just a bad influence.”

“I was ill,” Billy insisted once more. “But I’m okay now. Shall we go bowling or something?”

“Absolutely not,” his mother told him. “Now, head upstairs. I want to talk with your aunt.”

“But…”

“Now.”

Billy huffed and sulked his way upstairs. Rebecca waited until they heard his bedroom door slam shut before laughing.

“He’s a terrible liar,” she said as she carried over their coffees. “When he found out you were coming, the whole sickness act started.”

“As long as he doesn’t make a habit of it. Seeing I’m now unemployed, you’re going to be putting up with me more often.”

“Oh great,” Rebecca joked, yet the moment she sat down, her face turned serious. “Have you looked at job vacancies yet?”

Agatha shook her head. “But I have an editing gig coming through on Monday that’ll give me a bit of extra cash. I’ll just keep trying and networking. Hopefully something will come up, preferably before I run out of rent money.”

“You know if you need to, you have a room here.”

“Thank you, but the commute is too long. Also, I’m not doing the medium distance relationship thing. A lesbian trope I am not.”

“Okay, Little Miss U-Haul,” Rebecca teased. “How are things with Rio?”

“Good,” Agatha said with a smile. “We’re taking things slow, but…”

“But?”

Agatha put her head in her hands. “I still want to marry her.”

“You still can! Just let things settle,” Rebecca advised. “You had a big blip, and soon everything will settle down.”

“It’s not just that. We talked about kids, and I really want us to have that, but I worry the longer we wait the chances of conceiving…”

“Woah, woah, woah.” Rebecca held her hands up. “Agatha, you don’t have a job. You can’t plan for a kid on top of that?”

“I know, I know.” Agatha sat up and smiled at her sister. “You and Rio are keeping me sane right now. I can’t cope with this lack of routine. Did you know I organised Jen’s calendar for the next year? She said I can come work for her, but I think one of us would get arrested for killing the other.”

Especially if she kept on bad-mouthing Rio , she added in her head. Rebecca didn’t need to know about all that.

“Well you know, family dinner was very much missed here this week. I think next week you should just come here all day. We can do some sister bonding, and I know Billy will be pleased to see you here after school.”

“That sounds perfect. I’ll see what Rio’s schedule-”

“Erm, Agatha,” Rebecca interrupted awkwardly. “I think maybe it’d be best if only you came this time.”

Agatha frowned. “Why? You said Rio would always be…”

“That was before,” Rebecca explained. “And before you say anything, I may not know the whole story, but I like Rio and I’m happy you worked things out.”

“Okay?” Agatha leaned back in her chair and folded her arms. “Then what’s the problem?”

“Billy.”

“Billy?”

“We thought he’d be as overjoyed as we were when you told us you and Rio had worked things out, but he got upset. He kept saying how he hated her, and how he doesn’t want her coming to the house. We’ve tried to talk to him, but he’s inherited his aunt’s stubbornness.”

“Fuck, right, okay.” Agatha got to her feet. “I’ll be right back.”

“Where are you going?” Rebecca asked as Agatha headed for the stairs.

“To talk to my nephew.”

When she made it upstairs, she knocked lightly on the door.

“Come in,” Billy’s voice called out, and Agatha walked inside.

Billy was sprawled out on his bed, his Switch in his hands. She offered him a warm smile.

“Hey kid.”

“Hey.” He set his Switch aside and sat up. “What’s up?”

Agatha sat down on the edge of his bed. “I talked with your mom, and she said you’re upset about me and Rio.”

Billy looked down at his lap. “I think you could do better.”

“You loved Rio!”

“I did until she hurt you! If she did it once, she can do it again. I can’t trust her.”

Agatha sighed. “Billy, you don’t need to worry about that.”

“But…”

“No,” she told him firmly. “I’m a grown adult, Billy. I can make my own decisions.”

Billy scrunched his face and folded his arms; muscle memory from when he was a small child. “I still don’t like her.”

Her heart dropped sadly. She wanted her two favourite people to be as inseparable as they were before, to see them laughing and joking together. Though it seemed now she’d be lucky to get them just in the same room.

“Well.” Agatha stood back up. “I’ll leave you to whatever ridiculous game you were playing. After all, I have a coffee downstairs getting colder by the moment.”

She had almost made it out of the door when he piped up again.

“Agatha?”

“Yes?”

“Are you angry with me?”

“No,” Agatha answered honestly. Maybe slightly annoyed, but not angry. “I just wish you’d give Rio another chance, but I understand why you’re feeling this way.”

Billy nodded in acceptance. “You’re coming for dinner this week, right?”

Agatha put on her best smile. “I wouldn’t miss it for the world, kid.”

Rio and Alice sat opposite each other at the small table in the cramped coffee shop. They both had their coffees, and had exchanged a bit of small talk, but that was all.

Rio wasn’t sure what to say. She was scared of saying the wrong thing. What if she just started talking about college and came across too casual? What if she jumped right into it and came across too crass? Then the ridiculousness of her being nervous about trying to talk to her own sister finally sunk in, and so she just said the first thing that popped in her head.

“Agatha told Jen to fuck herself on Wednesday.”

Alice almost spat out her drink. “She never told me that!”

“She did! I heard her shouting from the other room!”

Alice laughed. “What were they talking about?”

“Me apparently,” Rio said with a casual shrug, but the fleeting high mood had already dropped.

“Oh Rio, just ignore Jen,” Alice insisted. “She’s just defensive and I swear she enjoys arguing with Agatha so will find any excuse to start one.”

“I think Agatha enjoys it too,” Rio admitted. “But I get it. What she saw…”

“Wasn’t what happened, and everyone has told her that,” Alice reminded her. “Just leave Jen to me, okay?”

Rio nodded. “Thank you.”

“I have something for you.” Alice reached into her backpack and handed over an envelope.

Rio took it cautiously. “What is it?”

“The pages from Mom’s journal. I might find more, but that’ll be the most of it. I figured you should have them.”

“You ripped up Mom’s journal?” Rio held the envelope close, knowing how dangerous and precious its contents was. “Why would you do that?”

“Because some things are more important than dragging up the past.” Alice reached across the table and took Rio’s hand. “No matter what, you’re my sister. I do wish I knew sooner, not so I could judge you but so you had someone to talk to. I can’t imagine how lonely it must have felt carrying a secret like that around with no one else to lean on. But now you have me, Lilia, and of course, Agatha. We’re here for you, always.”

Rio squeezed Alice hand as tears began to pool in her eyes. “Thank you.”

“And whatever you decide to do with the pages, I’ll support you,” Alice insisted. “Without a doubt.”

Rio smiled, as a tear trailed down her cheek. “I love you, Al.”

Alice smiled, her own eyes glistening. “Love you too, sis.”

When Agatha arrived back at her apartment, she found Rio sat on her living room floor with Scratchy running around her.

“You’re cleaning up his mess,” she told her. “Whoever gets him out, sorts him out. Those are the house rules.”

“Oh really?” Rio smirked up at her. “What other rules are there?”

“Well, to take out the trash whenever you notice it’s full.”

“That’s a given.” Rio got to her feet. “Anymore?”

Agatha stepped towards Rio. “To share the covers equally.”

“That’s a rule for you, not me,” Rio teased. “But continue.”

Agatha brushed a piece of lint off Rio’s shirt, right above her heart. “Whoever makes dinner gets dessert.”

Rio cocked an eyebrow. “I better learn how to cook then.”

“And whoever wears the strap, cleans the strap.”

“What if we both wear one?”

Agatha frowned. “How would that even work?”

“I don’t know, but we could try?”

Agatha chuckled and kissed her girlfriend sweetly. “Let’s cuddle on the couch instead.”

Rio flopped on the couch and patted the space beside her. “M’lady.”

Agatha rolled her eyes and settled beside her, resting her head on Rio’s shoulder. “Did you have a good day?”

“Yeah.”

“Just yeah?” Agatha teased. “How was Alice?”

“She’s good, and we’re good,” Rio said with a smile. “We talked and laughed and cried. It’s what we needed, I think.”

“Oh honey, I’m so happy for you.” Agatha linked their arms and squeezed even closer. “And you’re right. Communication is key to any healthy relationship.”

“Is that your mantra now?”

“It is! I’m considering becoming a motivational speaker.”

Rio laughed loudly. “Please don’t. You’ll make them cry.”

Agatha gasped dramatically. “I’ll have you know, I give great pep talks! Look at Sharon. Thanks to me, she’s living her bisexual dreams.”

“That’s all thanks to Lilia and whatever spell she uses to make herself catnip for women over sixty, and under sometimes.” Rio grimaced. “No, you’d be like one of those body-builder guys who get paid to shout at people until they cry and finally try to improve themselves.”

Agatha considered Rio’s words. Perhaps that was a plausible career move?

Before she could think much into it, Rio reached into the pocket of her hoodie and pulled out a folded envelope. “Alice gave me this.”

Agatha frowned. “What is it?”

Rio tore open the envelope to reveal a half dozen small pieces of lined paper, all ripped down one edge, covered in fine, spiralling handwriting. Agatha knew what they were instantly.

“She gave you the pages?”

Rio nodded, turning the papers over in her hand. “She said its up to me what I do with them.”

Agatha’s heart beat fast. “And what were you thinking?”

“I don’t know…”

“Rio, I’m not dating you through visitations. If you step foot in a police station…”

“I’m not going to the police,” Rio assured. “I’m not stupid.”

“I know you’re not.” Agatha tucked a strand of hair behind her ear. “But you’re too honest.”

“Well, the only options I’m thinking of are hiding them or burning them.”

“I vote burning!” Agatha went to stand, but Rio dragged her back down.

“I need to think about it, okay? I don’t know if I want to read them, or if I just try to move on. I don’t know.” Rio looked down at the pages, and Agatha could see the struggle in her eyes. “Can we just forget for now?”

Agatha took the papers and tossed them on the floor. “Out of sight, out of mind.”

Rio rolled her eyes. “You’re a menace.”

“Don’t you know it,” Agatha grinned, until she remembered she had a confession of her own. “Hey, I need to tell you something too.”

“Okay?” Rio looked both curious and concerned. “What’s up?”

“Rebecca’s asked me to go round for dinner next week, but just me.”

“Oh.” Rio shifted away from her. “Is she mad-”

“No, she’s fine. Really. It’s, well. It’s Billy.”

“Billy?” Rio’s eyes widened, and Agatha couldn’t bare the sadness that began to wash over her love’s face.

“He’s just taking it hard,” Agatha assured. “He just needs time, but…you know what? I’m going to call Rebecca and cancel.”

“What? No, Agatha. You can’t cancel! They’re your family!”

“Well you’re my family too,” Agatha insisted. “You’re the person I’m going to marry and have kids with, and that’s something Billy will just have to learn to accept.”

Rio stared at her, eyes wide and mouth agape. Agatha realised what she said and kicked herself. So much for taking it slow.

“Rio, I-”

The next thing she knew, she was on her back with Rio Vidal sprawled on top of her.

“You want to marry me?”

“I do,” Agatha confirmed. “I really, really do.”

Rio grinned. “I want to marry you too.”

Agatha stared up at her in awe. “You do?”

Rio nodded. “So does that make us engaged?”

“Nope, I want to ask you properly.”

“Hey, why can’t I ask you?”

“Because I want to ask you.”

“I want to ask you too!”

“Not if I want to ask you first!”

“Wanna bet, Harkness?”

“You don’t want to bet me, Vidal.”

Rio leaned down and kissed her fiercely. Every time they kissed it was magical, but when Rio kissed her like that, Agatha felt like she was floating.

When she pulled away, Rio smirked down at her. “Wanna take this show to the bedroom?”

Agatha slipped out from under her. “Let’s hydrate first.”

Rio groaned. “Fuck hydration, Agatha. I’m too wound up for this.”

“Patience my love,” Agatha said as she got to her feet. “Now, let me get us some lemonade.”

She had almost made it to the kitchen when she heard Rio screech.

“Shit!”

Agatha whirled round. “What?”

Rio leaned down and picked a shredded piece of paper off the floor. “Scratchy ate the pages!”

Agatha stared at the mess of nibbled papers surrounding the bunny who was chewing away, once more oblivious to his actions.

She tried, she really did, but she just couldn’t hold in the laughter bubbling inside her. To her relief, Rio joined her, flopping back on the couch as she burst into giggles.

Meanwhile, Senõr Scratchy remained blissfully unaware of the chaos he had just caused, just happy that he was safe in a home filled with love and excitement…and tasty paper too.
